- `pdf/` — **Export to PDF** via Apache **PDFBox 3.x** (`pdfbox`/`pdfbox-io`/`fontbox` are **automatic modules**; `commons-logging` 1.3.5 is a real multi-release module. `module-info` `requires org.apache.pdfbox`). **jlink/moditect (critical):** all three pdfbox-family modules log via `commons-logging`, but jdeps reports `commons-logging` "not found" (it isn't on moditect's jdeps path) and the global `--ignore-missing-deps` then **drops the `requires`** — so jlink silently prunes `commons-logging` and **all PDF export dies on the packaged build** with `NoClassDefFoundError`/`IllegalAccessError: org/apache/commons/logging/LogFactory`. So the `dist` profile gives pdfbox/pdfbox-io/fontbox **hand-written `<moduleInfoSource>`** descriptors (not jdeps-generated `<moduleInfo>`) that explicitly `requires org.apache.commons.logging` (fontbox also `requires org.apache.pdfbox.io`); the export lists come from jdeps' generated set. This was latent — packaged PDF export never worked until device-tested. Belt-and-suspenders: `PdfExportService` (and `PrintService`/`OfficeExportService`) catch **`Throwable`**, not just `Exception`, and log via j.u.l — their `exec.submit(...)` tasks otherwise swallow an `Error` into the `Future` and hang the "Exporting…"/"Preparing…" status forever with no error. Output is **light-theme** regardless of the app/editor theme and is generated **off the FX thread** on a daemon executor. `PdfExportService` (the `GitService`/`MermaidService` idiom: single `pdf-export` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater` callbacks returning a `Result{ok,message}`) has `exportCode(...)` (tokenizes off-thread via `GrammarRegistry.shared().forFileName` + `TextMateHighlighter.compute` when highlighting is on — no grammar ⇒ plain text — then `CodePdfWriter.write`) and `exportMarkdown(...)` (`MarkdownPdfWriter.write`). **`PdfTheme`** is the single Primer-Light palette: a `class→Color` `TOKEN` map mirroring `syntax.css` plus `colorFor`/`bold`/`italic` decisions for a TextMate scope-class collection. **`PdfText`** is the pure/unit-tested code-layout core: `splitIntoLineRuns(text, spans, tabSize)` → per-line styled `Run{text,color,bold,italic}` (tab-expanded, `\r`-dropped, same-style merged) and `wrap(line, maxCols)` for monospace column wrapping. **`CodePdfWriter`** embeds the four JetBrains Mono TTFs, computes char/gutter/column metrics, paginates, and draws the optional right-aligned muted line-number gutter (blank on wrapped continuations) + colored runs + a centered page number; missing glyphs degrade to `?` (`safeShowText`). **`MarkdownPdfWriter`** is a second CommonMark-AST backend beside `MarkdownRenderer` (reuses `MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument`), emitting **native vector text** via a `Cur` cursor (embedded+subset **Inter** for prose — matching the on-screen preview on every platform, and giving full Unicode coverage WinAnsi Helvetica lacked — plus embedded JBMono for code; `Cur.embed(doc, relPath)` loads each as a `PDType0Font`): headings (sized + underline rule), inline-run paragraphs (bold/italic/`code`/links), bullet/ordered lists, block quotes, fenced/indented code blocks, thematic breaks, and GFM tables (measured columns, header shading, cell wrap, greedy `flow` wrapping with automatic page breaks). Images resolve like the FX renderer (`data:`/http/file/relative-to-`baseDir`) and embed via `PDImageXObject`; a ` ```mermaid ` block renders to a PNG through `Mermaid.renderPng` and embeds (degrades to a code block when no `mmdc` command is supplied); unfetchable images fall back to alt text — image failures never abort the PDF. Page size is `letter`/`a4` (`pageRectangle`). **Settings** (`pdfLineNumbers`/`pdfSyntaxHighlighting` default on, `pdfPageSize` default `letter`; schema 5→6 additive-identity) surface in **Settings → Editor → Export & Print** (the section is shared with printing — see `print/`). `MainController.exportCodePdf`/`exportPreviewPdf` (mirror `exportMermaid`: FileChooser `*.pdf` defaulting to `<base>.pdf`, "exporting…" status, success/error via `reportPdf`) back commands `editor.exportPdf` + `preview.exportPdf` (the preview one gated to `EditorBuffer.hasPreview()`, routing `.mmd`→`mermaidService.export` and Markdown→`pdfService.exportMarkdown` with `mmdc` only when Mermaid is enabled). *Deferred: headers/branding, watermarks, TOC/bookmarks, password protection, a follow-dark-theme option.*
- `office/` — **Markdown preview → MS Word (`.docx`) + OpenDocument Text (`.odt`) export.** Walks the same CommonMark AST as the PDF/preview renderers (`MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument`) via the shared, pure, unit-tested **`InlineRun`** (`flatten(node)` → styled runs: bold/italic/strikethrough/underline/inline-code + link `href`; soft/hard breaks → `"\n"`, inline images → alt text) and **`OfficeImages`** (resolve a Markdown image to raster bytes — local-relative-to-`baseDir`, `data:` URI, or `http(s)` fetch; **SVG rasterized to PNG** via the preview's `PreviewImageLoader.svgToPng` so shields.io/GitHub badges embed; PNG/JPEG/GIF/BMP sniffing for POI type + ODT media-type/extension — plus `renderMermaid(mmdc, src)`→PNG via `mmdc` and `renderMath(latex, display)`→PNG via JLaTeXMath). Block-level `$$…$$` display math (`InlineRun.soleDisplayMath`) (which spans soft line breaks, so a multi-line `$$` block on its own lines is detected) and ` ```mermaid ` fences (`InlineRun.isMermaidInfo`) embed as images in both formats (degrading to a code block / alt text when the tool is unavailable). **Inline `$…$` math** also embeds in all three exporters: a non-code text run is split via `editor/MathSpans.segments` and each math span renders to a PNG (`OfficeImages.renderMath` / `MathImages.renderPng`) placed inline — DOCX via a picture `XWPFRun` (`DocxWriter.embedInlineMath`), ODT via an as-char `<draw:frame>` (`OdtWriter.mathFrame`; the `Embedded` `images` list is threaded through `inline`/`paragraph`/`tableXml`), PDF via an image `Word` drawn baseline-aligned in the flow (`MarkdownPdfWriter.addInlineText`/`mathWord`). Each falls back to literal `$latex$` text when render fails / math is off. **`DocxWriter`** uses Apache **POI** XWPF (headings via `Heading*` style + sized bold runs, paragraphs, bullet/ordered lists prefix-marked + indented to dodge the heavy XWPF numbering API, block quotes indented, fenced/indented code as monospace per-line paragraphs, GFM tables via `XWPFTable`, thematic breaks as bottom-bordered paragraphs, hyperlinks via `createHyperlinkRun`, and local/`data:` images via `addPicture`+`Units.toEMU`). **`OdtWriter`** is **hand-written** (a ZIP of XML via `java.util.zip` — `mimetype` STORED first, then `content.xml`/`styles.xml`/`META-INF/manifest.xml`/`Pictures/`): the pure, unit-tested **`contentXml(...)`** emits ODF (`<text:h>`/`<text:p>` with nested `<text:span>` style runs `TBold`/`TItalic`/`TStrike`/`TUnderline`/`TCode`, `<text:a>` links, `<text:list>` bullet/number `L1`/`L2`, `<table:table>`, `Preformatted_20_Text` code paragraphs with `<text:s>`/`<text:tab/>`, `Quotations`, `Horizontal_20_Line`, `<draw:frame>` images), with paragraph/heading/list styles in `styles.xml`. **ODF Toolkit (odfdom) is deliberately NOT used** — its transitive Apache **Jena** + **xercesImpl** deps break the modular/jlink build (xerces split-packages with `java.xml`), so ODT is hand-rolled with zero new deps for that half. **`OfficeExportService`** (the `PdfExportService` idiom: a single `office-export` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater` → `Result{ok,message}`) runs both off the FX thread. `MainController.exportPreviewDocx`/`exportPreviewOdt` (mirror `exportPreviewPdf`: FileChooser, "exporting…" status, success/error via `reportOffice`) back commands `preview.exportDocx`/`preview.exportOdt` (palette + the preview right-click menu, Markdown buffers only — diagrams aren't supported); wired into `EditorBuffer` via `setPreviewExportDocxHandler`/`setPreviewExportOdtHandler`. `module-info` `requires org.apache.poi.ooxml`/`org.apache.poi.poi`. **`-Pdist` jlink:** POI 5.4.x + xmlbeans + commons-compress/io/codec already ship real module descriptors and link directly; only the four automatic leaf deps — **SparseBitSet** (`com.zaxxer.sparsebitset`), **commons-math3** (`commons.math3`), **commons-collections4** (`org.apache.commons.collections4`), **curvesapi** (`com.github.virtuald.curvesapi`) — get moditect `add-module-info` descriptors (names matching POI's own `requires`). POI's optional batik/bouncycastle/santuario/xmlgraphics/pdfbox-graphics2d deps are `requires static`, so jlink doesn't pull them. **Device-tested**: the packaged macOS app image (`-Pdist`, jlink + AOT) exports a `.docx` (re-openable; 3 embedded `word/media` images) and `.odt` (mimetype-first ODF zip; 3 `Pictures/`) with the math/mermaid/badge all rendered. NOTICE updated (Apache-2.0). *Deferred: Windows/Linux dist device-test.*
- `print/` — **Printing** via **`javafx.print`** (no AWT — `java.awt.print` would throw `HeadlessException` under `App.main`'s `java.awt.headless=true` SVG guard; `javafx.print` is in `javafx.graphics`, already required, **no `module-info`/dependency change**). Mirrors the PDF feature and reuses its layout core; output is always **light**, paper size comes from the print **dialog** (not `pdfPageSize`). **Preview-first flow:** `PrintService` (the `PdfExportService` idiom: single `print` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater`) does the off-thread *prepare* and returns a **`Paginator`** (`paginate(PageLayout)→List<Node>`, a layout-agnostic recipe) inside a `Prepared{paginator,error}`: `prepareCode(...)` tokenizes off-thread (`GrammarRegistry`+`TextMateHighlighter`, null grammar ⇒ plain) → `PdfText.splitIntoLineRuns` → a paginator over `CodePrintLayout`; `prepareMarkdown(...)` off-thread `MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument` → paginator over `MarkdownPrintLayout`; `prepareMermaid(...)` runs `Mermaid.renderPng` (mmdc) off-thread → paginator yielding a scaled `ImageView` page. The same paginator drives both the on-screen preview and the final print, so **what you preview is what prints**. The static `PrintService.printPages(pages, layout, job)` does the actual `printPage`/`endJob` on the FX thread. **`CodePrintLayout`** is the JavaFX analog of `CodePdfWriter`: reuses `PdfText.wrap` + `PdfTheme` (its `java.awt.Color`→JavaFX `Color`), builds one `VBox` of `TextFlow` rows per page (optional muted right-aligned line-number gutter), paginating by **whole lines**; pure `columns(printableWidth,charWidth)`/`linesPerPage(printableHeight,lineHeight)` are unit-tested. **`MarkdownPrintLayout`** renders the preview (light `md-light` + `app.css`/`syntax.css`), measures each top-level block offscreen (`measureBlockHeights`), and does **block-aware pagination** via the pure/unit-tested `packBlocks(heights,pageHeight)` — greedily packs whole blocks so nothing splits across a page edge; a single block taller than a page gets its own page, uniformly scaled to fit. **The measure scene is created at a definite width (`new Scene(root, pw, ph)`), *not* wrapped in a `Group`:** a `Group` shrink-wraps to its child's intrinsic width, which collapses a **percent-width table `GridPane`** to a few characters — wrapping every cell and grossly over-measuring the table's height, so even a small table got bumped to its own page (the print preview didn't match the on-screen preview). A fixed-width scene gives the columns a real width to distribute; `measureBlockHeights` is FX-harness-tested (`MarkdownPrintLayoutFxTest`). `MainController.printCode`/`printPreview` create a `PrinterJob` (no dialog yet), call the matching `prepare*` ("preparing…" status), then `openPrintPreview` opens **`ui/PrintPreview`** — a modal window showing each page on a scaled white "paper" sheet (◀/▶ navigation, "Page N of M") built via the paginator for the default page layout. Its **Print…** button shows the native `showPrintDialog(stage)`, **re-paginates for the chosen `PageLayout`** (fresh nodes — also avoids re-using preview nodes already in a scene), prints, and reports via `reportPrint`; **Close** cancels. These back **palette-only** commands `editor.print` + `preview.print` (no keybinding — `C-p` is Emacs `nav.lineUp`). Print reuses the PDF settings `pdfLineNumbers`/`pdfSyntaxHighlighting` (the relabeled **Export & Print** section); **no new Settings field, no schema bump**. *Deferred: page-setup dialog, headers/footers / page numbers on printed output, a toolbar Print button / keybinding, print-selection / custom page ranges.*
- `search/` + in-editor find — **Search**. The pure, unit-tested **`editor/SearchMatcher`** is the shared core: `matches(text, query, caseSensitive, regex, wholeWord)` → `List<int[]>` non-overlapping ranges (literal via `regionMatches`, regex via `Pattern` with `\b…\b` wrapping for whole-word; bad regex → empty, `regexError(query)` reports it) plus `nextIndex`/`indexAt` navigation. **In-file** `ui/FindReplaceBar` (top of the editor, `C-s`/`C-r`/`M-S-5`; a repeated `C-s`/`C-r` **cycles** to the next/previous match, `C-g` closes the bar; the bar's actions are also **palette commands** `find.next`/`find.previous`/`find.replaceCurrent`/`find.replaceAll`, which open the bar if it's closed) delegates to it: **incremental** (debounced 150 ms search-as-you-type), case/regex/**whole-word** toggles, a "{n} of {total}" count, and **highlight-all** via **`editor/SearchHighlightOverlay`** (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`: amber wash on every visible match + an orange box on the active one; visible-only, coalesced, off in large-file mode; wired through `EditorBuffer.setSearchMatches`/`clearSearchMatches`). The bar takes a `Supplier<EditorBuffer>` (not just the `CodeArea`) so it can drive the overlay. **Seed from selection**: opening the bar (`FindReplaceBar.show`→`seedFromSelection`) or Find in Files (`MainController.openSearchInFiles`→`selectedLineForSearch`→`SearchPanel.setQuery`) pre-fills the query with the editor's selection when it's non-empty and on a single line (multi-line selections are left alone — they aren't sensible find terms), the VS Code convention. **Multi-file** lives in `com.editora.search`: pure **`MultiFileSearch`** (`matchesInText` → per-line 1-based `LineMatch{line,col,length,lineText}`; `replaceAll(text,query,replacement)` → spliced text + count, both unit-tested) and **`SearchService`** (the `GitService` idiom: daemon executor + generation guard) which walks the active project root (`ProjectManager.active()`, skipping dot-dirs / oversize / binary) **plus open buffers' in-memory text** (so unsaved edits win, and open files outside the root are included), capped, posting an `Outcome` on the FX thread. **Ripgrep backend (optional, auto-detected accelerator):** when `rg` is on PATH, `SearchService` runs the on-disk half of Find in Files through ripgrep instead of the Java walk — much faster and **`.gitignore`-aware** (rg's default; the walker now honors it too — see below). Pure `search/RipgrepArgs` (`SearchQuery`→flags) + `search/RipgrepOutput` (parse `rg --json`; rg's **byte** submatch offsets → Java **char** columns via `charIndexForByteOffset`, multibyte-safe; both unit-tested) + the `search/Ripgrep` facade (`command`/`detect`, the `mermaid/Mermaid` idiom). `SearchService.setBackend(useRipgrep, rgCommand, respectGitignore)` selects it; it **falls back to the walker** on an rg pattern/IO error (exit 2), a remote (non-`Vfs.isLocal`) root, or rg absent — and **open buffers always overlay** via `MultiFileSearch` (unsaved text wins, open files outside the root included). **`.gitignore` exclusion** (`Settings.searchRespectGitignore`, default **on**, schema 42→43; palette `view.toggleSearchGitignore`; Settings → Search): on ⇒ rg uses its native gitignore handling and the walker filters through the pure, unit-tested **`search/GitignoreFilter`** (parses the project-root `.gitignore` — comments, `!` negation/last-match-wins, `dir/` directory-only, root-anchored vs. base-name patterns, `*`/`**`/`?`/`[...]`; the walker `SKIP_SUBTREE`s ignored dirs like `target/`/`node_modules/` and skips ignored files like `*.log`); off ⇒ rg gets `--no-ignore` and the walker skips the filter. Reads only the root `.gitignore` (nested ones / `.git/info/exclude` are rg-only — the walker is the no-tools fallback). The **Project tool window's filter box** honors the same `Settings.searchRespectGitignore` (pushed via `MainController.applyProjectSupport` → `ProjectPanel.setRespectGitignore`, default on): its BFS filename search (`ProjectPanel.search`, unit-tested) skips `.gitignore`d files/subtrees (`target/`, `node_modules/`, `*.log`, …) via a `GitignoreFilter` loaded off-thread from the root, so the full lazy tree still shows everything but filtering hides ignored files. (Opening the Project window also focuses the filter field — `focusFirstItem` — with Down/Enter moving into / opening the results, via the shared `ui/FilterFieldNav.install(field, tree, onEnter)` bridge; the **Structure**, **Bookmarks**, and **Personal Notes** tool windows use the same helper + focus-the-filter-on-open, so all four filterable tool windows behave alike.) Gated by `Settings.ripgrepSearch` (default **on**) + `ripgrepCommand` (blank ⇒ `rg`); `MainController.applyRipgrepSupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirroring `applyMermaidSupport`) detects off-thread then `setBackend`s; **Settings → Search** page (toggle + path + found/not-found status) + palette `view.toggleRipgrep`/`search.setRipgrepCommand`; schema 36→37 additive-identity; no new dependency (rg resolved on PATH like git/mmdc). **`ui/SearchPanel`** ("Find in Files"; a `ToolWindowContent`, `tool.search` on `M-6`, `Icons::find`, registered `Side.RIGHT` — a *default* that respects each window's persisted `WorkspaceState.toolWindowSides`, so existing sessions keep BOTTOM) shows results grouped file→match (Emacs nav `C-n`/`C-p`/`C-f`/`C-b`) with a query/replace box; **`search.inFiles`** (`C-S-f`) opens+focuses it. **Selection opens the match** (mirroring `StructurePanel`): a `selectedItemProperty` listener (guarded by `suppressNavigation` during `setResults`' root swap) **previews** on single-click / keyboard selection — `Actions.openMatch(file, line, col, focusEditor=false)` jumps there but `SearchPanel.focusResults()` keeps focus in the tree so the user can keep arrowing — while **double-click / Enter activates** (`openMatch(…, true)`, focus into the editor). `MainController.openMatch` opens the path then `gotoInFile(file, line, col, focusEditor)` (the new overload only `requestFocus`es the area when `focusEditor`). **Panel extras:** a top **"Searching in:" scope row** (`.search-scope-*`, `SearchPanel.setScope(display, fullPath)`) shows the folder being searched — `MainController.searchScopeRoot()` = this window's project root, else the active file's parent folder ("Current Folder"), else null (open buffers only); home-collapsed display + full-path tooltip, pushed by `refreshSearchScope()` from `setWindowContext` / tab switch / `openSearchInFiles` / each search. That same `searchScopeRoot()` is now the scope passed to `searchService.search(...)`, so a **non-project window searches the current file's folder on disk** (previously it matched only open buffers). file-header rows are **bold** (`.search-file-row`); a **ripgrep badge** (`.search-backend-badge`, `SearchPanel.setBackendActive`, pushed from `applyRipgrepSupport`'s effective flag) shows when rg is the active backend; the query field is an **editable `ComboBox<String>`** bound to the persistent **search history** (`config/SearchHistory` → `search-history.json`, schema `ConfigSchema.SEARCH_HISTORY`, capped/deduped, most-recent-first; `Actions.recordSearch` on each run, `setHistory` binds the dropdown); and two **include/exclude glob fields** (comma-separated, parsed by pure `search/Globs.split`) flow through the widened `Actions.search(query, include, exclude)` → `SearchService.search(…, include, exclude, cb)` → ripgrep `-g`/`-g !` (`RipgrepArgs.build`) **and** the walker/open-buffer overlay (`Globs.accept` over the root-relative path, reusing `editorconfig/EditorConfigGlob.matches`). **Replace-in-files** (`MainController.replaceInFiles`): a confirm dialog, then open buffers are edited in-memory (undoable) and closed files rewritten on disk (UTF-8, EOL preserved since it lives in the text) via `MultiFileSearch.replaceAll`, then the search re-runs to refresh the panel. **Regex capture groups in replace:** in regex mode `replaceAll` routes through `Matcher.replaceAll` (shared `SearchMatcher.compileRegex`, so `$1`/`${name}` work; a bad group ref is a graceful no-op), while literal mode still splices `$` verbatim. **AceJump** (avy-goto-char): `nav.aceJump` (`M-g j`) → `EditorBuffer.startAceJump()` → **`editor/AceJumpOverlay`** takes the keys (`editora.ownsKeys` + `KEY_TYPED`/`KEY_PRESSED` filters on `area`, blocking insertion), the next typed char labels its visible occurrences with the pure/unit-tested **`editor/AceLabels`** (1-char while they fit, else uniform 2-char, capped at alphabet²), and typing a label jumps the caret; `Esc`/`C-g` (or scrolling) cancels. **Line-mode** (avy-goto-line): `nav.aceJumpLine` (`M-g L`) → `EditorBuffer.startAceJumpLine()` → `AceJumpOverlay.startLine()` labels every visible line at once (no char step) and typing a label jumps to that line's first non-whitespace character. **`M-g` closes a focused tool window** (any tool window, not just search) — a generic `KeyDispatcher` pre-dispatch hook (`setPreDispatch`) wired in `MainController.setKeyDispatcher` → `ToolWindowManager.toolWindowOf(target)` + `close` + refocus the editor. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** The Find-in-Files window wiring lives in **`ui/SearchCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `SearchService` + the `SearchPanel`, the scope/`runFileSearch`/`replaceInFiles`/`openToggle`/selection-seed logic, and the ripgrep/walker backend selection (`applyRipgrepSupport`/`probeRipgrep`), reaching the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for project root / open-match / tool-window toggle / open-buffer-for-path / search-history / rg-status); `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `searchCoordinator.panel()`), the search-history store, and the `search.*`/ripgrep command registrations (routing their apply through `applyRipgrepSupport`, their action through `openToggle`), and the MCP `findInFiles` bridge reuses `searchCoordinator.service()`. **Find-in-Files popup** (`search.inFilesPopup`, palette-only, no replace): a keyboard-first in-scene overlay `ui/SearchInFilesPopup` (modeled on `QuickOpen`/`CommandPalette`, shown via the shared `OverlayHost`, `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` dismiss) — a query field + case/regex/whole-word toggles (+ the same `ripgrep` backend badge as the panel, `setBackendActive` pushed from `applyRipgrepSupport` via the coordinator's `applyBackendBadge`) + an **editable search-folder field** over a grouped file→match result `ListView` (bold file headers with a match count, indented match rows with a muted line number + preview; `.fif-*` in `app.css`). Typing runs a debounced (150 ms) search through the same `SearchService` (via `SearchCoordinator.showFindInFilesPopup` + a small `SearchInFilesPopup.Ops` for the default root / async search / open-match / history); `↑↓`/`C-n`/`C-p` move, Enter jumps to the match (a header opens the file) and closes, run queries are recorded into the shared search history. The **root field seeds** from `searchScopeRoot()` (project root in a project window, else the active file's folder) and is user-editable (`~` expanded; a blank field or a non-directory ⇒ open-buffers-only, with a "folder not found" hint when non-blank); the pure `SearchInFilesPopup.displayPath(root, file)` (unit-tested) relativizes header paths. *Deferred: search-in-selection, a replace preview/diff.*
- `todo/` — **TODO / highlight patterns** (IntelliJ-style "TODO" patterns; **on by default**, gated by `Settings.todoHighlight`). User-configurable regex patterns are highlighted everywhere they match in the editor and listed in a tool window. Pure, unit-tested core: **`TodoPattern`** (Jackson POJO `name`/`pattern`(regex)/`color`(web hex)/`caseSensitive`/`enabled`, persisted in `settings.toml` as `todoPatterns`, an array of tables — `opens com.editora.todo to jackson.databind`), **`TodoPatterns`** (`compile(list)` → `Compiled{name,color,Pattern}` skipping disabled/blank/invalid-regex; `defaults()` = the standard keyword set **TODO/FIXME/HACK/NOTE/XXX + DONE** (the mark-done state), case-sensitive `\bWORD\b`, each a distinct color; `DONE_KEYWORD`="DONE"), **`TodoScanner.scan(text, compiled)`** → `TodoMatch{start,end,line,col,lineText,patternName,color,parsed}` in document order (mirrors `MultiFileSearch.matchesInText`; matches **anywhere**, zero-length-safe). **Structured "Comment Manager" format** (IntelliJ [TODO Highlighter & Comment Manager](https://plugins.jetbrains.com/plugin/32376)): pure/unit-tested **`TodoComment.parse(lineText, kwStart, kwEnd)`** splits a match into `{keyword, tag, priority, description}` + each part's line offsets — an optional `[tag]` then optional `(priority)` (critical/high/medium/low, case-insensitive) right after the keyword (a `TODO:` colon tolerated), the rest is the description; carried on `TodoMatch.parsed` (a back-compat `TodoMatch` ctor omits it, so it's null-safe). **`TodoColors`** (pure): the default per-priority + tag part colors; the user-configurable set is the pure/unit-tested **`TodoPartColors`** (`of(tag,critical,high,medium,low)` falling back to the `TodoColors` default for a blank field), built by `TodoCoordinator` from `Settings.todoTagColor`/`todoPriority{Critical,High,Medium,Low}Color`. **In-editor highlight**: `editor/TodoHighlightOverlay` (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SearchHighlightOverlay`: visible-only, coalesced, 1×1 when empty, off in large-file mode) washes **each parsed part** in its color — keyword in its pattern color, `[tag]` in the tag color (with an underline), `(priority)` in its level color — fed neutral `editor/TodoMark{start,end,colorWeb, tag/pri absolute spans + colors}` via an injected `editor/TodoMatcher` (keeps `editor` free of `todo`/`config`); `EditorBuffer.setTodoMatcher`/`setTodoHighlightEnabled` recompute on the existing debounced (300 ms) edit pulse. **`TodoService`** (the `SearchService` idiom: daemon executor + generation guard) scans the active project root (skipping dot-dirs/oversize/binary, and — when `Settings.searchRespectGitignore` is on, via `setRespectGitignore` + the shared `search/GitignoreFilter`, mirroring Find in Files — `.gitignore`d paths like `target/`/`node_modules/`) **plus open buffers' live text**, capped, posting an `Outcome` on the FX thread. **`ui/TodoPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`; id `todo`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.todo`/`M-g o`, `Icons::todo`) is the Comment-Manager list: a **"Group by" selector** (File/Priority/Tag/Keyword, via the pure/unit-tested **`todo/TodoGrouping`** — priority groups ordered by urgency with the no-priority bucket last, tag/keyword ordered with the catch-all last, file keeps active-file-first) over a tree whose match rows render the structured parts colored in a `TextFlow` (`KEYWORD [tag] (priority) description` + a muted `— file:line`); Enter / double-click → `gotoInFile`, `C-n`/`C-p` nav; a Refresh button; auto-scoped (project root if a project is open, else open files). **Editable from the panel** (right-click a match): **Mark Done** (rewrites the keyword to `DONE`) / **Reopen**, a **Priority** submenu (critical/high/medium/low/none), and **Edit Description…** — each rebuilds the comment line via the pure/unit-tested **`todo/TodoEdit`** (preserves the indent + comment opener, re-emits `KEYWORD [tag] (priority) description` canonically) and applies it through `TodoCoordinator.Ops.applyLineEdit` → `MainController.applyTodoLineEdit`, which opens the file, verifies the target line still matches the scan snapshot (else a status + re-scan), then replaces exactly that paragraph via an **undoable** `replaceText` (marks the buffer dirty; guarded by `activeEditable()`), and the panel re-scans. **The active file's group sorts to the top** (IDE convention) via `TodoPanel.setActiveFile(normalizedPath)`, pushed on every tab switch by `TodoCoordinator.setActiveFile` (the shared pure `ui/ActiveFileOrder`; as-walked path form to match the scan keys). A top **"Scanning in:" scope row** (`TodoPanel.setScope(display, fullPath)`, reusing the Find-in-Files `.search-scope-*` styling) shows that scope (home-collapsed + full-path tooltip; "open files only" when no project), pushed by the coordinator's `refreshScope()` from `runScan()`. **`ui/TodoCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `TodoService` + the `TodoPanel`, reaching the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension for the project root / open-match / tool-window toggle / home-collapsed path): `applyHighlight()` (init + every settings apply) compiles the patterns into a `TodoMatcher` and pushes it + the on/off to every buffer (`toTodoMarks` maps scanner→marks); `runScan()` drives the panel; `refreshPanelIfOpen()` re-scans when patterns change. It registers `tool.todo` (toggle + scan), `todo.refresh`, and `todo.addPattern` (palette quick-add: name → regex prompt), and `todo.next`/`todo.previous` (`M-g ]`/`M-g [` — move the caret to the next/previous TODO match in the active file, wrapping, via `EditorBuffer.jumpToNextTodo`/`jumpToPreviousTodo` over the buffer's live `TodoMatcher` marks); `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `todoCoordinator.panel()`), calls `applyToBuffer`/`applyHighlight` from `addBuffer`/init/settings-apply, and keeps the `view.toggleTodoHighlight` command (the generic `toggleSetting`, delegating its apply to the coordinator). **Overview stripes** (IntelliJ-style, mirroring the LSP diagnostic stripes): `editor/TodoStripe` — a thin per-match stripe docked over the scrollbar (generic colored marks + click-to-jump + a line-text hover tooltip, the `DiagnosticStripe` idiom; positioned beside it via `EditorBuffer.updateTodoStripe`, shifted left by `DiagnosticStripe.WIDTH` when LSP is also active so they don't overlap) — plus **left-edge ticks on the `Minimap`** (`setTodoMarks`/`setTodoEnabled`, drawn on the left so they never clash with the right-edge diagnostics). Both are fed the same `List<TodoMark>` from `EditorBuffer.refreshTodoMarks` (so `TodoMark` carries the 0-based `line` + `lineText` alongside the offsets); inert/empty when off or huge-file. **Settings → Editor → TODO Highlighting**: an enable checkbox + a per-pattern editor (enabled / name / regex / a real **`ColorPicker`** / case + add/remove; text fields commit on Enter/blur, the picker + checkboxes immediately) + a **TODO Part Colors** section with five `ColorPicker`s (tag + the four priority levels) writing `Settings.todoTagColor`/`todoPriority*Color` live; the palette `todo.setPartColor` (pick a part → `#RRGGBB` prompt) mirrors it and re-syncs the Settings pickers. `Settings.todoHighlight` (default true) + `todoPatterns`; schema 32→33 (todoHighlight/todoPatterns), **49→50**, 55→56 (todoGroupBy), **57→58** (the five part colors) (`ConfigMigrations.growTodoDefaultKeywords` grows an existing user's `todoPatterns` to include the new HACK/NOTE/XXX/DONE defaults, keeping custom entries + never duplicating). CSS `.todo-panel`/`.todo-file-row`/`.todo-run`/`.todo-row-location`/`.todo-color-tag`/`.todo-stripe-tooltip` (the editor highlight + stripes + structured rows are inline-colored). i18n in all six catalogs (`todo.groupBy.*`/`todo.menu.*`/`todo.priority.*`). **No new dependency.** *Deferred: comment/string-only matching (TextMate-scope-aware).*
- `externaltool/` — **External Tools** (IntelliJ-style user-defined CLI commands, always available; the tool list is empty by default so it's inert until configured; **disabled in Simple UI mode**). Pure, unit-tested core: **`ExternalTool`** (Jackson POJO mirroring `todo/TodoPattern`: `name`/`command`/`arguments`/`workingDir`/`StdinSource {NONE,SELECTION,BUFFER}`/`OutputTarget {CONSOLE,REPLACE_SELECTION,REPLACE_BUFFER,INSERT_AT_CARET}`/`enabled`; static `commandIdFor(name)` → `externalTool.run.<slug>`, `slug` copied from `MacroService`), **`ToolContext`** (record captured from the active buffer: filePath/fileDir/fileName/baseName/selectedText/1-based line+column/projectFileDir/bufferText), **`ToolMacros.expand(template, ctx)`** (pure `$Name$` expander over `$FilePath$ $FileDir$ $FileName$ $FileNameWithoutExtension$ $SelectedText$ $LineNumber$ $ColumnNumber$ $ProjectFileDir$`; unknown `$X$` left literal, `$$`→`$`), **`ToolInvocation.of(tool, ctx, defaultDir)`** (argv = `tokenize(expand(command)) ++ tokenize(expand(arguments))` via `run/ProgramArgs.tokenize`; workingDir = expanded or default; stdin per source; `displayCommand`). The impure **`ExternalToolService`** (the `MermaidService` idiom: single daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) runs an invocation off-thread via **`ProcessRunner.run(workingDir,timeout,argv,env,stdin)`** — a **new stdin overload** on the single subprocess chokepoint that writes the buffer/selection to the child's stdin on a daemon thread then **closes** it (so `jq`/`wc` see EOF); 2-min `DEFAULT_TIMEOUT`. **`ui/ExternalToolPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `RunPanel` minus Stop/stdin — runs are one-shot; id `externalTool`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::tools`, `tool.externalTools`; reuses the `run-*` CSS + the package-private `RunPanel.installLinkClicks` so output paths are clickable). **`ui/ExternalToolCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern, like `HttpClientCoordinator`) owns the `ExternalToolService` + the console panel + the run/output logic + the `externalTool.*` commands, reaching the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension (`projectRoot()`/`openConsole()`/`onOutputLink(link)`); `MainController` keeps only the `externalToolToolWindow` (built with `externalToolCoordinator.panel()` as content; **registered default-hidden** via `toolWindows.register(tw, false)` — the stripe is off until enabled via `tool.externalTools` / the `externalTool.run` picker / Settings → Tool Windows), its availability gating, the `tool.externalTools` toggle, and a thin `refreshExternalToolCommands()` delegate (the `WindowManager` broadcast contract). The coordinator's `buildContext()`/`defaultDir()` read the active buffer + window project; `run(tool)` → `ExternalToolService.run` → `applyResult` on the FX thread — CONSOLE opens the panel always; REPLACE_*/INSERT apply stdout **only when `r.ok() && !r.out().isEmpty()`** (mirrors `format-runner-plugin`), stripping one trailing newline for selection/caret inserts, else surfacing stderr in the panel + status; `REPLACE_BUFFER`→`area.replaceText(out)` (whole-document undoable, as `ActiveEditor.setText`), `REPLACE_SELECTION`→`replaceSelection`, `INSERT_AT_CARET`→`insertText`. **Dynamic commands** mirror the macro pattern: `registerExternalToolCommands`/`refreshExternalToolCommands` register one `externalTool.run.<slug>` per *enabled* tool (title = tool name, so it's palette- + keybinding-editor-visible and key-bindable), re-synced across windows via `WindowManager.broadcastExternalToolsChanged()` from `onSettingsApplied`. Static commands `externalTool.run` (`QuickOpen` picker), `externalTool.rerunLast`, `externalTool.clearOutput` (`ExternalToolPanel.clearConsole`), `tool.externalTools`. **Gating** = `externalToolsEnabled() = !simpleModeActive()`; the palette predicate hides `externalTool.*`/`tool.externalTools` in Simple mode and `runExternalTool` early-returns. **Persistence**: `Settings.externalTools : List<ExternalTool>` in `settings.toml` (default empty; `opens com.editora.externaltool to jackson.databind`; schema 35→36 additive-identity). **Settings → External Tools** is a **master-detail** page (left `ListView` of tool names + Add/Remove; right form: name/command/arguments/working-dir/stdin combo/output combo/enabled, localized enum `StringConverter`s + a `$Macros$` help note) reusing the `todoRow` commit idiom (combos/checkbox apply immediately, text fields on Enter/blur → `setExternalTools` + `apply()`). i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency.** *Deferred: live-streamed console output (v1 is one-shot capture), per-tool timeout/env, output-to-new-file, `$Prompt$`.*
- `macro/` — **keyboard macros** (Emacs-style record/replay, always on). Pure, unit-tested model + engine: **`MacroStep`** (a record `{kind,value}` with `kind ∈ command|text`; the `is*` accessors are `@JsonIgnore`d so the boolean getters don't pollute `macros.json` or break record deserialization), **`Macro`** (`name` + ordered `List<MacroStep>`), **`MacroRecorder`** (accumulates the interleaved stream; `recordCommand`/`recordChar`, consecutive chars coalesced into one TEXT step; no-op unless `start()`ed), **`MacroPlayer`** (`play(macro, times, runCommand, typeText)` dispatches each step in order N times; a single `playing` re-entrancy guard makes a self-referential / bound-to-itself macro run once, not recurse). **`MacroService`** (per-window coordinator over `ConfigManager`; depends only on config + the pure model) owns the recorder/player + the just-recorded "last" macro, exposes `start/stopRecording`, the recording hooks `onCommand`/`onTypedChar` (both short-circuit on `!isRecording()` — the idle hot path — and ignore replay), `replayLast`/`run`, `saveLast`/`saved`/`delete`, and the static `commandIdFor`/`slug`. **Capture** is two hooks fed in FX-event order so commands and typed text interleave correctly: `CommandRegistry.setExecutionListener(Consumer<String>)` (fires after each `run(id)`; `onCommand` ignores `macro.*` + `palette.show`) and `KeyDispatcher.setTypedListener(Consumer<Character>)` (each real, non-consumed `KEY_TYPED` char). **Replay of TEXT steps** routes through **`EditorBuffer.typeChar/typeString`**, which reuses the *same* assists the live key filters use — extracted into `applyEnter` (Markdown-list/`Indenter` auto-indent), `applyAutoCloseTyped` (`AutoClose` pair/skip/wrap), `applyCloserDedent`, and `applySmartTab` — so a replayed `(` pairs and a replayed newline re-indents exactly as hand-typed (no synthetic `KeyEvent`s, which would re-enter `KeyDispatcher`). COMMAND steps replay via `registry::run`. **Persistence** is app-global `config/MacroStore` (`schemaVersion` + `List<Macro>`, `put`/`find`/`remove`) in `macros.json`, owned by `SharedConfig` (`getMacroStore`/`saveMacros`, loaded via `ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(..., ConfigSchema.MACROS)`) and delegated by `ConfigManager`; `opens com.editora.macro to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind` (the records). **Each saved macro is registered as a synthetic command `macro.run.<slug>`** (explicit title = the macro name) so it appears in the palette and the Settings → Keymaps keybinding editor and is **bindable to a key** like any command; `MainController.refreshSavedMacroCommands` drops stale `macro.run.*` then re-registers the current set, and `WindowManager.broadcastMacrosChanged()` runs it in every window after a save/delete (mirroring `broadcastSettingsApplied`). The window wiring lives in **`ui/MacroCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern): it owns the per-window `MacroService`, the capture hooks (`onCommand`/`onTypedChar`, fed from `CommandRegistry.setExecutionListener` + `KeyDispatcher.setTypedListener`), and the `macro.*` commands, reaching the window via the shared host plus a one-method `Ops` extension (`refreshAllWindows`, which needs `WindowManager`); `MainController` keeps only a thin `refreshSavedMacroCommands()` delegate (the `WindowManager` broadcast contract) + `refreshSavedMacroCommandsAllWindows()`. Commands (registered by the coordinator): `macro.startRecording` (`F3`), `macro.stopRecording` (`F4`), `macro.replayLast` (`C-x e`; auto-finalizes if still recording), plus palette-only `macro.replayLastN` (count prompt), `macro.nameAndSave`, `macro.runSaved` (`QuickOpen` picker), `macro.deleteSaved`. Status echoes via `setStatus` (`status.macro.*`). Bound only in `emacs.json` (Emacs has no `.mac` variant); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency.** **Settings → Macros management page** (`SettingsWindow.macrosEditor`, `Category.MACROS` under the System group): a master-detail editor over `config.getMacroStore().macros` — list saved macros, **rename** (with keybinding migration old→new id), **edit the steps** (a `MacroStep` list with Add Command / Add Text / reorder ▲▼ / Remove + an editable value field for the selected step), **delete**, and **assign a keybinding inline** (reuses the Keymaps `ShortcutActions` rebind/reset + the shared `rebindWithConflictCheck`, capturing chords via `KeyDispatcher.chord`; binds the macro's `macro.run.<slug>` command). Persists via `config.saveMacros()` then the injected `setMacrosChangedHandler` (→ `MainController.refreshSavedMacroCommandsAllWindows`) re-registers the commands in every window. *Deferred: import/export, a persistent "● REC" status segment, scripting overlay/picker input during replay.*
- `maven/` — **Maven support** (IntelliJ-style toolbar icon + actions popup reading the active project's pom.xml; on by default, self-gating — the toolbar button stays hidden until a pom.xml is actually detected; **disabled in Simple UI mode** and for remote/SFTP files). Pure, unit-tested core: **`PomModel`** (record: groupId/artifactId/version/packaging, top-level `List<Plugin> plugins`, `List<Profile> profiles`; `Plugin{groupId,artifactId,version,List<Execution> executions}`, `Execution{id,phase,List<String> goals}` — `phase` is the literal text only, no default-phase resolution — `Profile{id,activeByDefault,List<Plugin> plugins}`, the last holding that profile's own `<build>/<plugins>` **not merged** into the top-level list). **`PomParser.parse(xml)`/`parseFile(path)`** uses the JDK's own `javax.xml.parsers` DOM parser (no third-party XML dependency), hardened against XXE (DOCTYPE disallowed outright, external general/parameter entities and external DTD loading disabled, no XInclude/entity-reference expansion) — deliberately **not** an "effective pom": no parent inheritance beyond a direct `<parent>` groupId/version fallback, no default-lifecycle-binding lookup, and `<pluginManagement>` is skipped entirely (contributes no runnable goal unless redeclared in `<plugins>`). **`MavenPluginPrefix.derive(groupId, artifactId)`** is Maven's own CLI-prefix convention (`maven-<name>-plugin` or `<name>-maven-plugin` → `<name>`, else the bare artifactId — validated against this repo's own pom: `spotless-maven-plugin`→`spotless`, `jacoco-maven-plugin`→`jacoco`, `exec-maven-plugin`→`exec`, …). **`MavenLifecycle.PHASES`** is the fixed `clean, validate, compile, test, package, verify, install, site, deploy` list. **`MavenExecutable.chooseArgv(hasWrapperUnix, hasWrapperWin, isWindows, overrideCommand)`** prefers the project's own `./mvnw`/`mvnw.cmd` wrapper when present (the caller does the `Files.isExecutable` probes, keeping this pure), else a Settings override (tokenized via the existing public `run/ProgramArgs.tokenize`), else bare `"mvn"` (resolved later via `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`). **`MavenArgs.build(goalsOrPhases, activeProfiles)`** appends a trailing `-P<a>,<b>` flag when profiles are checked. The one impure class, **`MavenService`**, mirrors `run/RunService`'s exact shape (daemon pump threads, a monotonic generation guard) but keyed on an explicit working-directory `Path` rather than a file's parent (Maven always runs at the project root). **`ui/MavenPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `RunPanel` minus the stdin field — a build isn't interactive) reuses the existing `.run-panel`/`.run-output`/`.run-status` CSS and the shared `run.*` i18n status strings. **`ui/MavenActionsPopup`** is modeled on `BranchPopup` (search field + sectioned `ListView`, arrow-key nav, Enter/click to run, Esc to close): a top "Run custom goal(s)…" action row (freeform `promptText`), a **Lifecycle** section (one row per phase), a **Profiles** section (checkable rows — checking one does **not** close the popup, since a profile composes with a phase/goal rather than acting standalone, and toggles that profile's own nested plugin section), a top-level **Plugins** section (one row per plugin execution's bound goal, labeled `<prefix>:<goal>`, tooltipped with its phase + execution id — a plugin with **no** bound executions is omitted, not shown for reference, since a non-runnable row is dead weight in a run-oriented popup; the freeform box covers those), and a nested **per-checked-profile Plugins** section for any profile declaring its own `<build>/<plugins>` (this repo's own pom concentrates almost all interesting plugins — antrun/exec/shade/jpackage/dependency — inside its `dist`/`fatjar`/`apidocs` profiles, not the top level, so this nesting is load-bearing, not cosmetic). **`ui/MavenCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern, mirroring `GitCoordinator`'s per-project detect/cache/refresh model) owns the service + panel + popup: `contextPath()` picks the active local file, else the active project root; `refresh()` walks up via the existing `lsp/RootResolver.findMarkerRoot(context, List.of("pom.xml"))` and parses the found `pom.xml` off-thread (generation-guarded), then flips the toolbar button's visibility — refreshed at startup and on the same cadence Git already uses (tab switch, window focus-regain, save, every settings apply). A malformed pom is tracked distinctly (pom found but `model == null`) so `showActionsPopup`/`runGoals` report a clear status instead of silently no-opping. `MainController` keeps the `mavenButton` toolbar button (hidden + unmanaged until `MavenCoordinator.Ops.setToolbarButtonVisible` says otherwise; a `reapplyVisibility()` re-derives it from the cached detection — no fresh re-detect — after a Simple-Mode toggle, since that only changes `isEnabled()`, not what's on disk) and the default-hidden `mavenToolWindow` (auto-opens on a run). **`OverlayHost` gained a `showBelow(...)` variant** (mirroring the existing `positionAbove`/private `show(...)`): the toolbar button is a top-of-window anchor, where the pre-existing above-anchoring would grow the card off the top of the window or land it far away, so a new `positionBelow` pins the card's top just below the anchor instead — purely additive, every existing `show(...)` caller is unchanged. **Settings**: `Settings.mavenSupport` (default **true** — inert until a pom.xml is found, the Mermaid/CSV-grid convention) + `Settings.mavenCommand` override (schema 61→62 additive), a Settings → Languages & Tools → **Maven** page (enable checkbox + command-override field + a found/not-found status reading the coordinator's cached detection — no separate subprocess probe needed, unlike Mermaid's mmdc/maid). Commands `view.toggleMavenSupport`, `tool.maven`, `maven.showActions` (also the toolbar button's own action), `maven.runCustom`, `maven.stop`, `maven.rerunLast`, `maven.refresh` — all palette-filtered when the feature/Simple-Mode gate says no (`Chrome.PaletteGates.maven`). i18n in all six catalogs; the Apache Maven feather toolbar glyph is vendored from Simple Icons (CC0, attributed in NOTICE). **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** beyond `requires java.xml;` (a JDK module, already implicitly bundled by jlink). *Deferred: full effective-pom resolution (default-lifecycle bindings by packaging type, real parent-POM inheritance, `<pluginManagement>`), a persistent run-configuration list, a project-tree "Run Maven Goal…" context-menu entry.*
- `git/` — **native-CLI Git integration** (no JGit; we shell out to the user's `git`). `ProcessRunner` is the *only* place Editora runs a subprocess: `ProcessBuilder` + concurrent stdout/stderr drainers + a hard timeout, `LC_ALL=C` and `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` for stable parsing and lock-free status. `GitService` is the facade: every command runs on a single daemon executor (the `highlightExecutor` idiom) and posts results to the FX thread via `Platform.runLater`; `git --version` presence and `rev-parse --show-toplevel` repo roots are cached, and `refresh(contextPath, diffFile, cb)` (status `--porcelain=v2 --branch` + `diff -U0 HEAD -- file`) carries a generation guard so stale results are dropped. Two **pure, unit-tested** parsers feed the UI: `StatusParser` (porcelain-v2 → `GitStatus`{branch, upstream, ahead/behind, `FileEntry`s with porcelain index/worktree letters + rename `origPath`}) and `DiffParser` (hunk headers → `LineChange`{0-based startLine, count, `ChangeType` ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED}; pure-insertion `b==0`→ADDED, pure-deletion `d==0`→a single DELETED marker on the following line, else MODIFIED — a v1 approximation). **`ChangeType.cssClass()`** maps to `git-added`/`git-modified`/`git-deleted`. *Caution:* a static `Path.of(...)` sentinel must not contain a NUL — `NO_ROOT = Path.of("")` (empty path, never returned by rev-parse, compared by identity). **Gutter change bars** (in `editor/`): `EditorBuffer.setChangeBars(Map<line,cssClass>, Map<line,hunkText>)` stores both maps (null = not tracked) and `FoldManager` (via `setChangeHook(enabled, classFor, tooltipFor)`) reserves a fixed `CHANGE_SLOT_WIDTH` stripe at the gutter's inner edge on every row while tracking is on (so a bar appearing/vanishing never shifts text indent), repainting only changed lines (`recreateParagraphGraphic`); colors are AtlantaFX semantic (`.git-change-bar.git-*` in `app.css`), off in large-file mode. **Hovering a change bar** shows that hunk's unified diff (the `-`/`+` lines) in a monospace `.git-diff-tooltip` — the per-line hunk text comes from `DiffParser.parseToHunkText` (pure, unit-tested; same `git diff -U0 HEAD` output that feeds the bars) carried on `GitService.GitDiff`/`RepoState.hunks`. **UI**: `StatusBar.setGitBranch(branch, ahead, behind)` shows a clickable `⎇ branch ↑a↓b` segment (`git.switchBranch`) **only when the active file is inside a repo** — a null/blank branch hides the segment entirely (centralized in `StatusBar.applyGitVisibility`: visible iff `gitFeatureEnabled && gitInRepo && !simpleMode`, so it's gone for files outside any repo and on the no-file Welcome tab). To keep that accurate per active file, `MainController.refreshGit()` short-circuits to `RepoState.NONE` when `gitContextPath()` is null (no file + no project), instead of falling back to the process working directory's repo. The **Commit** tool window is shown only inside a repo via **`ToolWindowManager.setAvailable(tw, inRepo)`** — a *transient* hide (distinct from the persisted `setVisible`; guarded by `shouldShowButton = isVisible && !unavailable`) so it never clobbers the user's show/hide preference; driven from `applyGitState`. The Commit + Git Log setters (`setCommitWindowAvailable`/`setGitLogWindowAvailable`) additionally **`&& activeBuffer() != null`**, and `updateBufferToolWindows()` force-hides both on a non-buffer tab — they act on the active file, so they vanish on the Welcome tab even inside a repo. `GitPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `BookmarksPanel`) groups Staged/Changes/Untracked with stage/unstage/discard + a commit box (Ctrl/Cmd+Enter), routing mutations through an `Actions` callback. The whole integration is **gated by `Settings.gitSupport`** ("Enable Git", Settings → Git, default **on** — self-gating, inert until `git` is on PATH): `MainController.applyGitSupport()` (mirrors `applyProjectSupport` — called at init + on every settings apply) disables the status-bar segment (`StatusBar.setGitEnabled`), hides the Commit window (`setAvailable(false)`), clears every open buffer's gutter bars, and the **`ifGit(...)`** wrapper makes each Git command/keybinding a no-op; `git.*`/`tool.commit` are filtered from the command palette + tool-window picker, and `refreshGit()` early-returns when off. `MainController` owns the wiring: it keeps `currentRepoRoot`, runs `refreshGit()` on tab switch / window focus-regain / save / auto-save / project switch (all coalesced by the service's generation guard), and `applyGitState(RepoState)` updates the status bar + `GitPanel` + active buffer's change bars in one pass. After a **git mutation** (commit/stage/unstage/discard/checkout/pull/push/refresh) it instead calls **`afterGitMutation()`**, which does `refreshGit()` *plus* re-diffs every **other open buffer in the same repo** (via `GitService.diff`) so a commit clears the gutter bars on background tabs too, not just the visible one. Git command **failures** are shown via **`gitError(summary, detail)`** — a scrollable error dialog (the often-multiline git stderr is unreadable in the one-line status bar) plus a short status summary. **The Git mutation operations live in `GitCoordinator`** alongside the engine (it already owned `GitService` + repo state): `gitOp`/`gitCommit`/`discardChanges`, `checkoutBranch`/`checkoutRemoteBranch`/`newBranch`, `gitSync`/`gitPush`, the stash commands (`gitStash`/`gitStashPop`/`gitUnstash`/`gitStashDrop`), the active-file `gitStageActiveFile`/`gitUnstageActiveFile`/`gitDiscardActiveFile`, `gitCommitFocus`, the `gitError` dialog, and **`git.clone`** (`GitCoordinator.cloneRepo` — the URL+destination `OverlayInput` form → `GitService.clone` → `openClonedEntry` opens a file from the clone; the pure/unit-tested folder-name deriver is `GitCoordinator.repoNameFromUrl`, named `cloneRepo` to avoid clashing with `Object.clone()`) — all running through its own `service()`/`repoRoot()`/`afterMutation()`; `MainController` keeps the `GitPanel`/`GitLogPanel`/`BranchPopup` + tool windows + `git.*` command registrations + the Git-Log/blame flows (their `Actions`/callbacks delegate to `git.*`; the clone callbacks — the `git.clone` command, the empty-`GitPanel` button, and the `BranchPopup` No-VCS action — delegate to `git::cloneRepo`), plus the `WindowOps` the coordinator drives (commit-message clear/focus, open Commit window, `checkExternalChanges`, `reloadAllFromDiskSilently`, the clone form's `keymap`/`openPath`). Commands (all no-op with a clear status when git is absent / not a repo): `git.commit` (`C-x g`, opens the Commit tool window + focuses the message), `git.stageFile` (+ the symmetric `git.unstageFile`/`git.discardFile` on the active file — `gitUnstageActiveFile`/`gitDiscardActiveFile`; discard confirms first), `git.switchBranch` (**toggles** `BranchPopup` — clicking the git status segment opens the dropdown, clicking again closes it; `MainController.chooseBranch` early-returns when `branchPopup.isShown()`/`justHidden()`, a `lastHiddenAt` guard absorbing the autoHide-then-click race like the message-log popup — an IntelliJ-style dropdown anchored above the status-bar branch segment via `StatusBar.gitSegmentNode()`: a search field over actions (New Branch/Pull/Fetch/Push/Commit) + Local/Remote branch sections from `GitService.branches`→`Branches{local:List<BranchInfo>, remote:List<String>}` (one `for-each-ref` with `%(upstream:short)`+`%(upstream:track)`, parsed by the unit-tested `GitService.parseTrack`); the header shows the **remote URL** (`Branches.remoteUrl` — origin's, else the first remote's); each local row shows its **upstream** + **incoming/outgoing** (`↓behind`/`↑ahead`) badge + tooltip ("Git Branch: … / N incoming commits"); local rows → `checkoutBranch`, remote rows → `checkoutRemoteBranch` (`checkout --track`)) and `git.newBranch`, `git.fetch`/`git.pull`/`git.push` (`runNetwork`, longer timeout; **`gitPush()`** uses `--set-upstream origin <branch>` when the branch has no upstream, else plain `push`), `git.refresh`, and `git.clone` (an `OverlayInput` form asks for **URL + destination directory** — a Browse button plus directory auto-fill to `<home>/<repo>` from the URL via the pure/unit-tested `GitCoordinator.repoNameFromUrl`; `GitService.clone` runs in the destination's parent; then `openClonedEntry` opens a file from the clone — its README if present — so Git activates **without** creating a project; clone/Projects are independent — also offered via a button in the empty `GitPanel`; the form + clone live in `GitCoordinator.cloneRepo`); the **Commit** tool window (id `commit`, title "Commit") is `tool.commit` (`M-4`) — the name "git" is intentionally left free for future use. Branch switch / pull / push call `reloadAllFromDiskSilently()` to refresh unmodified open buffers whose files changed on disk. **No new dependency / `module-info` change** — it's pure CLI. The diff viewer (below) reuses this facade — `GitService.show(root, spec, cb)` fetches a blob via `git show HEAD:/:/<ref>:rel`, `log(root, file, max, cb)` lists commits (pure `parseLog`), and the pure `repoRelative(root, file)` builds the `git show` spec. **History / Log, blame, and stash** (IntelliJ/VSCode-parity "Core trio", all `ifGit`-gated): `GitService` adds `blame(root, file, cb)` (`git blame --line-porcelain` → the pure, unit-tested `BlameParser` → `BlameLine{hash, author, epochSeconds, summary, uncommitted}`; all-zero sha ⇒ uncommitted), `commitFiles(root, hash, cb)` (`git diff-tree --no-commit-id --name-status -r -M` → the pure `parseNameStatus` → `CommitFile{status, path, origPath}`), `stashList(root, cb)` (`git stash list` → the pure, unit-tested `StashParser` → `StashEntry{index, ref, branch, subject}`), and reuses `run(...)` for the mutations (stash push/pop/apply/drop; `checkout`/`reset --soft|--mixed|--hard`/`revert --no-edit`/`cherry-pick <hash>`). The pure `RelativeTime.of(epoch, now)` buckets an age into `(Unit, value)` for blame labels (unit-tested). **Git Log tool window** (`ui/GitLogPanel`, a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `GitPanel`; id `gitLog`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.gitLog`/`M-g h`, `Icons::gitLog`, `setAvailable(inRepo)` from `applyGitState`): a commit `ListView` over the selected commit's changed files; selecting a commit fetches its files (`commitFiles`), double-clicking a file opens a **read-only** diff (commit~1 vs commit via `openDiff`), and a commit's context menu offers Copy Hash / Checkout / Soft·Mixed·Hard Reset / Revert / Cherry-Pick / New Branch (each → `MainController.gitMutate` → `gitService.run` → `afterGitMutation` + reload log). The same operations are also **palette commands** `git.log.checkout`/`newBranch`/`revert`/`cherryPick`/`reset`/`copyHash` that act on the panel's selected commit (`MainController.withSelectedCommit` over the new `GitLogPanel.selectedHash()`, reusing the stored `gitLogOps` `Actions` instance; `git.log.reset` prompts soft/mixed/hard via a `ChoiceDialog`). Whole-repo log = `tool.gitLog`; the active file's history = `git.fileHistory` (also the tab context menu's "Show File History"); `loadGitLog(file)` caps at 200 commits. **Blame annotations** (IntelliJ-style "Annotate" gutter column, all lines): a leftmost fixed-width gutter slot built by `FoldManager` (via `setBlameHooks(enabled, infoFor, columnWidth, onClick)` + `buildBlameSlot`, mirroring the breakpoint/bookmark/change-bar slots — so toggling it shifts the editor right as a block and line numbers stay aligned) shows per-line `author` (left, ellipsized) + `date` (right) with an **age-heatmap** background tint, a hover tooltip (full commit: author / date / relative time / summary / short hash), and click → that line's commit diff. `EditorBuffer.setBlame(List<editor/BlameInfo>)` stores the list, measures the (fixed) column width from the widest author+date in the editor font, and rebuilds the gutter; `blameHashAt(line)`/`blameHashAtCaret()`/`isBlameOn()` keep `editor` git-free (the neutral `BlameInfo{author, date, tooltip, bg, hash}` is mapped from git blame by `GitCoordinator.toBlameInfos`). The heatmap is the pure/unit-tested `git/BlameHeatmap.intensity(epoch, min, max)` (0=oldest → 1=newest across the file's committed lines) → a theme-aware rgba tint (`heatmapColor(intensity, dark)`); the date is ISO `yyyy-MM-dd` and the tooltip's relative time uses `RelativeTime` via i18n. The blame subprocess runs **once per file** (off-thread, re-run only on the coarse `applyGitState` events — tab switch / focus / save / mutation) and only the active buffer is annotated; there is no per-keystroke/per-caret work (the old per-caret `BlameOverlay` canvas was removed). **The whole inline-blame feature lives in `GitCoordinator`** — the engine (`applyBlame`/`refreshBlame`/`toBlameInfos`) *and* the UI (`toggleBlame`/`blameShowCommit`/`onGutterBlameClick`); `MainController` just registers the commands (delegating to `git::toggleBlame`/`git::blameShowCommit`) and wires the gutter click (`buffer.setGutterBlameClick(git::onGutterBlameClick)`). The two surfaces the UI touches outside the coordinator route through `WindowOps`: `syncBlameCheck()` (the Settings checkbox) and `openCommitFileDiff(hash, repoRel)` (the line's commit diff — through the window to reach `DiffCoordinator` without a circular dependency). Gated by `Settings.gitBlameInline` (default off; schema 20→21 additive-identity; `git.toggleBlame`/`M-g a`; Settings → Git checkbox + `SettingsWindow.syncGitBlameCheck`). `git.blameShowCommit` opens the caret line's commit diff; clicking any line's annotation opens that line's. CSS `.blame-slot`/`.blame-author`/`.blame-date`/`.blame-tooltip` in `app.css` (semantic colors, theme-tracking). **Stash** commands (`git.stash` with an optional message prompt, `git.stashPop`, `git.unstash`/`git.stashDrop` over a `QuickOpen<StashEntry>` picker) plus **Stash/Unstash** rows in the `BranchPopup` actions list. All gated by `gitEnabled()` (so disabled in Simple UI mode); `git.*`/`tool.gitLog` are palette-filtered when Git is off. *Deferred (later phase): a richer log graph/filtering, live-as-you-type gutter diff vs the HEAD blob, interactive rebase/merge/tag UIs.*
- `diff/` — **Diff viewer + merge-conflict resolution** (SDD-driven). Pure, unit-tested core on **java-diff-utils** (`io.github.javadiffutils`, an automatic module — moditect injects a descriptor for the jlink dist, like pdfbox; deps only `java.base`, not signed so no strip). No diff-match-patch: its Maven artifact isn't a reliable JPMS module, so intra-line word highlighting is done in-house. **`DiffEngine.compute(left, right)` → `DiffModels.DiffModel`** walks the java-diff-utils `Patch` deltas into aligned **side-by-side rows** (`Row{type EQUAL/ADDED/REMOVED/MODIFIED, left, leftLine, right, rightLine, leftWordRanges, rightWordRanges}` — a CHANGE delta is paired line-by-line into MODIFIED rows + filler for the longer side) plus derived **unified rows** and `changeBlockStarts` (prev/next nav); `lines(text)` normalizes CRLF + drops one trailing newline. **`compute(left, right, DiffOptions{ignoreWhitespace, wordLevel})`** is the options overload (drives the File History tool window's inline-diff toggles): `ignoreWhitespace` runs the Myers diff over whitespace-normalized lines but — since normalization is strictly 1:1 per line — the delta positions still index the originals, so every `Row` renders the **original** text (only equality changes); `wordLevel=false` skips the per-line `InlineDiff` (whole-line highlight). `DiffService` gained a matching options overload. **`InlineDiff`** tokenizes a changed line into word/non-word runs, diffs the token lists, and maps changed tokens back to `[start,end)` char ranges (word-level emphasis, no second lib). **`ConflictParser`** parses Git markers (`<<<<<<<`/`|||||||`/`=======`/`>>>>>>>`) → ours/**base**/theirs segments (the 3-way `|||||||` common-ancestor region is **captured** when present — i.e. `diff3`/`zdiff3` `merge.conflictStyle`; empty under Git's default `merge` style, gated via `Conflict.hasBase()`/`ConflictFile.hasBase()`) + `resolve(file, choices)` (OURS/THEIRS/**BASE**/BOTH/UNRESOLVED-keeps-markers, where UNRESOLVED round-trips the captured base region verbatim). **`PatchWriter.unifiedDiff`** → a `.patch` via `UnifiedDiffUtils`; the reverse direction, **`PatchParser.parse(text)`**, is a pure/unit-tested parser that reconstructs each file section's old/new line sequences from a unified diff (tolerant of a bare `diff -u` file, a git `diff --git`/`index`/rename preamble, several files back to back, `/dev/null` add/delete sides, and a `\ No newline at end of file` marker; a hunk's declared `@@ -a,b +c,d @@` line counts gate exactly how many lines are consumed as content, so a removed/added line that happens to start with `---`/`+++` is never mistaken for the next file's header). The reconstructed lines feed straight back into `DiffEngine.compute` — no new row type needed. **`DiffCoordinator.openPatchFile(buffer)`** opens the active `.patch`/`.diff` buffer's first file-section as a read-only structured diff tab this way (via the tab-menu **"Open in Diff Viewer"** item — shown only for a `.patch`/`.diff` file — or the palette-only `diff.openPatchFile`); it parses the buffer's own live text (not a re-read from disk), so unsaved edits to the patch are reflected, and reports a status note when the patch has more than one file (v1 shows just the first). **`DiffService`** runs `DiffEngine` off the FX thread (the `GitService` idiom; posts `null` past a 60k-line guard). **UI** (`ui/`): **`DiffViewerPane implements TabContent`** — side-by-side (default) is two read-only `editor-area` `CodeArea`s with synced vertical scroll (guarded `estimatedScrollYProperty` listeners; aligned row counts mean equal line heights), per-side original-line-number gutters (`setParagraphGraphicFactory`), TextMate syntax (`TextMateHighlighter.compute`) **overlaid** with intra-line `.diff-word` spans (`StyleSpans.overlay`), and per-line diff backgrounds via `setParagraphStyle` (`.diff-added/-removed/-modified/-filler`); a toolbar toggles **unified** (one CodeArea, `+/−` gutter), navigates prev/next change, and exports the patch. The toolbar's view-toggle / apply-all / prev / next actions are also **palette commands** `diff.toggleView`/`diff.applyAll`/`diff.nextChange`/`diff.previousChange` (via `DiffCoordinator.withActiveDiff` over the active tab's `DiffViewerPane`; `applyAllChanges()` no-ops on a read-only diff). **`MergeViewerPane implements TabContent`** lists each conflict (ours/theirs `TextArea`s — plus a middle **base** column with an **Accept Base** button when the conflict `hasBase()`, styled `.merge-base`) with Accept Ours/Theirs/Both + a resolved-count toolbar; Save routes the resolved lines back (replaces the active buffer text, undoable). **`Icons.diff()`/`merge()`** + `.diff-*`/`.merge-*` CSS in `app.css`. **The whole diff/merge feature lives in `ui/DiffCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `DiffService`, `openDiff`/`refreshOpenDiffs`/`withActiveDiff`, the `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` "apply change" flow, `worktreeText`, `exportPatch`, the compare entry points, and `resolveConflicts`; git-backed diffs reach the repo via the shared `GitCoordinator` passed in; reaches the window via an `Ops` extension for add-diff-tab / open-buffer-for-path / open-background-buffer / save-buffer / the open-&-active diff-pane lookups / finder-start-dir). `computeDiff` + `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` are **package-visible** so the Local File History tool window (`FileHistoryPanel`, via `HistoryCoordinator`) reuses them for its inline revision diff + per-hunk chevrons, and `applyToLocal` also lets History's `restoreHistory` write a restored revision through the same undoable-buffer path. **The Local File History feature itself lives in `ui/HistoryCoordinator`** (the same `CoordinatorHost` pattern) — it owns the `HistoryService` (off-thread snapshot/blob engine) + the `FileHistoryPanel`, the record hooks (save/autosave/external/pre-delete), the per-file + folder-history views, the label / recent-changes pickers, and the revision diff/restore (via the shared `DiffCoordinator`), reaching the window via an `Ops` extension (the `history/index.json` bucket maps + save / blobs dir / the File History tool-window availability+open / open-path / tree-refresh / current-text). **The revision diff lives inline in the tool window** (there is no separate history window — the old `ui/LocalHistoryWindow` was folded in): `FileHistoryPanel` is a horizontal `SplitPane` — the revision `ListView` (+ label/reason/time filter) on the left, and on the right a **live** side-by-side diff of the *selected* revision (before) vs the current file (after), rebuilt on selection by re-diffing off-thread via the injected `FileHistoryPanel.DiffSupport` (→ `DiffCoordinator.computeDiff`) into a reused `DiffViewerPane` (its own toolbar keeps side-by-side/unified + prev/next). A right-pane toolbar shows the revision-timestamp header, an **N-differences** count (`model.changeBlockStarts().size()`), **Ignore whitespace** / **Highlight words** `ToggleButton`s (both `recompute()` via `DiffEngine.DiffOptions`), and a **Revert** button (→ `restoreHistory`, undoable). The diff's current-file (RIGHT) side is **editable**, so the IntelliJ-style **per-hunk apply chevrons** do selective restore (a fragment from the snapshot into the file through the undoable buffer, via `DiffSupport.applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal`); after an apply/undo the panel re-baselines (`currentText`) and re-diffs so the remaining chevrons update (`reDiffAfterEdit`). No diff runs until a revision is selected (nothing when the window is closed / no selection), and the right pane resets to a "select a revision" prompt on tab switch / new file. `DiffSupport` is injected once by `HistoryCoordinator.setDiffSupport` (delegating to `historyService.content` / `diff.*` / `ops.currentTextOf` / `host.settings` / `restoreHistory`); folder-history mode keeps the tree on the left with the right pane disabled (its revisions belong to different files). `MainController` keeps the File History `ToolWindow` (built with `historyCoordinator.panel()`) + the `history.*`/`tool.fileHistory` command registrations + the project-tree "Show Local History" item (delegating to the coordinator). `MainController` keeps the `diff.*`/`merge.resolve` command registrations + the tab-menu / Git-panel / project-tree / Git-log entry points (delegating to the coordinator), and calls `diffCoordinator.refreshOpenDiffs()` on window focus-regain + in `afterGitMutation`. Entry points: `diff.vsHead` (`C-x v =`; tab menu "Compare with HEAD"; Git-panel "Show Diff" → `diffGitPanelFile(rel, staged)` = staged: index↔HEAD, unstaged: working↔index), `diff.compareWith` (FileFinder picks the second file — **ungated**), `diff.vsCommit` (`QuickOpen` over `GitService.log`), `merge.resolve` (opens the merge view when `ConflictParser.hasConflictMarkers`). Git-backed diffs are `ifGit`-gated; the working side uses the open buffer's live text when the file is open (canonical-path match), else disk. **Live refresh**: each side is a re-fetchable `DiffSide` (a `Consumer<Consumer<String>>` — a `git show` blob or `worktreeText`), and `openDiff` installs a `DiffViewerPane.refresher` that re-fetches both + `pane.updateContent(...)` **only when the content changed** (`pane.matches(l,r)` guard, so an unchanged refresh keeps the view + scroll); `refreshOpenDiffs()` (iterates tabs whose `userData instanceof DiffViewerPane`) runs on **window focus-regain** (a compared file changed on disk) and in **`afterGitMutation`** (a commit/stage/checkout moved HEAD/index/working). **Apply change** (IntelliJ's hunk-accept arrow): `DiffViewerPane.setEditable(EditableSide, onApply)` marks which side is the writable local file (RIGHT for vs-HEAD/vs-commit/unstaged, LEFT for compare-with, NONE for staged index↔HEAD); that side's gutter then shows apply chevrons (`.diff-apply`): a **single chevron on every changed row** (per-line / sub-hunk — `applyRow` → `computeApplied(i,i+1)`) and a **double chevron at each change block's first row** (whole hunk — `applyBlock(start)` → `computeApplied(start, blockEndFrom(start))`), both over the pure aligned rows; an **Apply-all** toolbar button (`Icons.check()`, shown only when a side is editable) replaces the editable file with the other side wholesale. Both hand the new full text to `DiffCoordinator.applyToLocal(target, text)` — which routes through an **undoable editor buffer** (`bufferForApply`: the open buffer, else one opened in the **background** via `addBuffer(buffer, false)` so the diff stays focused), `replaceText`s it (marks dirty), then `refreshOpenDiffs()` re-diffs. The toolbar's **Undo** (`undoLocal` → the buffer's `undo()`) and **Save** (`saveLocal` → `save(buffer)`) act on that buffer, so applies are revertible and persisted explicitly. **Apply-all** confirms first (it replaces the whole file). (`setEditable` rebuilds the view so the arrows + Undo/Save/Apply-all toolbar buttons appear, since it runs after construction.) **One new dependency + its moditect entry; no `module-info` opens / Settings / schema change.** *Deferred: a **computed** 3-way merge — fetch base/ours/theirs (the conflicted index stages `:1:`/`:2:`/`:3:` via `GitService.show`, or `git merge-base` + blobs outside a conflict) and run a diff3 engine that auto-resolves non-conflicting hunks and surfaces only true conflicts, independent of the user's `conflictStyle` (the base **column** itself already ships — see `MergeViewerPane`/`ConflictParser` — but it's only populated for `diff3`/`zdiff3` markers); in-diff editing, gutter-arrow stage/revert hunks, the SDD's standalone Diff Model persistence, multi-file `.patch` tabs (one tab per file section).*
- `process/` + `mermaid/` — **Mermaid diagram support** (on by default — inert until the `mmdc` CLI is detected — gated by `Settings.mermaidSupport`). The generic subprocess runner `ProcessRunner` lives in **`com.editora.process`** (moved out of `git/` so Git and Mermaid share it; `GitService` passes `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` through the new `run(dir,timeout,cmd,extraEnv)` overload, and `LC_ALL=C` is always set). **GUI-launch PATH fix (important):** a Finder-launched `.app` (or a `.desktop`) inherits a stripped `PATH` (`/usr/bin:/bin:…`) without Homebrew/npm/Node dirs, so `mmdc`/`npx`/`maid` (and a Homebrew `git`) wouldn't be found — `ProcessRunner` builds an **augmented PATH** = the inherited PATH **+ the user's login-shell PATH + the usual install dirs**, then rewrites a bare command name to its absolute path against it before launching (Java's Unix `ProcessBuilder` resolves the executable against the JVM's own stripped PATH, not the child env, so both steps are needed). The **login-shell PATH** (`ProcessRunner.loginShellPath()`) is the crucial part for version managers: it runs the user's `$SHELL -l -i -c 'printf …$PATH…'` **once** (stdin `/dev/null`, stderr discarded, 5 s timeout, markers fence the PATH off from any rc banner — the pure marker parse `extractMarked` is unit-tested; the VS Code `resolveShellEnv` approach) and folds its entries in. This recovers bin dirs that are **version-specific and so can't be hardcoded** — e.g. **nvm**'s `~/.nvm/versions/node/<ver>/bin` (where npm-global servers like `typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`yaml-language-server` live), fnm/asdf/volta, and a profile-set Homebrew. The hardcoded `EXTRA_PATH_DIRS` (`/opt/homebrew/bin`, `/usr/local/bin`, `/opt/local/bin`, `~/.local/bin`, `~/go/bin`, `~/.cargo/bin`, …) remain as a fallback. `augmentedPath()` is cached after the first call, and `LspManager`'s constructor **warms it off-thread** (the probe spawns a process) so neither detection nor the FX-thread `session.start()` blocks. Windows yields no login-shell PATH (no POSIX convention). A Settings absolute path still overrides. `com.editora.mermaid.Mermaid` is the static CLI facade over **mmdc** (mermaid-cli; renders/exports) and **maid** (`probelabs/maid`; a fast pure-JS linter): `renderPng(mmdc,source,dark)` (writes a temp `.mmd`, runs `mmdc -i -o -t default|dark -b transparent -s 2`, reads the **PNG** — *not* SVG, because JavaFX/JSVG can't apply mermaid's embedded `<style>` CSS or render its `<foreignObject>` HTML labels, so SVG comes out all-black/textless; mmdc rasterizes faithfully via headless Chromium), `exportTo(...)` (format by the chosen file extension — SVG/PNG/PDF, mmdc writes it directly), `validate(maid,source)` (runs `maid --format json`, parsed by the pure, unit-tested `MaidOutput` → `Diagnostic{line,column,severity,code,message}`; JSON with a text fallback). `MermaidService` (UI-owned, mirrors `GitService`: daemon executor + `Platform.runLater` + cached availability probe) backs the export command + the Settings detection status. Because `MarkdownRenderer` is synchronous/pure but mmdc is a multi-second subprocess, the editor-side **`MermaidImages`** static façade (like `PreviewImageLoader`: daemon pool + cache, configured via `configure(enabled,mmdcExe,maidExe,dark)` injected from `MermaidCoordinator.applySupport`) returns a placeholder `StackPane` immediately and fills it async — decoding mmdc's PNG with a JavaFX `Image` (logical width = pixels ÷ `RENDER_SCALE`) into an `ImageView` sized by a caller-supplied `DoubleUnaryOperator` (embedded Markdown blocks clamp to the content column; a standalone `.mmd` multiplies by the preview zoom so zoom actually resizes the image) — **cached by `sha-256(source+theme)`** so the debounced whole-document re-render never re-invokes mmdc for unchanged diagrams; on failure it shows `maid`'s precise line/column diagnostics (else mmdc's stderr) in a `.mermaid-error` label. (No JSVG/AWT in the Mermaid path — PNG decodes natively.) `MarkdownRenderer` special-cases a fenced block whose info string is `mermaid` (`isMermaidInfo`) → `MermaidImages.node(...)`, else the usual `codeBlock`. Standalone **`.mmd` files** (TextMate grammar `grammars/mermaid.tmLanguage.json` → `source.mermaid`, `LanguageRegistry` `mmd`→`mermaid`) get the same 3-mode preview: `EditorBuffer.isDiagram()`/`hasPreview()` generalize the markdown gating, and `scheduleRenderPreview` branches to render the whole buffer as one diagram. **Markwhen timelines** (`.mw`/`.markwhen` → language `markwhen`, scope `source.markwhen`, authored `grammars/markwhen.tmLanguage.json`) get the same 3-mode preview via the identical seam: the pure, JavaFX-free **`com.editora.markwhen`** package (`MwDate` — ISO + English month-name dates as half-open `[start,endExclusive)` intervals; sealed `MwNode` `Event`/`Group`; `Timeline`; tolerant line-based `MarkwhenParser.parse` — frontmatter `title:`/`#Tag: color`, `#`-header sections nested by level like Markdown, single/range events split on a whitespace-surrounded `-`/`/`, `//` comments — all unit-tested) parses the buffer **off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`** (a fourth `scheduleRenderPreview` branch beside `isMarkwhen()`, `previewGen` stale-guard) and **`editor/MarkwhenTimeline.build(model, zoomScale, viewportWidth)`** renders it on the FX thread as a **node-based `Pane`** (time axis + tick gridlines, one row per event/group, range→rounded `Region` bar / point→`Circle`, `#`-section bands, hover tooltips, `#tag` colors from the frontmatter else a fallback palette; capped at 500 events → placeholder), themed via `.markwhen-*` AtlantaFX looked-up colors in `app.css` (no per-theme override). Folding reuses the Markdown heading-level algorithm (`FoldRegions.markwhen`, `headingLevel` ignores space-less `#tag:` decls); `Commenter` `//`; `FileIcons` `table` glyph; horizontal zoom scales the axis width (re-render via `applyPreviewScale`). **A second renderer — `editor/MarkwhenCalendar` (month-grid: a vertical stack of Sun–Sat month cards, tag-colored event chips on each covered day, capped at 120 months) — is toggled per file** (`EditorBuffer.MarkwhenView` TIMELINE/CALENDAR, `toggleMarkwhenView`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.markwhenViews`; the render branch picks the renderer); both share `editor/MarkwhenPaint` (tag→color).
