The Markwhen preview right-click menu (and palette `markwhen.exportJson`/`markwhen.toggleView`) offers **Export to JSON** (`markwhen/MarkwhenJson.toJson` — a clean pretty-printed tree of title/tagColors/nested nodes, not `@markwhen/parser`'s schema) and **Switch to Calendar/Timeline View** instead of the PDF/Word/Print items. The preview's PDF/Word/Print exports are gated **off** for markwhen in v1 (`isMarkwhen()` guard in `exportPreviewPdf`/`printPreview` → `status.export.markwhenUnsupported`; docx/odt/html are already `isMarkdown()`-only) — a node-`snapshot`-to-PDF follow-up is deferred, along with relative/human-fuzzy dates, recurrence, times/timezones, lane-packing, and a markwhen CLI (none renders to an image like `mmdc`). Command `mermaid.export` (`FileChooser` SVG/PNG/PDF → `MermaidService.export`). Each tool is run as a **tokenized command** (`Mermaid.command(configured, default)`, whitespace-split) so a bare binary *or* an npx invocation works: defaults are `mmdc` (a binary; the user installs mermaid-cli) and **`npx -y @probelabs/maid`** (maid is normally run via npx, not a global bin — `MermaidService.DEFAULT_MMDC`/`DEFAULT_MAID`). maid emits its JSON report on stdout regardless of exit code, so `validate` always parses it (doesn't gate on success); the real shape is `{errors:[{line,column,message,severity,code,hint}], …}` — locked in by a `MaidOutputTest` case. Settings → **Mermaid** page: enable checkbox + `mmdc`/`maid` command fields (Browse; blank = the defaults above) + a live found/not-found status (`detect` counts any clean launch, not just exit 0). **`ui/MermaidCoordinator`** (a feature coordinator extracted from `MainController`, the `LogViewerCoordinator` pattern — owns the `MermaidService` + the detected-tool `Availability` + the apply/gating/export logic, reaching the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface; `MainController` keeps one-line delegations and a fake `Host` makes it unit-testable, see `MermaidCoordinatorFxTest`): `applySupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`, init + every settings/theme apply) configures the façade + service + re-renders open previews, then detects the tools and gates lint/autocomplete; the `export` command no-ops when off (`ifEnabled`) and `mermaid.*` is filtered from the palette. The mermaid reads other features need are exposed as coordinator methods: `mmdcCommandOrNull()` (PDF/print embedding), `effectiveAutocomplete()` (the completion config), `exportDiagram()` (PDF diagram export), and `service()` (the Settings → Mermaid detection-status row). **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (grammar rides the existing `opens com.editora.grammars`; mmdc/maid are external CLIs the user installs via npm). **Live linting**: `.mmd` buffers run **maid** debounced (~450 ms) while typing via `MermaidService.validate(source, cb)` (async, gen-guarded) injected into `EditorBuffer.setMermaidValidator`; `MermaidLintOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`) draws red wavy underlines at each diagnostic's `line/column/length` (visible paragraphs only, coalesced), and an `area` `MOUSE_MOVED` handler shows the maid message in a tooltip over a squiggle. Gated by `EditorBuffer.setMermaidLintEnabled` (controller sets it = mermaid on && maid detected, re-applied after the async `detect`). **Autocomplete**: `.mmd` buffers get Mermaid keyword completions (`completion/MermaidKeywords`, merged in `CompletionEngine.complete` when `snippetLang == "mermaid"`) + bundled `snippets/mermaid.json`, gated by `Settings.autocompleteMermaid` (Settings → Editor, default on; `view.toggleAutocompleteMermaid`) — **effective only** when the master autocomplete is on, Mermaid is enabled, and mmdc is detected (`MermaidCoordinator.effectiveAutocomplete()`; `EditorBuffer.updateCompletion` routes diagram buffers through this flag). `MaidOutput.Diagnostic` carries `length` for the underline span. *Deferred (per the SDD): a Markdown→HTML/PDF export pipeline (none exists to hook "render before export" into), a Mermaid LSP (no LSP layer exists), and block-at-caret export from Markdown.*
- `lsp/` — **Language Server Protocol** support (off by default, gated by `Settings.lspSupport`). **Servers: Java** (Eclipse **JDT LS**, `jdtls`), **TypeScript/JavaScript** (`typescript-language-server --stdio`, serving js/ts/jsx/tsx), **Python** (`pyright-langserver --stdio`), **XML** (`lemminx`, serving the `xml` language id — xml/xsd/xsl/svg/fxml/pom/…), **JSON** (`vscode-json-language-server --stdio`), **Bash/Shell** (`bash-language-server start`, serving the `shell` language id — sh/bash/zsh; its diagnostics come from `shellcheck` when that's on PATH), **YAML** (`yaml-language-server --stdio`), **Go** (`gopls`, root markers `go.mod`/`go.work`), **Rust** (`rust-analyzer`, root marker `Cargo.toml`), **PHP** (`phpactor language-server`, root marker `composer.json`), **Ruby** (`ruby-lsp`, root markers `Gemfile`/`.ruby-version`), **C/C++** (`clangd` — one server serving both the `c` and `cpp` language ids, root markers `compile_commands.json`/`CMakeLists.txt`/…), **HTML** (`vscode-html-language-server --stdio`), **CSS** (`vscode-css-language-server --stdio`), **Kotlin** (`kotlin-language-server`), **Lua** (`lua-language-server`), **Dockerfile** (`docker-langserver --stdio`), **SQL** (`sqls`), **Terraform** (`terraform-ls serve`, root markers `.terraform`/lock file), **TOML** (`taplo lsp stdio`), and **C#** (`csharp-ls`, root markers `global.json`/`.git`) — **twenty-one servers** total. Most already had highlighting + folding, so each was just a registry/Settings entry; the five with **no grammar** (PHP, Lua, Dockerfile, Terraform, TOML) each got a bundled `*.tmLanguage.json` (PHP `source.php` from VS Code MIT; Lua/Dockerfile/Terraform/TOML `source.lua`/`source.dockerfile`/`source.hcl.terraform`/`source.toml` from the shiki tm-grammars collection — see NOTICE) + `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter` entries, like the JS/TS case. **Dockerfile** is matched by **filename** (extension-less `Dockerfile`/`Containerfile`, or a `Dockerfile.<tag>` suffix) via a special case in both `LanguageRegistry.forFileName` and `GrammarRegistry.scopeForFileName`; TOML moved off the borrowed INI grammar onto its own `source.toml`. **Adding a server = one `ServerDef` in `LspServerRegistry` + its id in `MainController.LSP_SERVER_IDS` + the served language id(s) in `EditorBuffer.LSP_LANGUAGES` + a Settings command/enable pair** (the Settings → LSP page is **data-driven** over a `SettingsWindow.lspServerUis()` descriptor list, so a new server is one entry there too) — `LspManager.configure(enabled, Map<serverId,command>)` is map-based so it never needs a signature change. The registry is **server-centric**: `LspServerRegistry` lists each server with the language ids it serves + its root markers (Java: `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/…; TS: `tsconfig.json`/`jsconfig.json`/`package.json`/`.git`), so `LspManager` keys **one session per `(serverId, root)`** and js/ts/jsx/tsx in one project share a single `tsserver`. Each server has its own configurable command (`Settings.javaLspCommand`/`typescriptLspCommand`; blank ⇒ default) + its own cached availability probe; `MainController` detects each independently and gates each buffer by *its* server's availability and the file's language id (`EditorBuffer.getLanguage()`, which here doubles as the LSP languageId: `java`/`javascript`/`javascriptreact`/`typescript`/`typescriptreact`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`shell`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`c`/`cpp`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`). **JS/TS also get syntax highlighting** — bundled `typescript.tmLanguage.json` (`source.ts`) + `typescriptreact.tmLanguage.json` (`source.tsx`) grammars from VS Code (MIT, see NOTICE); `.ts/.mts/.cts/.js/.mjs/.cjs`→`source.ts`, `.tsx/.jsx`→`source.tsx` (the TS grammar tokenizes plain JS, so no separate JS grammar), with the extensions registered in `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter`. **Auto-imports**: accepting an LSP completion runs an optional `Completion.onAccept` hook (`CompletionMapper.map(items, onAcceptFor)`); for an item that `mayHaveAdditionalEdits` (carries resolve `data`), `MainController.autoImportAccept` → `LspManager.resolveCompletion` (`completionItem/resolve`) and applies the resolved `additionalTextEdits` (e.g. a TS `import` line) via `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits(List<editor/LspTextEdit>)` (offset-mapped, applied bottom-to-top; the `LspTextEdit` record keeps `editor` lsp4j-free). Uses **LSP4J** (`org.eclipse.lsp4j` + `.jsonrpc`, automatic modules → moditect-patched in the `dist` profile like tm4e/pdfbox; jsonrpc reuses the existing `gson`). `module-info` **`opens com.editora.lsp;`** (unqualified, **not** qualified-to-jsonrpc) because Gson reflectively reads our `@JsonNotification("language/status")` param DTO (`LanguageServerSession.LanguageStatus`) and, under `mvn javafx:run`, runs in the **unnamed** module — a qualified opens to `org.eclipse.lsp4j.jsonrpc` alone leaves it unable to set the DTO fields accessible. **`LanguageServerSession`** runs one external server process per workspace root over stdio: it launches via `ProcessBuilder` reusing `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`/`applyStandardEnv` (the GUI-launch PATH augmentation, so a Finder-launched `.app` finds `jdtls`), drives it with an LSP4J `Launcher` on a daemon executor, implements `LanguageClient` (receives `publishDiagnostics`/log/show-message), does `initialize`/`initialized` + client capabilities, full-text document sync (`didOpen`/`didChange`/`didSave`/`didClose`), the request subset (completion/hover/definition/references), **queues requests until initialize completes**, and `shutdown`+`exit` on dispose. **The server's stderr is drained on a daemon thread** (`LanguageServerSession.drainStderr`, capped, into the Debug Log so a failed launch surfaces *why* — missing JDK, lock, bad command) — it **must** be consumed: leaving it a PIPE lets a chatty server (jdtls logs heavily) fill the ~64 KB OS pipe buffer and block mid-startup (LSP traffic is on stdout). (The standalone DAP adapters still `Redirect.DISCARD` their stderr instead.) **Dispose kills the whole descendant process tree** via **`process/ProcessRegistry.killTree`**, not just the launcher: jdtls (and others) is a wrapper script (Homebrew `jdtls` → python → java), so destroying only the wrapper **orphans the real server JVM**, which keeps running and holds its Eclipse workspace `.lock` — the next session for the same root then can't acquire the lock and hangs (no diagnostics/completion). **Per-project jdtls workspace:** to avoid that lock contention up front, jdtls is launched with **`-data <configDir>/jdtls-workspaces/<sha256(root)>`** (`LspServerRegistry.withDataDir`/`workspaceDirName`, pure/unit-tested; base dir injected via `LspManager.setJdtlsWorkspaceBase` from `applyLspSupport`) so each root gets its own Eclipse workspace instead of the single shared default (which deadlocked when two roots — or a leaked run, or another editor — contended for it, leaving `initialize` unresolved → loading bar spinning forever + dead completion). The workspace persists across sessions (jdtls's index is reused); a user-supplied `-data` in the configured command is respected (`withDataDir` no-ops then). **`com.editora.process.ProcessRegistry`** is the central lifecycle owner for *every* spawned external server (LSP **and** DAP — `LanguageServerSession.start` and `DapClient.connectStdio`/`setAdapterProcess` call `ProcessRegistry.track(process)`): (1) **`killTree(process)`** destroys the descendant tree (children first so the wrapper can't reparent-orphan its child), then escalates to a **force-kill after a `GRACE_MS` grace period** if SIGTERM is ignored — **non-blocking** (a daemon scheduler), so it's safe on the FX thread during a window close; (2) a **JVM shutdown hook** (`installShutdownHook`, called from `App.main`) force-kills every tracked tree on exit — covering a normal quit *and* SIGTERM/`kill`/OS-quit/most crashes, the paths that bypass the window-close teardown and used to leak servers; (3) a small on-disk **ledger** (`<configDir>/spawned-servers.txt`, set via `setLedgerFile`) records each spawned root pid + start-time + executable, and **`reapOrphans()`** (called once from `App.start` *before* any window builds) kills any server **leaked by a previous run that died too hard for the hook** (SIGKILL / power loss). The pure `LedgerEntry` parse/format + `shouldReap(...)` decision (reap only when pid **and** start-instant **and** executable all match — so it can never kill an unrelated reused PID) are unit-tested (`ProcessRegistryTest`). `untrack` + an `onExit` self-clean keep the live set/ledger accurate; only long-lived servers are tracked (short-lived start-then-destroy probes aren't). Uses only `java.base` — no dependency / `module-info` change. **`LspManager`** is the UI-facing facade (mirrors `MermaidService`: one session per `(lang, root)`, cached async `detect()`, request `CompletableFuture`s marshaled to the FX thread via `Platform.runLater`, neutral `Target(file,line,char)` results, mapped-diagnostics callback, `shutdownAll`). Pure/unit-tested helpers: **`LspServerRegistry`** (language→spec + command tokenization; `java`→`jdtls`, root markers `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/…), **`RootResolver`** (active project → nearest build file → file's dir), **`LspPositions`** (offset↔LSP line/char), **`DiagnosticMapper`** (LSP `Diagnostic`→`editor/LspDiagnostic`), **`CompletionMapper`** (`CompletionItem`→`completion/Completion`; snippet-format items fall back to the label so `$0` placeholders aren't inserted). **Diagnostics UI** (`editor/`): `LspDiagnostic` (range+severity record) + `LspDiagnosticOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `MermaidLintOverlay`, multi-line/range-aware, severity colors, visible-paragraphs + coalesced, `CanvasGuards`). **Diagnostic stripes** (IntelliJ-style, fed by the same `setLspDiagnostics`, both gated on `lspActive`): the **minimap** edge stripes (`Minimap.setDiagnostics`/`setDiagnosticsEnabled` — errors-on-top; the LSP setters only repaint stripes over an *already-cached* snapshot and **never** force a `renderContent()`/`snapshot()`, since a synchronous snapshot during the editor's first layout blanks the surface until a relayout), plus an always-on thin **`editor/DiagnosticStripe`** docked over the vertical scrollbar that maps the whole document to its height by the editor's real content metrics (`totalHeightEstimate` ÷ paragraph count, read lazily at draw time — **no listener**, which would force eager re-computation and starve repaints) so marks sit at the actual on-screen line; mouse-transparent until it has marks, hover shows the message, click jumps via `EditorBuffer.jumpToLine`; releases its canvas to 1×1 when empty. `EditorBuffer` mirrors the mermaid hooks — `setLspActive`/`setLspDiagnostics`/`setLspChangeListener` (debounced `multiPlainChanges`→didChange)/`setLspCompletionProvider` + an `installLspHover` diagnostic tooltip — kept decoupled (`editor` imports nothing from `lsp`; `isLspLanguage()` checks a hardcoded set of the served languages, kept in sync with `LspServerRegistry`). `ui/ProblemsPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `SearchPanel`; id `problems`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.problems`/`M-8`) groups diagnostics **by programming language → file → diagnostic** (language via `LanguageRegistry.forFileName`, a friendly `.problem-lang-row` header). **The active file sorts to the top** (IDE convention): `ProblemsPanel.setActiveFile(canonicalPath)` — pushed on every tab switch via `LspCoordinator.setProblemsActiveFile` — orders the active file's language group first and, within it, the active file first, re-sorting the cached tree without needing fresh diagnostics (pure/unit-tested `ui/ActiveFileOrder`, shared with the TODO window; the caller passes the canonical path so it matches the LSP diagnostic keys). **`MainController`** owns the manager + an `lspProblems` map **scoped to open files** — a server publishes diagnostics project-wide (jdtls especially), so `onLspDiagnostics` drops any file without an open tab to keep the Problems window from filling with whole-workspace noise; the open-tab lookup (`tabForPath`) matches by **canonical (symlink-resolved) path** via `MainController.canonicalPath` (`Path.toRealPath`, falling back to `toAbsolutePath().normalize()`) — a server reports diagnostics under the file's *real* URI (e.g. `/private/tmp/…` for a `/tmp/…` symlink on macOS, or any symlinked project dir) while a buffer keeps the path as opened, so plain `normalize()` matching silently **dropped every diagnostic** (no squiggles, empty Problems) — the unit-tested fix; `applyLspSupport()`/`applyLspGating()`/`ifLsp()` mirror `applyMermaidSupport` (configure → async detect → per-buffer `syncBufferLsp` open/activate/close), run at init + every settings apply; lifecycle: open on `addBuffer`/save-as, didChange (debounced in the buffer), didSave from `writeBuffer`, didClose on tab removal, `shutdownAll` when disabled. Commands (all `ifLsp`-gated, palette-filtered when off): `lsp.gotoDefinition` (`M-.`), `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`, ≥2 results → the **References tool window**; a lone result jumps straight there), `lsp.gotoSymbol` (**Go to Symbol in Workspace** — palette-only), `lsp.hover` (`C-c h`, hover markdown via `MarkdownRenderer` in a tooltip), `lsp.restartServers`, `lsp.formatDocument` (whole-file `textDocument/formatting`, palette-only: `LspManager.formatDocument` → `LanguageServerSession.formatting` → `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits` (undoable); gated by `LspManager.supportsFormatting` reading the `documentFormattingProvider` capability; `FormattingOptions` from `Settings.tabSize` + `EditorBuffer.detectInsertSpaces`), `tool.problems` (`M-8`), `view.toggleLsp`. **The entire LSP integration lives in `ui/LspCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern). It owns: the nav/format flows (`gotoDefinition`/`findReferences`/`showHover`/`formatDocument` + the hover popup); diagnostics routing (the per-open-file `problems` map + the `ProblemsPanel` + the `onDiagnostics` callback — compact-source-noise filter + open-files scoping); and the **configure/detect/gating + per-buffer lifecycle** — `applySupport()` (mirrors `MermaidCoordinator`; sets the jdtls workspace base, `lspManager.configure(...)`, gates the Run affordance, then per-`SERVER_IDS` detect → `applyGating()`), the per-server `serverEnabled`/`serverCommand`/`setServer*` switches, `serverAvailable` (read by DAP's `debugEffectiveFor` via `lspCoordinator.isServerAvailable("java")`/`serverEnabled("java")`), `syncBuffer()` (open/activate/close + push trigger-chars/format/range-format/semantic flags), `updateStatusBar()` (the `LSP:` segment + Problems availability), `requestStructureSymbols()`, `requestSemanticTokens()`/`applySemanticHighlight()`, `onServerStatus()` (the ready event → refresh capabilities + pull diagnostics + structure), `restartServers()`, `notifyDocumentSaved()`, `wireBuffer()` (the addBuffer hook set: didChange/pull-diagnostics/semantic/completion/doc-resolver/range-formatter/nav-actions + `syncBuffer`), and the `lsp.toggleServer`/`lsp.setServerCommand` pickers. It reaches the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension (open-and-goto / active-editable / lsp-feature-enabled / set-loading-bar / buffer-for-path / set-status-bar-LSP / set-problems-available / set-structure-symbols / refresh-run-button / jdtls-workspace-base / lsp-project-root). The `lsp.*` commands + `buffer.setLspNavActions` delegate to it, and the MCP bridge reads `lspCoordinator.problems()`. The `LspManager` stays owned by `MainController` (Debug layers on the jdtls session, the MCP bridge reads its diagnostics) and is passed to the coordinator as a ctor arg; its `publishDiagnostics`/`status` callbacks route through thin `MainController.onLspDiagnostics`/`onLspServerStatus` method-ref delegates (to dodge an illegal forward reference at the manager's field initializer). `MainController` keeps `lspEnabled()` (used widely by Run/Debug gating), the `ifLsp`/`toggleLsp` command glue, the Problems `ToolWindow` (built with `lspCoordinator.problemsPanel()`), and `canonicalPath`/`tabForPath`. The first three are also prepended to the **editor right-click menu** while `EditorBuffer.isLspActive()` (gated to LSP-on + a managed buffer of a served language); the menu items move the caret to the click offset first so they target the right-clicked symbol (labels reuse the `command.lsp.*` titles — no new i18n keys). **Ctrl/Cmd-click go-to-definition:** the same `EditorBuffer` `MOUSE_PRESSED` filter that opens a Markdown link on Ctrl/Cmd-click also, in a code buffer with `isLspActive()`, moves the caret to the clicked symbol, focuses the area, and fires `lspGotoDefinitionAction` (deferred via `Platform.runLater` so focus/caret settle first) — the IDE go-to-definition gesture, reusing the existing `gotoDefinition` flow (no new command/i18n). It only consumes the click for a served buffer, so a non-LSP file's normal click (and the multi-caret gestures) are untouched. **Format Document** joins that menu only when the server advertises formatting (`EditorBuffer.setLspFormatAvailable`, pushed from `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event like `setLspTriggerChars`). **Tab line re-indent**: in a buffer whose server advertises **range** formatting (`documentRangeFormattingProvider` via `LspManager.supportsRangeFormatting`, pushed to `EditorBuffer.setLspRangeFormatAvailable` alongside the format flag at `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event), plain Tab re-indents the current line to the server's convention — **indentation only**, not a full line reformat. `EditorBuffer.tryLspReindentLine` (in the `addSnippetKeys` Tab branch, after snippet-prefix expansion and before `applySmartTab`) requests `textDocument/rangeFormatting` over the line via the injected `setLspRangeFormatter` (→ `LspManager.rangeFormatting` → `LanguageServerSession.rangeFormatting`), then the pure/unit-tested `editops/LineIndent.formattedIndent` computes the formatted line's leading whitespace and `applyLspLineIndent` applies only that (async, generation-guarded + line-unchanged check). It returns false (→ normal smart-Tab) for a selection, a blank line (formatters strip blank-line whitespace, so a fresh line keeps the local indent), non-LSP buffers, or servers without range formatting; completion-accept / snippet-tab still take Tab first. The status bar shows an **`LSP: <server>`** segment (`StatusBar.setLsp`, `MainController.updateLspStatusBar`) for managed files, clickable → Problems, plus an indeterminate **loading bar** while a server starts (`StatusBar.setLspLoading`) — kept determinate (a fixed value) when idle so its animation timeline can't keep pulsing the scene and starving repaints; flipped indeterminate only during the load. The bar is **cleared when the `initialize` handshake resolves** — `LanguageServerSession` emits a synthetic `onStatus("ServiceReady", null)` on success / `("Error", null)` on failure (null message ⇒ no echo write), which `onLspServerStatus` turns into `setLspLoading(false)`. This is **universal** across every server and a clean file that never publishes a diagnostic — earlier the bar only stopped on incoming diagnostics or jdtls's vendor-specific `language/status`, so a no-diagnostic file (or any non-jdtls server) left it spinning forever. lsp4j's "Unsupported notification method" log noise (JDT LS's `language/status` etc.) is quieted via `App`'s `org.eclipse.lsp4j` logger set to SEVERE. **LSP completion** is an async source merged into the existing `CompletionPopup` for code buffers (`EditorBuffer.requestLspCompletion`/`mergeCompletions`, generation-guarded; LSP items first, then local snippets). **Completion fires on the server's advertised trigger characters**, not just `.`/a word prefix: `LanguageServerSession.capabilities()` carries the `initialize` result, `LspManager.triggerCharacters(file)` (pure `triggerCharsOf(ServerCapabilities)`, unit-tested) reads `completionProvider.triggerCharacters`, and `MainController` pushes the set into `EditorBuffer.setLspTriggerChars` (in `syncBufferLsp` + refreshed on the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event, since capabilities are only known post-`initialize`); `EditorBuffer.endsWithLspTrigger` checks that set. So `<` in HTML, `:` in CSS, etc. pop the completion (the trigger was previously hardcoded to `.`, so HTML/CSS completion effectively never fired even though the server returns 100+ tag/attr items — confirmed by driving the real `vscode-html-language-server`). **Pull diagnostics** (LSP 3.17 `textDocument/diagnostic`): the client declares `DiagnosticCapabilities`, and for a server advertising a `diagnosticProvider` (vscode-html/css/json, …) `LspManager.pullDiagnostics(file)` requests diagnostics and routes the report through the **same** `onDiagnostics` path as pushed `publishDiagnostics` (`DiagnosticMapper.mapReport` maps a full report, returns null for an "unchanged" report — both unit-tested). No-op for push-only servers (jdtls/Pyright/tsserver have no `diagnosticProvider`). Pulls are debounced on the existing 300 ms didChange pulse (`EditorBuffer.setLspDiagnosticsRequester`, fired *separately* from `lspChangeListener` so a completion-keystroke flush doesn't trigger a pull) + once on save + once when the server reports ready (initial diagnostics). **Settings → LSP** page (enable checkbox + a server-command field **per server** (all twenty-one) with Browse + a live found/not-found status row each via `LspManager.detect(serverId, …)`; **data-driven** — the page, `load()`, `refreshLspStatus()`, and `updateLspRowsEnabled()` all loop over `lspServerUis()` descriptors keyed into `lspEnableChecks`/`lspCommandFields`/`lspStatusLabels` maps, so adding a server is one descriptor; `syncLspCheck` for the palette toggle). `Settings.lspSupport` + a per-server `…LspCommand` + `…LspEnabled` pair for each of the twenty-one server ids (`java`/`typescript`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`bash`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`clangd`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`; default on, only effective under the global enable; `MainController.serverEnabled` gates `syncBufferLsp` and `applyLspSupport` calls `LspManager.shutdownServer(serverId)` for a disabled server). The `configure(...)`/migration maps use `Map.ofEntries` (>10 servers exceed `Map.of`'s overloads). Schema 7→8→9→10→11→12→13 (additive-identity migrations). The Settings → LSP page's per-server **found/not-found** status is colored green/red (`settings-git-found`/`settings-git-missing`, like the Git page). Servers are **auto-detected, never bundled** (`jdtls`/`typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`lemminx`/`vscode-json-language-server`/`bash-language-server`/`yaml-language-server`/`gopls`/`rust-analyzer`/`phpactor`/`ruby-lsp`/`clangd`/`vscode-html-language-server`/`vscode-css-language-server`/`kotlin-language-server`/`lua-language-server`/`docker-langserver`/`sqls`/`terraform-ls`/`taplo`/`csharp-ls` on PATH; Settings override). **Document symbols / Structure outline**: `LanguageServerSession.documentSymbol(uri)` (`textDocument/documentSymbol`) + `LspManager.documentSymbols(file, cb)` (capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `documentSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`) map the response — modern hierarchical `DocumentSymbol` or legacy flat `SymbolInformation` — via `lsp/DocumentSymbolMapper` into the neutral, lsp4j-free `lsp/SymbolNode` tree (`kindName` lowercases the `SymbolKind`; `descendInto` keeps children **only for type-like containers** (class/interface/enum/struct/namespace/module/package/object); every callable (method/function/constructor) is a leaf, so a server reporting method-body internals as children — jdtls emits locals/lambdas/anonymous-class methods, which showed as "methods inside methods" — is flattened away. Nested functions in Python/JS therefore appear flat too). `MainController.requestStructureSymbols(buffer)` pushes it into `ui/StructurePanel.setLspSymbols(buffer, syms)` for the **active** buffer on tab switch, the debounced didChange pulse, and the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event; the panel renders an LSP-precise hierarchy with per-kind icons (`ui/StructureIcons`); method/function/constructor rows append the server's signature (`SymbolNode.detail`, e.g. `(String x) : void`) in a muted `.structure-detail` colour beside the name — or `()` when there's no detail **and** the label doesn't already carry its own param list (jdtls names methods like `setX(Foo)`, so `StructurePanel.StructureCell.signature` suppresses the redundant `()` to avoid `setX(Foo)()`); plus a **sort** selector (Position/Name/Kind) and a **kind filter**, falling back to the fold-region/TextMate heuristic for non-LSP/remote files, LSP-off, or an empty result (`setLspSymbols(buffer, null)`). Each row also shows its **leading doc comment** as a hover tooltip via the pure/unit-tested `ui/StructureDoc.commentAbove(lines, declLine)` (Javadoc/JSDoc/PHPDoc + plain `/* */` blocks, and `//`/`#`/`--` line-comment runs above the declaration, skipping intervening annotation/decorator lines, capped) — `StructurePanel.attachDocs` reads it from `buffer.getContent()` for both the LSP and heuristic outlines. **Go to Symbol in Workspace** (`workspace/symbol`): `LanguageServerSession.workspaceSymbol(query)` (client capability declared via `WorkspaceClientCapabilities.setSymbol`) + `LspManager.workspaceSymbols(anchorFile, query, cb)` (maps both the legacy flat `SymbolInformation` and modern `WorkspaceSymbol` shapes — the latter's URI-only range-less location → line 0 — into the neutral `WorkspaceSymbolMatch{name, container, kind, file, line, character}`; capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `workspaceSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`). `LspCoordinator.gotoSymbolInWorkspace` opens **`ui/WorkspaceSymbolPopup`** — an incremental in-scene overlay (modeled on `SearchInFilesPopup`: `OverlayHost`, `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` dismiss) whose query field re-runs `workspace/symbol` on the active file's server debounced (150 ms, stale-generation-guarded) as you type; `↑↓`/`C-n`/`C-p` move, Enter jumps to the symbol via `ops.openAndGoto` (cross-file), the query seeded from a single-line selection. Command `lsp.gotoSymbol` (palette-only, no keybinding); reports `status.lsp.workspaceSymbolsUnsupported` when the server lacks the capability. **References tool window**: `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`) now routes ≥2 results into **`ui/ReferencesPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `ProblemsPanel`; id `references`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::find`, `tool.references`, **registered default-hidden** — the coordinator `open`s it on demand) — a `TreeView` grouped **by file → reference** (`line:col preview`), Enter / double-click jumps (`ReferencesPanel.Actions` → `ops.openAndGoto`); a **lone** reference jumps straight there (no window). `LspCoordinator` owns the panel (`referencesPanel()`, like `problemsPanel()`) + `previewLine(target)` — the one-line preview comes from the file's **open buffer** when a tab holds it (cheap, FX-safe, reflects unsaved edits), else empty (closed files show just the line number — no disk I/O on the FX thread); the `references` window's availability is gated alongside Problems (`Ops.setProblemsAvailable`), opened via `Ops.openReferencesWindow`. *Deferred: previews for closed files (off-thread read), more languages, on-type formatting, rename/code actions/quick fixes, incremental sync, a TOML-driven server registry.*
- `run/` — **Run a file from a gutter ▶**, **gated by the LSP feature** (`EditorBuffer.setRunEnabled`, pushed = `Settings.lspSupport` from `MainController.applyLspSupport` on init + every settings apply; off ⇒ no gutter glyph / menu item / Run window). **Runnable files**: a **Java 25 compact source file** (JEP 512) — detected by the pure, unit-tested **`editor/CompactSource`** (a `.java` with a `void main(` at **brace depth 0** after blanking comments/string/char/text-block literals length-preservingly; `mainLine(source)` is the glyph line) — **any Python script** (`language == "python"`; the glyph sits on the `if __name__ == "__main__":` guard via `EditorBuffer.pythonRunLine`, else the first line) — **or a shell script** (`language == "shell"`, glyph on line 0/the shebang) **but only when the Bash LSP server is enabled** (`EditorBuffer.setShellRunEnabled`, pushed = `lspSupport && Settings.bashLspEnabled` from `applyLspSupport`/`addBuffer`; a per-buffer gate *separate* from `setRunEnabled` so Java/Python are unaffected — they need only the global LSP feature) — **or a GNU Makefile** (`language == "makefile"`, `EditorBuffer.isMakefile()`): unlike the single-entry script types, **every rule target gets its own gutter ▶** (the `.http` multi-glyph model), and clicking it runs `make -f <file> <target>` in the file's dir. The pure/unit-tested **`run/MakefileTargets.parse`** extracts each runnable target's name + 0-based line (skipping recipe lines, variable assignments `:=`/`?=`/…, directives, `%` pattern rules, `.PHONY`/dot targets, and `$var` names), stored as a line→name map that `recomputeRun` fills alongside the `.http` request-line set (both set `runnable=true` + `runLine=-1`); the generic **"Run File"** / `file.run` runs the **default goal** (bare `make`). `RunCoordinator.runMakeTarget(buffer, target)` saves first then streams via `RunService` (`-f <basename>` so a `build.mk`/`Makefile.inc` buffer runs *itself*, not the dir's default Makefile); `MainController` wires `setMakeRunHandler`. Rides the same Run-feature gate as Java/Python — **no `make`-on-PATH detection** (a missing `make` surfaces as a clear `onError` in the Run console). **Shebang language detection** (pure/unit-tested **`editor/Shebang`**): when a file's extension resolves to plaintext, `EditorBuffer.maybeApplyShebang` (run at the top of `recomputeRun`) promotes it to the language named by a first-line interpreter shebang — direct path (`#!/bin/bash`), `env` lookup (`#!/usr/bin/env python3`), or `env -S` with args — reducing the interpreter to its basename (version-stripped: `python3.12`→python), mapping it to a **representative extension**, and resolving language+grammar through the normal `forFileName("shebang.<ext>")` path so highlighting/folding/run/LSP all follow (shell for bash/zsh/sh/dash/ksh/…, python, javascript for node, typescript for deno/bun/ts-node/tsx, ruby, php, lua, groovy, powershell). A `java --source N` shebang → Java compact source: `getShebangJavaSource()` widens `recomputeRun`'s compact-source branch (via `CompactSource.hasTopLevelMain`, no `.java` needed) and feeds `RunCoordinator.buildRunCommand` a `java --source N <file>` argv (an extensionless file needs the flag). It never overrides a real extension or the user's status-bar language pick (`setLanguageOverride` sets a `languageUserOverride` guard). *(jdtls keys off `.java`, so an extensionless Java shebang file gets highlighting/run but likely no jdtls LSP; python/shell LSP work since the languageId is sent explicitly. The tab file-icon stays generic — it's filename-based.)* `EditorBuffer.recomputeRun` caches `runnable`/`runLine` (recomputed on load, Save-As, and the debounced 150 ms edit pulse; skipped for large files), fires `onRunnableChanged`, and exposes `isRunnable()`/`isPython()`/`isShell()` + `setRunHandler` (→ controller `runActiveFile`). **Gutter affordance**: `FoldManager.setRunHooks(enabled, isRunLine, onRun)` reserves a fixed `RUN_SLOT_WIDTH` slot **just left of the line number, only while runnable** (so other files' gutters are unaffected and the glyph never shifts text), drawing a clickable green play glyph (`FoldManager.runGlyph()`, `.run-marker`, right-aligned) on the entry line; the same glyph is the **right-click "Run File"** item. **`run/RunService.run(file, argv, listener)`** streams a launched program — `[java, <file>]` (JDK source-file launcher; needs JDK 25 on PATH, no `--enable-preview` since JEP 512 is final in 25), `[python3, <file>]`, or `[bash, <file>]` (the controller picks by `isPython()`/`isShell()`, else java) — via `ProcessBuilder` reusing `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`/`applyStandardEnv`, two daemon reader threads posting stdout/stderr to the FX thread (generation-guarded), `stop()` kills it; **`sendInput(line)`** writes one line to the process's stdin off-thread (so `IO.readln`-style console programs work) and **`detectJavaMajor(cb)`** probes `java -version` once (cached; the pure `javaMajorOf` parse handles the legacy `1.8` scheme — tested) so `runActiveFile` can **preflight** a java run and report a clear "needs JDK 25 — found Java N" instead of a cryptic launcher error. **Program arguments**: per-file args persist in `WorkspaceState.programArgs` (path → raw string; additive field), tokenized by the pure/unit-tested **`run/ProgramArgs.tokenize`** (quote-aware) and appended to the run argv; **the same stored args feed debug launches** (`DapManager.setProgramArgs` before `startLaunch` — sticky across `restart()`; `LaunchConfig.launch` already took java args, `program(...)` gained an args overload for debugpy/js-debug). Commands `file.runWithArgs` (prompt pre-filled via `promptText`, saved per file) and `run.rerun` (re-runs the last file+argv). **Clickable stack traces**: the pure/unit-tested **`run/StackTraceLinks.parse(line)`** recognizes Java (`(File.java:12)`), Python (`File "/path", line N`), and Node (`/path/x.js:12:5`) frames; double-clicking such a console line (the shared `RunPanel.installLinkClicks`, also installed on the Debug console) resolves the file (absolute path → direct; bare Java name → open tabs → the run file's dir → the project root) and jumps via `openAndGoto`. **jdtls noise filter**: for a compact buffer (`language==java && isRunnable()`), `onLspDiagnostics` drops implicit-class complaints from a server whose compliance predates JDK 25 (pure `MainController.isCompactSourceNoise`, tested) while real errors still surface. Bundled `snippets/java.json` gained `cmain` (compact main skeleton) + `ioprintln`/`ioreadln` (JEP 512 final dropped the implicit static IO import, so bodies use `IO.println`). **`ui/RunPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`; tool id `run`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.run`/`M-9`, `Icons.run()`) is a read-only monospace console (output capped) with Stop/Clear + a run-state header. The window wiring lives in **`ui/RunCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `RunService` + the `RunPanel`, the `runActiveFile`/`rerunLast`/`launchRun`/`buildRunCommand`/`stopRun` flow + the `lastRun` file/argv, reaching the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for open-tool-window / save-buffer / program-args get+set / stack-trace-link jump): `runActiveFile` saves first (dirty → save; untitled → Save-As), opens the Run window, then streams. `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `runCoordinator.panel()`), `updateRunButton` (gates the Run stripe on `isRunnable()`), the `programArgsFor` helper (shared with debug launches), and the shared `openRunLink` stack-trace resolver (which reuses `runCoordinator.lastRunDir()`); `buffer.setRunHandler` and the `file.run`/`run.*` commands delegate to the coordinator. Commands `file.run` (`C-c r`), `run.stop`, `run.clear` (`RunPanel.clearConsole`), `tool.run` (`M-9`) — palette-discoverable, localized in all six catalogs. **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (`com.editora.run` is internal to the module). *Deferred: running regular (non-compact) Java / other languages, a configurable run command per language, run configurations.*
- `http/` — **HTTP Client for `.http`/`.rest` files** (on by default, gated by `Settings.httpClientSupport`). Runs requests with the **built-in JDK `java.net.http.HttpClient`** (no external tool — `ijhttp` was tried first but it's a CI test-runner: slow JVM startup + a progress report instead of the response body). **`http/HttpFile`** (pure, unit-tested) parses a file into `Request{startLine,endLine,method,url,name,block}` (requests split on `###`) and one request's `block` into `Parsed{method,url,List<String[]> headers,body}` (`parseRequest`; merges indented URL-continuation lines, stops the body at a `>`/`<>` response-handler line); `requestIndexAt(text,line)` maps a clicked line; `fileVariablePairs(text)` returns the `@name = value` declarations. **`http/HttpEnv`** (pure) reads environment names + one environment's variable map from `http-client.env.json`. **`http/HttpVars`** (pure, unit-tested) substitutes `{{name}}` from a resolved map + dynamic built-ins (`{{$uuid}}`/`{{$timestamp}}`/`{{$randomInt}}`/`{{$isoTimestamp}}`); `resolve(env, fileVars, clock)` layers the file's `@vars` over the env vars (each resolved against the accumulating map). **`http/HttpClientService`** (UI façade, daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) executes a `Parsed` request via the shared `HttpClient` (`run`, and `runAll` for the whole file) — substitutes url/headers/body, skips JDK-restricted headers, times it, returns an **`HttpResult`** (status/headers/body/contentType/elapsed/size/error). **`http/HttpResponseFormat`** (pure, unit-tested) renders a readable report: status line + headers + blank + body (**pretty-printed JSON** by content type) + a `status · ms · size` footer. **Gutter ▶ per request**: `.http` reuses the run-slot — `FoldManager.setRunHooks`'s `onRun` was generalized from `Runnable` to `IntConsumer onRunLine` (the clicked line); `EditorBuffer.recomputeRun` marks **every** request start line runnable for an http buffer (`isHttpFile()` + `setHttpEnabled`, a gate *separate* from the LSP-gated `setRunEnabled`), and `onRunGlyph(line)` dispatches to the injected `httpRunHandler` (→ `HttpClientCoordinator.runRequest`). Syntax highlighting via a bundled authored `grammars/http.tmLanguage.json` (`source.http`, ext `http`/`rest`; registered in `GrammarRegistry` `scopeToResource` **and** `mapExtensions` — both needed; plus `LanguageRegistry`/`Commenter` `#` entries). **`ui/HttpClientPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`; id `http`, **`Side.RIGHT`**, `tool.http`/`M-0`, `Icons.httpClient()`) shows the rendered response in a read-only monospace area with an **environment `ComboBox`** (names from `HttpEnv`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.httpEnvironment`), **Save response** (FileChooser), and Clear. **Auto-show for `.http` buffers:** `MainController.applyHttpAutoToolWindow(buffer, httpActive)` (from `updateRunButton`, run on every tab switch) auto-opens the HTTP window when the active buffer is a `.http` file (feature on) and auto-hides it otherwise — `setAvailable(false)` already closes it on leave, and showing it **displaces then restores** any other right-side window (`openRightWindowExcept` + the `httpDisplacedRight` field). A **manual** close is remembered per buffer in `httpUserClosed` (a weak-keyed `Set<EditorBuffer>`) so it isn't re-shown for that file until the user reopens it (a manual open / running a request clears it); an *automatic* close on leaving isn't remembered, so returning re-shows it. User-vs-auto is detected via `ToolWindowManager.setStateListener((tw,opened)->…)` (fired from `open`/`close`), guarded by the `httpAutoMutating` flag the controller wraps around its own programmatic open/close. **`ui/HttpClientCoordinator`** (extracted from `MainController` — the shared-`CoordinatorHost` pattern plus a small `WindowOps` extension for the tool-window/tab/run-gating; `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` registration): `runRequest(buffer,line)` parses the request, builds the variable map (`httpVariables`: the selected env's public+private env-file vars overlaid with the file's `@vars`), runs it off-thread, renders the result into the panel; `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply) pushes `setHttpEnabled(on)` to each buffer + re-gates the tool window (no external detection); the commands no-op when off (`ifHttp`) and `http.*`/`tool.http` are filtered from the palette. Commands `http.runRequest` (run the request at the caret), `http.runFile` (all requests sequentially), `http.selectEnvironment`, `tool.http` (`M-0`). `Settings.httpClientSupport` (Settings → **HTTP Client**, just an enable checkbox; schema 18→19 additive-identity). **`module-info` `requires java.net.http`** — no new Maven dependency (env JSON uses the existing Jackson; the grammar rides `opens com.editora.grammars`). *Deferred: response-handler JS scripts (`> {% %}`) + cross-request captured variables (a request needing an earlier one's token can't run in isolation), request history, multipart/file bodies, a form/structured response viewer.*
- `web/` — **HTML Live Preview** (on by default, gated by `Settings.htmlPreviewSupport`). A floating "open in browser" globe overlaid top-right of any `.html`/`.htm`/`.xhtml` editor (mirroring the Markdown preview toggle) opens the current file in a **detected desktop browser** over a tiny embedded HTTP server, with **live-as-you-type reload**. **`web/LivePreviewServer`** wraps one JDK `com.sun.net.httpserver.HttpServer` bound to `127.0.0.1:0` (**loopback only**, never the LAN). `setPreview(file, Supplier<String> liveText)` makes the file's parent dir the document root; the previewed file is served from the buffer's **live in-memory text** (so unsaved edits show), assets (CSS/JS/images) from disk; a `/__editora_livereload` **long-poll** endpoint holds the request until `bumpVersion()` advances a `volatile long` (or a ~25 s timeout), and a small **injected `<script>`** (spliced before `</body>`, appended if none) reloads the page on a `200`. Pure/unit-tested helpers: `injectReloadScript`, `contentType` (extension→MIME), `safeResolve` (path-traversal guard rejecting escapes outside the doc root). A cached daemon thread pool backs it so held polls don't starve serving. **`web/Browsers`** (pure/unit-tested) detects installed browsers per-OS — macOS app bundles (`Safari.app` always; `Google Chrome.app`/`Firefox.app`/`Microsoft Edge.app` in `/Applications` + `~/Applications`, launched `open -a`), Linux PATH binaries (via `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`, launched `[bin, url]`), Windows Program Files exes (`cmd /c start`) — plus a **System Default** entry routed through `HostServices.showDocument`; the OS + filesystem/PATH probes are injected so detection + `launchArgv` are testable. **`web/HtmlPreviewService`** (UI-owned, the `MermaidService` idiom: single daemon executor + `Platform.runLater` + cached `detectBrowsers`) owns the one server per window; `preview(file, liveText, browser, cb)` (re)binds the doc root, launches the browser **detached** (fire-and-forget, so a foreground browser process can't stall the executor) or via the system opener, and posts a `Result`; `notifyChanged()` → `bumpVersion()`; `stopServer()` (feature disabled) vs `shutdown()` (window close). **`EditorBuffer`** (editor pkg, no `ui` dep): `isHtml()`, an injected `setHtmlPreviewControl(Node)` overlaid via the same code-pane top-right anchoring as the Markdown toggle (`attachControlToCodePane` generalized to place either the markdown `viewModeControl` *or* the `htmlPreviewControl` — mutually exclusive, a buffer is one or the other), and `setHtmlPreviewDirtyListener` fired from the **existing debounced** `multiPlainChanges` 250 ms pulse while `isHtml()` (no new per-keystroke work). **`ui/HtmlPreviewToggle`** (a `Button`, `Icons.htmlPreview()` globe, `.html-preview-toggle`) drops a `ContextMenu` of detected browsers (+ System Default) on click, **each menu item with its own recognizable glyph** (`HtmlPreviewToggle.iconFor(id)` → `Icons.browserSafari/Chrome/Firefox/Edge` — a Material compass for Safari + the Simple-Icons monochrome single-path logos for the rest; System Default / unknown falls back to the globe; Simple Icons is CC0, attributed in NOTICE). **`ui/HtmlPreviewCoordinator`** (a feature coordinator extracted from `MainController`, the `LogViewerCoordinator` pattern — owns the `HtmlPreviewService` + the detected-browser list + the browser picker, and reaches the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface; `MainController` supplies an anonymous `Host` adapter and keeps one-line delegations, and a fake `Host` makes it unit-testable — see `HtmlPreviewCoordinatorFxTest`): `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirrors `applyMermaidSupport`) (un)attaches the globe on local HTML buffers + async-detects browsers, or `stopServer()`s when off; `ensureControl` gates on `isEnabled() && isHtml() && host.isLocalBuffer` (remote SFTP excluded — the server reads sibling assets from disk); `previewActive` requires a saved file (so assets resolve), remembers the last-used browser in `Settings.htmlPreviewBrowser`; `onBufferEdited` reloads the served file on the debounced edit pulse; the `open`/`openIn` commands no-op when off (`ifEnabled`) and `htmlPreview.*` is palette-filtered. Commands (palette-only, no keymap binding — like preview/print): `htmlPreview.open` (last-used/default browser), `htmlPreview.openIn` (`QuickOpen` browser picker), `view.toggleHtmlPreview` (master toggle → `SettingsWindow.syncHtmlPreviewCheck`). `Settings.htmlPreviewSupport`/`htmlPreviewBrowser` (Settings → **HTML Preview**, enable checkbox; schema 24→25 additive-identity). **`module-info` `requires jdk.httpserver`** — **no new Maven dependency, no moditect** (a JDK module jlink bundles automatically); no `opens` (the last-used-browser is a plain `Settings` string). *Deferred: in-app WebView render (Editora ships no `javafx.web`; external browsers are the explicit design), remote (SFTP) HTML preview, multi-file concurrent previews (v1 serves one active file + its dir), a configurable server port, project-root document root.*
- `dap/` — **Multi-language debugging (Debug Adapter Protocol)** for **Java**, **Python**, and **JavaScript (Node)**, off by default (gated by `Settings.debugSupport`). Three transports, abstracted in `dap/DapClient`: **Java** is **layered on the jdtls LSP session** (not a standalone server) — jdtls is started with the Microsoft **java-debug** plugin jar in `initialize.initializationOptions.bundles`, which registers `vscode.java.*` debug commands; at debug time `LspManager.executeCommand(file, "vscode.java.startDebugSession")` returns a **TCP port** and `DapClient.connect(port, "java")` opens a socket. **Python** is **debugpy over stdio** — `DapManager` spawns `<python> -m debugpy.adapter` and `DapClient.connectStdio(proc, "python")` wires DAP to the process's stdin/stdout. **JavaScript** is **vscode-js-debug over a socket** — `DapManager` allocates a free port, spawns `node <dapDebugServer.js> <port>`, and `DapClient.connect(port, "pwa-node")` connects. All speak DAP via **`org.eclipse.lsp4j.debug`** (`DSPLauncher`). The standalone adapters' stderr is `Redirect.DISCARD`ed (undrained PIPE deadlocks, like the LSP servers), and `DapClient.dispose()` kills the adapter subprocess **tree** (descendants first, then root) so a wrapper script can't orphan the real adapter. **`dap/DapServerRegistry`** (pure, unit-tested) is the language→adapter spec: `java`→`Kind.JDTLS`, `python`→`Kind.STDIO` (launch `type="python"`, default interpreter `python3`, adapter args `-m debugpy.adapter`), `javascript`→`Kind.SOCKET` (launch `type="pwa-node"`, interpreter `node`); `languageIdsForDebug()`={java,python,javascript} gates the breakpoint gutter + debug commands; `interpreterArgv(lang, command)` tokenizes the configured interpreter (blank ⇒ default). The **LSP bridge** (`lsp/`, java only): `LanguageServerSession` gained an optional `initializationOptions` (jdtls gets `{"bundles":[<jar>]}` only when debugging is on) + `executeCommand`; `LspManager` gained `setDebugBundles`/`executeCommand`/`restartServer("java")` — toggling debug **restarts jdtls** so it reloads with the bundle. **`dap/DebugAdapterLocator`** (pure, unit-tested) finds each adapter: `locate(...)` the java-debug jar (`com.microsoft.java.debug.plugin-*.jar` from a configured path / VS Code `vscjava.vscode-java-debug-*` / mason / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/java/`, newest wins); `locateJsDebugServer(...)` the newest `dapDebugServer.js` (config path / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/javascript/` / mason `js-debug-adapter` / VS Code `ms-vscode.js-debug-*`, by an embedded path version); `locateDebugpy(...)` a `PYTHONPATH` dir containing a `debugpy` package (config path / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/python/`, empty ⇒ rely on the interpreter importing debugpy). **`dap/DapClient`** (mirrors `LanguageServerSession`) runs the DAP handshake (`initialize` with the per-transport `adapterId` → on the `initialized` event fire `setBreakpoints`/`setExceptionBreakpoints`/`configurationDone` **without `.join()`** — that callback runs on the reader thread, so blocking deadlocks), `launch`/`attach`, and the control + inspection requests; events arrive on the launcher thread and a `Host` (DapManager) marshals to FX. **`dap/DapManager`** (UI facade, mirrors `LspManager`+`RunService`) owns the **single** session and dispatches `startLaunch(file, language, picker)`: `java` → the jdtls flow (`resolveMainClass` → pick → `resolveClasspath` → `resolveJavaExecutable` → `startDebugSession` → connect → `launch`, with a `compileAndLaunch` javac fallback for loose files); `python`/`javascript` → `startProgram` (snapshot breakpoints on FX, then off-thread spawn the adapter + connect + `launch`). `configure(enabled, javaPluginPath, pythonEnabled, pythonCommand, jsEnabled, jsPath)` resolves all three adapter locations synchronously; `detectPython`/`detectJs` probe `python -c "import debugpy"` / `node --version` off-thread and cache `isLanguageAvailable(lang)`. It exposes neutral records (`dap/DapModels`) so `ui`/`editor` never import lsp4j.debug; jdtls's untyped `executeCommand` results (gson `JsonElement`s) are parsed with gson (`module-info` `requires com.google.gson` + `opens com.editora.dap`). **`dap/LaunchConfig`** (pure, unit-tested) shapes the DAP arg maps: `launch` (java mainClass+classpath), `attach` (java JVM host:port — **attach stays Java-only**), and `program(type, program, cwd, runtimeExecutable, stopOnEntry)` for python/js (the interpreter goes under `python` for python, `runtimeExecutable` for node). **Breakpoints** (`config/Breakpoint` + per-project `config/BreakpointStore` in `breakpoints.json`, `ConfigSchema.BREAKPOINTS`; `editor/BreakpointManager` mirrors `BookmarkManager`, `shift`/`reanchor` pure + unit-tested) show in a **leftmost gutter strip** (`FoldManager.setBreakpointHooks` reserves `BREAKPOINT_SLOT_WIDTH` only while debug is on **and the buffer's language is debuggable** — java/python/javascript, via `DebugCoordinator.isDebuggableBuffer`; clicking toggles a bp + consumes so it never collides with the bookmark gutter click; red dot `.breakpoint-marker`, amber/blue/hollow for conditional/logpoint/disabled). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the bookmark API + a **current-execution-line** (`setExecutionLine`/`clearExecutionLine`, `.exec-line`). **`ui/DebugPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`, id `debug`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.debug`/`M-g d`, `Icons.debug()`) is **IntelliJ-styled**: an icon-only grouped toolbar (resume/pause/stop/restart | step over/into/out/run-to-cursor, full titles in tooltips; the state + session file right-aligned), a **thread `ComboBox`** over the call-stack `ListView` (rich `name:line, File` `TextFlow` cells), a lazy variables `TreeView` with **type-colored values** (`record VarRow(name,value,type,ref,parentRef,Kind {SCOPE,VARIABLE,WATCH,ADD_WATCH})`; the pure, unit-tested **`ui/DebugValues`** classifies a rendered value STRING/NUMBER/BOOLEAN/NULL/OTHER → `.debug-val-*` CSS), and an always-visible console with an evaluate REPL. **Watches** are merged into the variables tree IntelliJ-style: a fixed top "Watches" node above the scopes + a trailing "+ Add watch…" row; add/edit/remove via the tree context menu or double-click, prompting through the injected `OverlayInput.Prompt` (`DebugPanel.setPrompt`); each watch evaluates per stop/frame-select with context `"watch"` via `DapClient.evaluateFull` → `DapModels.EvalResult(result, variablesReference, type)` (expandable when structured); the expression list persists in **`WorkspaceState.debugWatches`** (additive field; restored at startup + on project switch, saved via `setOnWatchesChanged`). **Set Value**: context-menu "Set Value…" / F2 / double-click on a leaf variable row → prompt pre-filled with the current value → `DapManager.setVariable` on the row's `parentRef`, updating the row in place + re-evaluating watches. **The whole DAP integration lives in `ui/DebugCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `DebugPanel`, breakpoint persistence + gutter gating, the DAP event sink (`dapListener`) + panel actions (`debugActions`), the inline-values/hover/execution-line editor surfaces (`applyInlineValues`/`highlightFrame`), the start/attach/step/run-to-cursor/jump flows, `wireBuffer` (the per-buffer breakpoint-gutter + change/hover hooks), and the `debug.toggleAdapter`/`debug.setAdapterPath` pickers; reaches the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for the Debug tool-window open/toggle/availability, the status-bar debug segment + loading bar, save-buffer, program-args (shared with Run), the stack-trace-link jump, open-path, buffer-for-path, the debug-watches workspace state, and the `breakpoints.json` map). The **`DapManager` stays a `MainController` field** (built on `lspManager`; `SettingsWindow` + window-dispose reach it) and is passed to the coordinator — mirroring the `lspManager`/`LspCoordinator` split; since Java debugging layers on the jdtls session, the coordinator also takes the `lspManager` + `LspCoordinator` (its `debugEffectiveFor("java")` reads `lspCoordinator.serverEnabled("java")`/`isServerAvailable("java")`; `applySupport` pushes the java-debug bundle + re-gates via `lspCoordinator.applyGating()`). `MainController` keeps the Debug `ToolWindow` (built with `debugCoordinator.panel()`), `isLocalBuffer`, the shared `programArgsFor`/`openRunLink`/`save` helpers, and the `debug.*` command registrations (delegating to the coordinator). **`DebugCoordinator`**: `applySupport()` configures all three adapters, pushes the java bundle into LSP (restart jdtls when changed), async-detects python/js (re-gating on each result), gates each buffer's breakpoint gutter via `debugSupportEnabled() && isDebuggableBuffer(b)`, and `setAvailable`s the Debug window; `debugEffectiveFor(language)` gates start (java = `lspSupport && javaLspEnabled && jdtls + plugin found`; python = `pythonDebugEnabled && debugpy detected`; js = `jsDebugEnabled && js-debug + node detected`); `debugStart()` reads the active buffer's language and dispatches; `ifDebug(...)` no-ops the commands when off (palette-filtered); persist/restore breakpoints on save/open. **Pause** (`DapClient.pause` → the `stopped` event flows through the normal path; enabled only while RUNNING) and **Run to Cursor** (`DapManager.runToCursor`: the pure, unit-tested `withTempLine` merges a temporary breakpoint into the file's set → `sendSetBreakpoints` → resume; the temp set is re-sent clean on the next stop/termination) complement the step commands. **Jump to Line** (the IntelliJ plugin's move-the-execution-pointer): DAP `gotoTargets`/`goto`, **capability-gated** via the stored `initialize` `Capabilities` (`DapClient.supportsGotoTargets`) — debugpy supports it, java-debug/js-debug don't (the command reports `status.debug.jumpUnsupported`); `DapManager.jumpToLine` teleports the suspended thread to the caret line *without executing* the code in between, and the adapter's `stopped(reason=goto)` refreshes everything. **Editor surfaces while suspended** (IntelliJ's inline values + value popup): on each stop/frame-select the controller fetches the selected frame's first non-expensive scope (capped at `MAX_INLINE_VALUES`) and pushes a name→value map to the frame's file buffer — **`editor/InlineValuesOverlay`** (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `WhitespaceOverlay`: visible paragraphs only, coalesced per pulse, 1×1 when inactive) paints grey-italic `name: value` annotations after each visible line that mentions a frame variable (pure, unit-tested **`editor/DebugIdentifiers.matchesIn`**); hovering an identifier evaluates it with DAP context `"hover"` (`DebugIdentifiers.wordAt` → the injected `EditorBuffer.setDebugHoverEvaluator` → `DapManager.evaluateHover`, which delivers null on failure so non-variables show nothing) in a `.debug-value-tooltip`; both are gated by `setDebugHoverActive`/`setInlineValues(null)` flipped on suspend/resume, so there is zero editor hot-path cost outside a paused session. Commands (all `ifDebug`-gated): `debug.start` (`C-c C-d d`, = continue when suspended) / `debug.continue`/`stepOver`/`stepInto`/`stepOut` / `debug.pause` (`C-c C-d p`) / `debug.runToCursor` (`C-c C-d u`) / `debug.jumpToLine` (`C-c C-d j`) / `debug.stop` / `debug.restart` / `debug.attach` (Java only) / `debug.toggleBreakpoint` (`C-c C-b`) / `debug.editBreakpoint` / `debug.toggleExceptionBreakpoints` / `tool.debug` (`M-g d`). The panel's data-inspection actions are also palette commands: `debug.evaluate` (open the Debug console + focus the eval field via `DebugPanel.focusEvaluate`), `debug.addWatch` (`DebugPanel.addWatch`), `debug.setValue` (`DebugPanel.setSelectedValue`). Settings → **Debugging** page is **data-driven** (`SettingsWindow.debugAdapterUis()`, mirroring the LSP page): a master enable + a per-language row group (Java/Python/JavaScript) — Python/JS each an enable checkbox + command/path field, Java a plugin-path field (no enable — gated by the Java LSP server) — each with a live green/red found status (`refreshDebugStatus` → the locators + `dapManager.detectPython/detectJs` probes). `Settings.debugSupport`/`javaDebugPluginPath`/`pythonDebugEnabled`/`pythonDebugCommand`/`jsDebugEnabled`/`jsDebugPath` (schema 15→16 additive-identity). **Adapter acquisition**: never bundled — `scripts/install-java-debug.sh` (java-debug jar from Open VSX), `scripts/install-debugpy.sh` (`pip install --target …/plugins/dap/python debugpy`), `scripts/install-js-debug.sh` (vscode-js-debug release → `…/plugins/dap/javascript/js-debug/src/dapDebugServer.js`); all honor `EDITORA_CONFIG_DIR` for `--dev`. **Dependency**: `org.eclipse.lsp4j.debug` (same version as lsp4j; moditect-patched + signed-jar-unsigned in `dist`); **no new dependency / `module-info` change** for python/js (debugpy/js-debug are external, user-installed, driven over stdio/socket; node/python come from the augmented PATH). *Deferred: browser/Chrome JS debugging, TypeScript source-map debugging, Python/JS attach (remote), more languages (Go delve, Ruby) via the registry, data/hit-count breakpoints, hot code replace, run/debug configurations, multi-session tabs, smart step-into, drop frame, the Jump-to-Line gutter-arrow drag affordance.*
- `install/` — **In-app install of language support** (LSP server + DAP adapter for Java/Python/JS, plus the Mermaid CLI), cross-platform (macOS/Linux/Windows), the Java path the bash `scripts/install-*.sh` used to be. Pure **`InstallCatalog`** (java.base only, unit-tested) maps a `Lang` (JAVA/PYTHON/JAVASCRIPT/MERMAID) → an ordered `Step` list (`Kind` NPM_GLOBAL/PIP_TARGET/VSIX/TARBALL + its prereqs + dest), with the pure URL/argv helpers (`openVsxLatestUrl`, `JDTLS_TARBALL_URL`, `JS_DEBUG_RELEASES_API`, `npmInstallGlobalArgv`/`pipInstallTargetArgv`/`tarExtractArgv`, `firstMatch` for asset-URL extraction, `forBufferLanguage`). Recipes: **pyright**/**typescript-language-server**/**mmdc** = `npm i -g` (then `npx puppeteer browsers install chrome-headless-shell` from mmdc's dir, version-matched, so the headless Chrome it renders with is present — `Kind.PUPPETEER_BROWSER`) (global); **debugpy** = `pip install --target <config>/plugins/dap/python`; **java-debug** = Open VSX `.vsix` (a ZIP) → reuse `plugin/Unzip` → `<config>/plugins/dap/java`; **jdtls** = Eclipse JDT-LS `.tar.gz` → system `tar` → `<config>/plugins/lsp/java` (then `Settings.javaLspCommand` ← `bin/jdtls`, the dir `ProcessRunner.EXTRA_PATH_DIRS` already anticipates); **js-debug** = GitHub release `.tar.gz` → system `tar` → `<config>/plugins/dap/javascript`. **`InstallService`** (the `GitService`/`MermaidService` idiom: one daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) runs the steps off-thread reusing `ProcessRunner.run/resolveExecutable` (npm/pip/tar; Windows `.cmd`/`.exe` resolution + augmented PATH so a GUI-launched app finds them), `PluginRegistry.readCapped`+`isHttps` over `java.net.http` for bounded HTTPS downloads, and `Unzip.extract` for the vsix; `detectPrereqs` probes npm/python/tar on PATH. **`ui/InstallCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern + a small `Ops` for config-dir / per-feature availability reads / re-detect): `installSupport(lang)` filters to the *missing* tools (per the existing `LspCoordinator.isServerAvailable`/`DapManager.isLanguageAvailable`/`MermaidCoordinator.mmdcAvailable` detectors), checks prereqs first (reports a missing Node/Python/tar instead of installing it — Editora never installs runtimes), runs them, then `reapplyToolSupport()` (`LspManager.invalidateDetection()` + `LspCoordinator`/`DebugCoordinator`/`MermaidCoordinator` `applySupport()` + persist) so the tools activate **without a restart**. Palette commands `install.javaSupport`/`pythonSupport`/`jsSupport`/`mermaidSupport`. **Settings → Language Servers** rows (java/python/typescript) and the **Mermaid** page also carry an **Install…** button (`SettingsWindow.setInstallActions` injected with a language-key consumer → `installSupport`; tracked in `installButtons`, flipped to "Installed"/disabled by `updateInstallButton` from the existing `refreshLspStatus`/`refreshMermaidStatus` detect callbacks; `MainController`'s `reapplyToolSupport` calls `SettingsWindow.refreshDetectionStatus()` after an install so it updates live — the JS row installs the LSP **and** js-debug, so the Debugger page needs no separate button). **In-editor install banner:** `EditorBuffer.getNode()`'s `BorderPane` top stacks (in a `VBox`, via `refreshTopBars`) a generic `.lsp-install-bar` (built lazily like `buildViewModeBar`; toolkit-only `setInstallPrompt(message, actionLabel, onInstall, onDismiss)` + `showInstallBar`/`setInstallBarBusy`, so `editor` stays decoupled) **above** the existing `.view-mode-bar`. `MainController.maybeOfferInstall(buffer)` (run on tab switch / after an install / on `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange`) shows it per `shouldOfferInstall`: the buffer's language has an installer, the relevant feature is **on** but its server/CLI is **confirmed missing** (`lspEnabled() && lspCoordinator.isServerMissing(...)` — tri-state, *probed-and-absent* not merely pending; or `mermaid.isEnabled() && mmdcDetected() && !mmdcAvailable()`), no live LSP session is already serving the file (`!lspCoordinator.isManaged(path)`), the user hasn't dismissed it (a `WeakHashMap` `installDismissed`, mirroring `httpUserClosed`), it's a local buffer, and the master nudge `Settings.lspInstallPrompts` (default on, schema 44→45 additive; Settings → Language Servers checkbox + `view.toggleInstallPrompts`) is on. **Install** runs `installCoordinator.installSupport(lang, ok→…)` (the callback overload spins the banner + hides on success); **Not now** dismisses for that buffer. The banner re-evaluates when LSP detection settles (`LspCoordinator.applyGating` → `Ops.onDetectionSettled` → `maybeOfferInstall`), so a late-starting server hides it without a tab switch. Downloads are HTTPS-only + capped; `Unzip` keeps its zip-slip/size guards; **no new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (`install` is internal). **More LSP servers (server-id-centric):** beyond the 4 `Lang` bundles, `InstallCatalog.installableServerIds()` + `serverInstall(serverId)` describe the **LSP-only** servers (no DAP) keyed by their `LspServerRegistry` server id; `InstallCoordinator.installServer(serverId[, cb])` installs one (filters on `lspAvailable(serverId)`, prereq-checks, runs, re-detects). The Settings → Language Servers rows get an **Install…** button for any `installableServerIds()` entry (`SettingsWindow.setInstallServerActions`), the editor banner offers them via `LspServerRegistry.serverIdFor(language)` (in `MainController.maybeOfferInstall`'s server-id branch), and the palette `install.languageServer` picks any installable server (`QuickOpen` over `installableServerIds()`). The npm batch (needs Node): **json/html/css** (one package `vscode-langservers-extracted`), **bash**, **yaml**, **dockerfile** (`dockerfile-language-server-nodejs`), **toml** (`@taplo/cli`). The **toolchain batch** (`Kind.TOOL_COMMAND` — argv carried in the `Step.npmPackages` field; runs via the language's own package manager, gated on that toolchain being on PATH via the new `Prereq` GO/RUBY/DOTNET/RUSTUP/COMPOSER): **go** (`go install …/gopls@latest`), **sql** (`go install …/sqls@latest`), **ruby** (`gem install ruby-lsp`), **csharp** (`dotnet tool install --global csharp-ls`), **rust** (`rustup component add rust-analyzer`), **php** (`composer global require phpactor/phpactor`). The **binary batch** (`Kind.ARCHIVE` + `InstallCatalog.archiveSpec(serverId)` → an `ArchiveSpec{apiUrl, Map<Platform,assetSubstring>, binaryName, binaryPrefix, commandSuffix}`; `InstallService.installArchive` picks the asset for `currentPlatform()` (`platformKey`, pure/unit-tested), downloads it, extracts (zip via the new capped `Unzip.extract(...,maxEntry,maxTotal,maxEntries)` since clangd's binary dwarfs the plugin caps; `.tar.gz` via system `tar`), `findBinary`-walks the tree, `chmod +x`es it, and returns the path → the coordinator persists it into that server's `Settings.<id>LspCommand` via `applyServerCommand`): **clangd** (clangd/clangd), **xml**/lemminx (redhat-developer/vscode-xml, binary prefix-matched `lemminx-…`), **kotlin** (fwcd/kotlin-language-server, single `server.zip`), **lua** (LuaLS, per-OS tar.gz/zip), **terraform** (releases.hashicorp.com via the HashiCorp releases API, command suffix ` serve`). All 21 LSP servers now have an installer. *Deferred: a keymap binding for the install commands.*
- **Markdown editing** (pure cores in `markdown/`, UI/overlays in `editor/`) — an IntelliJ-style **selection format bar** + smart editing, gated to Markdown buffers (`isMarkdown()` + editable + non-huge + view mode ≠ pure PREVIEW). Pure, unit-tested cores (no toolkit) all return a `markdown/MarkdownEdit` record (`from,to,replacement,selStart,selEnd`, applied via `area.replaceText`+`selectRange`, mirroring `Commenter`): **`MarkdownInline`** (toggle wrap/unwrap of `**`/`*`/`~~`/`` ` ``; `link(...)`; `linkAround(caret)` for open-link), **`MarkdownLines`** (`continuation(line)`/`isEmptyItem`/`markerLength` for list/quote continuation + `toggleBullet`), **`MarkdownHeading`** (`apply(delta)` promote/demote + `setLevel`, clamped 0–6, multi-line), **`MarkdownTable`** (`blockBounds(caret)` + `reflow` padding/aligning pipes honoring `:--`/`:-:`/`--:`; plus **table generation/editing** — `generate(rowsTotal, cols)` builds an aligned skeleton, `addRow`/`deleteRow`/`addColumn`/`deleteColumn` and `setAlignment(…, Align)` mutate the caret's table, each returning a `Nav{block,caret}` the controller applies like `tab`; the existing `tab`/`enter` give Tab-to-next-cell + add-row-on-Enter); `MarkdownLines.toggleTask` adds/removes a GFM checkbox (`- [ ] `). The **`editor/MarkdownFormatBar`** is a non-focus-traversable, free-positioned HBox of **icon buttons** — the same `MenuIcons` glyphs the editor right-click menu uses (bold/italic/strikethrough/code/link) plus bullet-list, **task-list/checkbox**, and an **insert-table** grid button (`MenuIcons.bulletList()`/`taskList()`/`table()`) and a Normal/H1–H6 `ComboBox` — calling back into `EditorBuffer` format methods (icons instead of letter labels keep it consistent with the menu and avoid the barely-slanted italic "I"; kept in `editor`, no `ui` dependency, like `CompletionPopup`). `EditorBuffer` owns the lifecycle: a **coalesced** `selectionProperty`/scroll listener (`scheduleFormatBar`/`updateFormatBar`, pending-flag per pulse — the `scheduleBraceMatch` idiom) positions it above the selection via `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen`→`screenToLocal`→`resizeRelocate` on `root`/`root2` (the ghost-label technique), hiding on Escape/blur/empty selection; format methods (`formatInline`/`formatLink`/`formatLinkFromClipboard`/`formatHeading`/`setHeadingLevel`/`formatBulletList`/`reflowTable`/`openLinkUnderCaret`) apply the core's `MarkdownEdit`; list/quote continuation lives in the existing `addAutoIndent` Enter filter; Ctrl/Cmd-click opens a link via an injected `setOpenUrlHandler` (controller `openExternalUrl`). Commands (markdown-gated, no-op elsewhere with a status): `markdown.bold`/`italic`/`strikethrough`/`code`/`link`/`bulletList`/`taskList`/`headingPromote`/`headingDemote`/`openLink`/`reflowTable`/`toggleFormatBar` + the table commands `insertTable` (the **mouse** path — the format-bar button + right-click "Insert Table" — opens a Typora/Word-style grid size-picker overlay; the **command-palette** path is keyboard-only, prompting for an `RxC` string parsed by the pure `MarkdownTable.parseSize`; both → `EditorBuffer.insertTable`)/`tableAddRow`/`tableDeleteRow`/`tableAddColumn`/`tableDeleteColumn`/`tableAlignLeft`/`tableAlignCenter`/`tableAlignRight`, with Emacs `markdown-mode`-style chords (`C-c C-s b/i/s/c`, `C-c C-s u`/`k` (bullet/task list), `C-c C-a l`, `C-c C-h p|d`, `C-c C-o`, `C-c C-s t` — note `C-c C-t` is taken by `view.toggleFold`) + a right-click **Format** group (`EditorBuffer.markdownMenuItems`, which also carries a **Table** submenu — insert/add/delete row & column/align). Gated by `Settings.markdownFormatBar` (default on; schema 13→14 additive-identity; Settings → Editor → Markdown checkbox + `SettingsWindow.syncMarkdownFormatBarCheck`; `MainController.applyViewSettings` pushes `setFormatBarEnabled`). CSS `.markdown-format-bar`/`.md-fmt-*` in `app.css`; i18n `command.markdown.*`/`tooltip.markdown.*`/`markdown.heading.*`/`settings.markdownFormatBar`/`status.markdown.*` across the six catalogs. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** The pure Markdown logic — the editing cores (`MarkdownEdit`/`MarkdownInline`/`MarkdownLines`/`MarkdownHeading`/`MarkdownTable`), the lint cores (`MarkdownLint`/`MarkdownLintConfig`/`MarkdownLintDirectives`/`MarkdownLintFix`), `MarkdownOutline`, and `MarkdownImagePaste` — lives in its own **`com.editora.markdown`** package (internal, no `exports`/`opens`/`module-info` change), with their unit tests under `com.editora.markdown`; the FX `MarkdownRenderer`, the preview/lint overlays + stripes, `MarkdownFormatBar`, and the image loaders (`PreviewImageLoader`/`MermaidImages`/`MathImages`) stay in `editor/` as the editor's rendering surfaces.  Tables also convert to/from **CSV**: pure/unit-tested `MarkdownTable.fromCsv` (delimiter auto-detect comma/semicolon/tab, RFC-4180 quoting, pipe-escaping) and `toCsv` back the GFM table block to the clipboard, via `EditorBuffer.tableFromCsv`/`tableToCsv` → commands `markdown.tableFromCsv`/`markdown.tableToCsv` + the right-click Table submenu. The caret's table also **file-exports** to **CSV / Excel (`.xlsx`) / ODF (`.ods`)**: `EditorBuffer.exportTableFile(format)` renders the table via `MarkdownTable.toCsv` then hands the CSV + format to the injected `setTableFileExporter` (editor stays free of `ui`/`office`); `MainController.exportMarkdownTableFile` picks the destination (`chooseOfficeDestination`) and either writes the CSV text (`exportCsvTextToFile`) or reuses the CSV grid's `csvExportSpreadsheet` (`CsvParser.parse` → `office/OfficeExportService.exportXlsx`/`exportOds`, header row = true since `toCsv` drops the `---` divider). Commands `markdown.tableExportCsv`/`tableExportExcel`/`tableExportOds` (palette + the right-click Table submenu, `MenuIcons.download()`); no new dependency.  **Table of contents:** pure/unit-tested `markdown/MarkdownToc` (`build`/`updated`/`slug`, reusing `MarkdownOutline.headings`) generates a nested list of GitHub-anchor heading links; `EditorBuffer.insertOrUpdateToc` inserts it wrapped in `<!-- toc -->`/`<!-- /toc -->` markers at the caret, or regenerates the existing marker block in place — command `markdown.toc` (palette + the right-click Markdown menu). (Supersedes the registry `markdown-toc` plugin.) **Image insertion** (pure `markdown/MarkdownImagePaste`: `uniqueFileName`/`relativePath`/`snippet`/`imageUrlFromDrag`/`extensionForUrl`): pasting a clipboard image (`tryMarkdownImagePaste`), dropping image **files** (`EditorBuffer.installImageDrop` → `MainController.insertDroppedImages`), and dragging a **raw image / image URL out of a web browser** (`setWebImageDropHandler` → `insertWebImage`) all copy/download the bytes into a sibling `assets/` dir and insert `![](assets/…)`. The browser path resolves the source via `MarkdownImagePaste.imageUrlFromDrag` (drag URL → `<img src>` in the dragged HTML → an image-looking string) and downloads it **off the FX thread** (`PreviewImageLoader.fetchBytes`, handling http(s) + `data:`); a raw `Dragboard` image is encoded to PNG via `PreviewImageLoader.imageToPng` (headless Java2D, no `javafx.swing`); on total failure it falls back to inserting the remote URL. Requires a saved local file (`assets/` resolves next to it; else `status.markdown.imageNeedsSave`). *Deferred: reference-style links, WYSIWYG inline rendering, table auto-format-on-type, table cell-merge / move-row-or-column, format bar in plaintext.*
- **Personal Notes** — file-attached annotations stored **outside** the file (for read-only/generated/shared code), built as a *separate* feature that reuses the **Bookmarks** machinery (see the bookmarks paragraph) rather than extending it; the two coexist. **Model** (`config/`, all Jackson-serialized so they ride the existing `opens com.editora.config to jackson.databind` — no `module-info` change): `enum NoteScope{WORD,LINE,RANGE}`, `enum NoteStatus{ACTIVE,RESOLVED,ORPHANED}`, `record FileIdentity(path,canonicalPath,size,lastModified,hash)` (pure `of(Path)` sha-256 capped at `MAX_HASH_BYTES`=5 MB, pure `match(a,b)` priority **canonicalPath → contentHash → similarPath**), `record TextAnchor(line,column,endLine,endColumn,selectedText,prefix,suffix)` (`MAX_TEXT`/`MAX_CONTEXT` caps), `record PersonalNote(UUID id, FileIdentity, NoteScope, TextAnchor, body, List<String> tags, NoteStatus, long createdAt, long updatedAt)` — **`long` epoch-millis timestamps deliberately** (the default `ObjectMapper` has no jsr310 module). `NoteStore` mirrors `BookmarkStore`: `schemaVersion` + per-project `Map<projectKey, Map<fileKey, List<PersonalNote>>> byProject` (fileKey = canonicalPath), static `mergePreservingOrder(prev,current)` (matches by note **id**). **Storage**: a single versioned `notes.json` (`ConfigManager.getNotesFile`/`getNotes()` = the active project's bucket via the same `currentBookmarkKey()` derivation as bookmarks / `saveNotes()` / `loadNotes()` via `ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(..., ConfigSchema.NOTES)` / `deleteNotesForProject`), kept out of `WorkspaceState` like bookmarks. **Anchoring** (`editor/`): pure, unit-tested `NoteAnchors` (`shiftOffset`/`shiftRange` interval-adjust through a `PlainTextChange`; `relocate(doc,savedStart,savedEnd,selectedText,prefix,suffix)` → `int[]{start,end}` or null=orphan: level-1 exact-offset check, else occurrence scoring with a prefix/suffix-context bonus + proximity, bounded by `MAX_OCCURRENCES`). `NoteManager` (per-buffer, like `BookmarkManager`): holds `Map<UUID,Tracked>` of notes + live offset ranges, subscribes to `area.plainTextChanges()` to shift ranges (does **not** fire `onChanged` on edit-shifts — only `onLinesRepaint`;
