persistence happens on save/tab-switch, never per-keystroke), exposes `isNoted(line)`/`notesOnLine`/`noteAt(offset)`/`activeLines`/`next`/`previous`/`activeSpans()` (for the overlay), `add/update/remove/setStatus/clear` (these fire `onChanged`), `snapshot()` (rebuilds anchors from offsets), and `restore(saved)` (relocates each via `NoteAnchors`, returns whether anything moved/orphaned so the controller self-heal-persists — the bookmark pattern). **Editor surface**: `NoteHighlightOverlay` (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`/`WhitespaceOverlay`: coalesced per-pulse redraw, visible-spans only, soft amber wash) paints behind each note's anchored span as a **flat, contiguous fill drawn like a text selection** (`paintSpan`, clamped to `first/lastVisibleParToAllParIndex`): one square fillRect **per visible line** with no per-line outline/rounding so adjacent lines join seamlessly; intermediate lines of a multi-line range fill to the viewport's right edge (matching how a selection paints the included line break), the first line starts at the start column and the last line stops at the end column; it also draws a small **amber corner-triangle marker at the note's start character** (inline, on the note's first visible line) — the "there's a note here" indicator is now inline at the selection start, **not** a gutter slot, and is **clickable** (`EditorBuffer.setNoteMarkerClick` → edit the note — restoring the old gutter click-to-edit). A `mouse-moved` hover (guarded to only update when the hovered note id changes) shows the body in a `Tooltip` whose graphic is the body **rendered as Markdown** (`renderNoteTooltip` → `MarkdownRenderer`, in the editor's own font family/size, with `app.css`+`syntax.css` attached to the node since the tooltip lives in its own popup scene; plain-label fallback on failure); the editor right-click menu prepends "Add Personal Note"/"Add Note to Selection" (when `path != null`). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the bookmark API: `getNoteManager`, `setAddNoteHandler`, `setOnNotesChanged`, `applyNotes`, `captureNoteDraft()` (infers WORD/RANGE/LINE + prefix/suffix context), `fileIdentity()`, `setNoteIndicatorsVisible`. **UI/commands**: `NotesPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `BookmarksPanel`) groups notes per file with a filter (bold file-header rows like Find-in-Files, plus a trailing clear-(`✕`) button shown only while the filter has text, reusing `.project-filter-bar`/`.project-filter-clear`), NoteCell context menu (Edit/Resolve↔Reopen/Delete, file: Delete all), double-click/Enter to open; tool window id `notes` (`tool.notes`, `M-5`, `Icons.notes()`). **`ui/NotesCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern) owns the `NotesPanel` + the two cross-file pickers + `persistNotes`/`restoreNotes` (run on save / tab switch / project switch; re-key by hash when the path key misses but the bucket is non-empty), `addNoteFromContext`/`addNoteAtCaret`, `editNoteAtCaret` (the `notes.editNote` command — edit the note at the caret, replacing the old gutter-click), `jumpNote` (next/previous), the `notes.jump` cross-file QuickOpen (`M-g n` — matches the note's first line) + `searchNotes` (`notes.search` — the same picker but its `QuickOpen` `searchKey` matches the **full body + tags + file** via `noteSearchText`, while the displayed label stays the first line; `QuickOpen` gained an optional `searchKey` ctor arg defaulting to the label, so other pickers are unchanged), `deleteNoteAtCaret`, `exportNotes` (FileChooser → JSON), the `showNoteDialog` editor, and the gating (`applySupport`/`ifEnabled`/`migrateKey`); it reaches the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension (open-path / navigate-to-line / the shared `noteKey` + open-buffer-for-key / install-emacs-keys / tool-window availability / the `notes.json` map). `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `notesCoordinator.panel()`), the global `promptText`/`noteKey`/`tabForKey`/`navigateToLine`/`openPath` helpers, the rename-migration call (`notesCoordinator.migrateKey`), and wires `addBuffer`'s note hooks + the `notes.*`/`view.toggleNotes` commands to the coordinator. (Resolve/Reopen is available from the panel's NoteCell menu; there's no caret command for it.) Bodies are edited via `showNoteDialog(initial, onAccept, onDelete)` — a **multi-line** `TextArea` `Dialog` (Enter = newline, Ctrl/Cmd+Enter = save) with the user's **configured keybindings** installed for caret movement + basic editing via `command/TextInputKeymap.install(textArea, keymap)` (a dialog has its own scene, so the global `KeyDispatcher` isn't there — `TextInputKeymap` adds a `KEY_PRESSED` filter that resolves the same chord token through `KeymapManager` and runs the matching `nav.*`/`edit.*` action on the `TextInputControl`, e.g. Emacs `C-a`/`C-e`/`C-f`/`C-b`/`C-n`/`C-p`/`M-f`/`M-b`/`C-d`/`C-k`/`C-w`/`M-w`/`C-y`; pure caret math `lineStart`/`lineEnd`/`lineUp`/`lineDown`/`backToIndentation` is unit-tested; reusable for any dialog text field); when editing an existing note it shows a left-aligned **Delete** button (`onDelete`) that **confirms first** (a native `CONFIRMATION` alert). The dialog also shows a muted hint (`.note-dialog-hint`) that the body supports **Markdown** (it renders as Markdown in the hover tooltip). `promptNoteBody` delegates to it with no delete. Commands: `notes.add` (`C-c n`), `notes.editNote` (`C-c e`, edit the note at the caret — also via clicking the inline marker), `notes.toggleResolved` (resolve/reopen the note at the caret), `notes.next`/`previous`, `notes.jump` (`M-g n`), `notes.search` (`M-g s`, full-text picker), `notes.delete` (deletes the note on the caret line; also in the panel + the editor's Delete button), `notes.export`, `tool.notes` (`M-5`). **Gated by `Settings.notesSupport`** ("Enable Personal Notes", Settings → Application, default **on**) — `NotesCoordinator.applySupport()` (mirrors `GitCoordinator.applySupport`, called at init + on every settings apply) hides the Notes tool window (`toolWindows.setAvailable`), sets each buffer's `setNotesEnabled` (gates the editor "Add Note" menu items), and on the off→on transition `restoreNotes` every open buffer; the `ifEnabled(...)` wrapper no-ops each `notes.*`/`tool.notes` command + keybinding, those ids are filtered from the command palette, and `persistNotes`/`restoreNotes` early-return while off. A second **view toggle** `Settings.showNoteIndicators` (default on, only effective when notes are enabled) hides just the inline start marker + highlight — `applyViewSettings` applies the effective `notesSupport && showNoteIndicators`, and the Settings "Show note indicators" checkbox disables when the master is off (autocomplete master/sub pattern). All strings localized in the six catalogs. *Deferred: fuzzy match beyond nearest-text, scrollbar/minimap markers, Markdown note bodies, team/cloud sync — the model already carries tags/status/FileIdentity so these are additive.*
- `vfs/` — **Remote file access (SFTP)**. Edit/browse/search files on a remote host over SSH/SFTP. The
  approach keeps `EditorBuffer.path` a `java.nio.file.Path` but lets it belong to a **non-default
  filesystem** (a MINA SSHD `SftpFileSystem`), so `Files.readString`/`writeString`/`list`/`walkFileTree`/
  `readAttributes` keep working over SFTP and the Project tree / search / open / save need no rewrite. The
  only local-only boundary is `path.toFile()` (used by `ProcessRunner`/LSP/DAP/run) — gated off for remote.
  **`Vfs`** (pure, unit-tested) is the seam: `isLocal(Path)` (= `path.getFileSystem() == FileSystems.getDefault()`,
  the single predicate every local-process feature gates on; a null/untitled path counts as local),
  `toStorableString`/`parseStorable` (a path↔string round-trip — local plain, remote as its `sftp://` URI,
  reconstructed through an injected resolver), `isRemoteUri`, `displayLabel`. **`SftpUri`** (pure,
  unit-tested) parses/formats `sftp://[user@]host[:port]/path` and yields the `authority()` connection key.
  **`RemoteConnection`** (record: host/port/user/`AuthMethod {DEFAULT_KEYS, KEY, PASSWORD}`/keyPath/label/
  lastPath — **no secret**) + **`config/ConnectionStore`** (schema-versioned `connections.json`,
  `ConfigSchema.CONNECTIONS`; `ConfigManager.getConnections`/`putConnection`/`removeConnection`/
  `saveConnections`/`loadConnections`). **`RemoteFileSystems`** (UI-owned, the `GitService` idiom: a daemon
  executor + `Platform.runLater`) holds one `SftpFileSystem` per `user@host:port`, `connect(conn, secret,
  cb)` (auth precedence **default `~/.ssh` keys → key file → password**; the secret `char[]` is wiped after
  use), `pathFor(SftpUri)`/`disconnect`/`shutdown`, and wires `Vfs.setRemoteResolver` so remote URIs in
  recent-files reconstruct to live Paths. **Local-only gating** (all inert for local files, so zero
  behavior change): `MainController.isLocalBuffer` + `Vfs.isLocal` guards on LSP (`syncBufferLsp`
  eligibility), DAP/breakpoints (`isDebuggableBuffer`), run/shell-run/HTTP (`addBuffer`), git
  (`refreshGit` → `RepoState.NONE` for a remote context), and external-change polling
  (`checkExternalChanges` skips remote — a network `mtime` per focus). **Remote stays text-capable**:
  editing, highlighting, search, bookmarks, notes, preview, PDF/print. **The SFTP UI/commands live in
  `ui/RemoteCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `RemoteFileSystems`
  engine + the `RemoteConnectionsPanel` + the mount state, reaching the window via the shared host plus an
  `Ops` extension for keymap / open-path / set-project-root / open-project-tool-window / active-project-root /
  error-report (reusing `GitCoordinator.gitError`) / the `connections.json` get/put/remove; `MainController`
  keeps the `remote` `ToolWindow` built with `remoteCoordinator.panel()`, queries `isMounted()` for the
  current-folder view, and wires the `remote.*`/`tool.remote` commands + the Welcome quick-connect to it).
  **UI/commands**:
  `remote.connect` (an `OverlayInput` form — host/port/user/auth + key Browse/secret/path, localized auth
  picker; on success **mounts the remote folder as the Project tree root** via `projectPanel.setRoot` +
  opens the Project tool window, and `config.putConnection`s it), `remote.manageConnections` (a `QuickOpen`
  over saved connections → re-opens the form pre-filled), `remote.openFile` (an `sftp://` URI →
  `Vfs.parseStorable` → `openPath`), `remote.disconnect` (restores the local project root). **Saved sites get
  three visible surfaces** (all over the same `connections.json` most-recent-first list — no schema/secret
  change): a **Remote Sites tool window** (`ui/RemoteConnectionsPanel`, id `remote`, `Side.RIGHT`, `Icons::remote`,
  `tool.remote`/`M-g r`, *not* buffer-gated, **registered default-hidden** via `toolWindows.register(tw, false)` —
  the stripe button is off until the user enables it (Settings → Tool Windows or `tool.remote`), and it opens on the
  right; the remote *functionality* is unaffected — a flat `ListView` of saved sites; double-click/Enter or the
  New/Connect/Remove bar → `connectRemote(c)`/`removeConnection`/`connectRemote()`, refreshed on open + after a
  mount); a **Settings → Remote master-detail page** (`SettingsWindow.remoteConnectionsEditor`, mirroring the
  External Tools page — list + label/host/port/user/auth/key-path form editing the immutable `RemoteConnection`
  record via `remoteItems.set(i, …)`, persisted through the new `ConfigManager.setConnections(list)` →
  `SharedConfig` whole-list replace; opened by `remote.settings` → `showRemote`); and a **Welcome-page "Remote
  Sites" quick-connect list** (`WelcomePane.remoteList`, shown only when non-empty, each row → `connectRemote(c)`).
  All three open the **prefilled connect form** on pick (so the secret is still prompted), never a silent
  reconnect. A remote buffer
  opens with a remote `Path`, so plain Save → `writeBuffer` → `Files.writeString` writes back over SFTP, no
  dialog; `saveAs` is guarded for remote. Recent files round-trip the `sftp://` URI (`Vfs.toStorableString`;
  a remote entry resolves only once its connection is open). **Dependency:** Apache **MINA SSHD**
  (`org.apache.sshd:sshd-osgi` + `sshd-sftp`) — the combined **sshd-osgi** bundle (module
  `org.apache.sshd.osgi`) is used instead of sshd-common+sshd-core, which **split** the
  `org.apache.sshd.common`/`server` packages across two automatic modules (illegal under JPMS); `sshd-sftp`
  **excludes** sshd-core/sshd-common + **`jcl-over-slf4j`** (its `org.apache.commons.logging` module
  collides with pdfbox's commons-logging under jlink), and **slf4j-api is forced to 2.0.17** (a real
  module, not the automatic 1.7.36 SSHD pins). `module-info` `requires org.apache.sshd.osgi`/`.sftp` +
  `opens com.editora.vfs to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind` (the `RemoteConnection` record). **dist/jlink
  moditect:** sshd-osgi uses a hand-maintained `src/moditect/module-info-sshd-osgi.java` (jdeps's 106
  exports + a `requires org.slf4j` jdeps drops under `--ignore-missing-deps` — without it every SSHD class
  fails at load), and sshd-sftp uses a hand-written client-only `<moduleInfoSource>` (drops the unused SFTP-
  *server* `SubsystemFactory` provides that jlink rejects, keeps only the nio FileSystemProvider). The
  `-Pdist` app-image builds, links, and launches. *Deferred: OS-keychain secret storage + auto-reconnect on
  launch, true ssh-agent (SSH_AUTH_SOCK), remote LSP/DAP/git/run, remote Save-As / new-file, a status-bar
  remote indicator + tab tooltip, remote-search caps, FTP/WebDAV/cloud providers (the layer generalizes).*
- `plugin/` — **Plugin support** (off by default, gated by `Settings.pluginSupport`; **also off in Simple UI
  mode** via `pluginsEnabled()`). A plugin is a folder `<configDir>/plugins/<id>/` with a `plugin.json`
  manifest + optionally a Java jar (`*.jar`/`lib/*.jar`) + `snippets/`/`templates/` dirs. **The one hard
  constraint:** the `-Pdist` build is a **sealed jlink image with no module path at runtime** and there is no
  `ServiceLoader` infra, so plugins are discovered by **manifest** and a Java plugin's classes load via a
  child **`URLClassLoader(jarUrls, appClassLoader)`** (parent = the app module's loader → the plugin can use
  Editora's **exported** packages `com.editora.plugin`/`command`/`ui`/`editor`/`config` + the baked JDK/JavaFX
  modules via normal parent delegation; **no `ModuleLayer`**). Compile a plugin on a plain **classpath**, not
  the module path. **API (the exported `com.editora.plugin` package):** `interface Plugin {void start(ctx);
  default void stop()}`; `interface PluginContext` (`registerCommand(id,title,Runnable)`, `bindKey(chord,
  commandId)`, `registerToolWindow(id,title,ToolWindowSide,Region,commandId[,Supplier<Node> icon])` (the icon
  overload sets the stripe glyph — a `Supplier<javafx.scene.Node>`, e.g. an `SVGPath` with the `toolbar-icon`
  style class; the no-icon overload is a `default` delegating with `null` ⇒ the jigsaw `Icons.plugin()`),
  `addEditorMenuItem(label,
  Consumer<ActiveEditor>)`, `addStatusBarSegment(label,commandId)`, `activeEditor()`, `pluginDir()/dataDir()/
  configDir()`, `log/setStatus`); `interface ActiveEditor` (narrow editor facade — `filePath/text/
  selectedText/replaceSelection/insertAtCaret/setText/openPath` (`setText` = whole-buffer replace, undoable —
  for whole-file transforms like formatting), **never** exposes `MainController`); `enum
  ToolWindowSide{LEFT,RIGHT,BOTTOM}` (keeps the API package free of a hard `ui` dependency); lenient Jackson
  `PluginManifest` (`@JsonIgnoreProperties` — `id/name/version/main`, `Map keymap`, `List<DeclaredCommand>
  commands{id,title,List<String> run,dir}`) + `PluginDescriptor` (manifest/dir/enabled/classLoader/loadError).
  **`PluginManager`** is **shared, owned by `ui/WindowManager`** (created once with `(pluginsDir, isEnabled
  predicate)` + `discover()`): `discover()` scans the dir, parses each manifest (`parseManifest`, unit-tested),
  builds one `URLClassLoader` per enabled Java plugin; `instantiate(descriptor)` does `Class.forName(main,...)`
  + `newInstance` under the plugin TCCL, catching `Throwable` → null (one bad plugin never blocks others).
  **The whole plugin feature lives in `ui/PluginCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern): it owns the
  per-window `PluginRegistry`/`PluginInstaller`, the started-plugin instances, the plugin-contributed tool
  windows + editor menu items, the "Browse Plugins" picker, and the two inner adapters
  (`PluginContextImpl`/`ActiveEditorImpl`). The shared `PluginManager` (owned by `WindowManager`) is passed
  in; `MainController` keeps the `pluginManager` field + thin `disposePlugins()` (the `WindowManager`
  window-close contract) and `pluginsEnabled()` delegates, and wires `applyPlugins` / the buffer-gating
  (`gateToolWindows`) / the editor-menu contributor (`editorMenuItems`) / the `plugins.*`+`view.togglePlugins`
  commands to the coordinator; `PluginCoordinator.pluginCapabilitySummary` is the public static the Settings
  page also calls. **Multi-window:** classes load **once** (shared manager), but a `Plugin` **instance + its
  tool-window content Node are built per window** (a Node can't live in two scenes) — `PluginCoordinator.applyPlugins()` (run in
  `init`, **before** `toolWindows.restore()` so contributed windows restore their visibility) registers the
  declarative bits + `plugin.<id>.<cmd>` external commands (`runDeclaredCommand` → `process/ProcessRunner`
  off-thread) + applies the shared `keymap.applyOverrides(manifest.keymap)`, then `instantiate` + `start(new
  PluginContextImpl(d))` each Java plugin; `disposePlugins()` (window close) calls each `stop()`.
  `PluginContextImpl.fullId(id)` namespaces a bare command/tool-window id to `plugin.<id>.<...>` (a dotted id
  = a built-in, used verbatim); tool windows register via `toolWindows.register` + a toggle command,
  status-bar segments via `StatusBar.addPluginSegment`, editor menu items via a `setMenuContributor` hook on
  each `EditorBuffer` (the `editor` package stays decoupled — a `Supplier<List<MenuItem>>` injected from
  `MainController.pluginEditorMenuItems`). **Buffer-gated stripe:** every registered plugin tool window is
  tracked in `MainController.pluginToolWindows` and its stripe button is gated on an open editor buffer
  (`toolWindows.setAvailable(tw, activeBuffer() != null)` at registration + in `updateBufferToolWindows()`,
  alongside the built-in Structure/File-Info/TODO windows) — plugins act on the active editor, so they're
  hidden on a non-buffer tab (e.g. Welcome). **Opt-out:** the full
  `registerToolWindow(id,title,side,content,commandId,icon,needsBuffer)` overload takes a `needsBuffer` flag
  (the icon/no-icon overloads are `default`s delegating with `true`); a plugin passes `false` for a
  self-contained tool window (scratchpad/calculator/…) so it's **not** added to `pluginToolWindows` and stays
  available on every tab. Declarative **assets**: `SnippetManager.addExtraSourceDir`/
  `TemplateRegistry.addExtraSourceDir` (generalized extra-source-dir lists, cache-clearing) merge a plugin's
  `snippets/`/`templates/` into the registries (`reload()`d once after applying). **Enabled set** lives in
  `<configDir>/plugins.json` (`config/PluginStore`, schema-versioned via `ConfigSchema.PLUGINS`, owned by
  `SharedConfig` — `getPluginStore`/`savePlugins`/`getPluginsDir`). **Gating:** `Settings.pluginSupport`
  (default off; schema 21→22 additive-identity) + `applyPlugins` early-returns when off, so `plugin.*`
  commands are never even registered when disabled (no palette filter needed). **Settings → Plugins** page
  (data-driven over `pluginManager.descriptors()`): a master *Enable plugins* checkbox + a "runs untrusted
  code, no sandbox" warning + the plugins-folder path + a **Reload** button (`discover()` + `refreshPluginList`)
  + a per-plugin enable checkbox row (writes `PluginStore.setEnabled` + `savePlugins`; load errors shown in
  red `settings-git-missing`) + a "restart to apply" note; `SettingsWindow.setPluginManager` is injected after
  construction (the page builds lazily on first `show`). Palette toggle `view.togglePlugins`
  (`togglePluginSupport` — persists + `syncPluginsCheck`, reports a restart is needed). `module-info`
  `exports com.editora.plugin;` + `opens com.editora.plugin to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind;` (the manifest
  DTO). **Plugins load at startup only** — enable/disable + the master gate take effect on the next launch (no
  hot classloader/UI unload; per-window `stop()` on close is the only teardown). **One new exported package; no
  new Maven dependency.** Plugin-API Javadoc (the author-facing surface) builds + doclint-validates via the `apidocs` profile: `./mvnw -Papidocs javadoc:javadoc` (scoped to `com.editora.plugin`, `doclint=all,-missing` so broken `@link`/HTML fail). Example: `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin with a
  `build.sh`) + `docs/plugins.md`. **Registry / install (browse + from-disk):** a plugin is distributed as a
  **`.zip`** whose top level is the plugin folder contents. **`RegistryIndex`/`RegistryEntry`** (lenient
  Jackson, static `parse`) model a curated **`index.json`**; **`PluginRegistry`** fetches it over HTTPS
  (the `HttpClientService` idiom — JDK `java.net.http`, daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, HTTPS-only
  guard `isHttps`, per-URL cache); **`PluginInstaller`** (off-thread) does `installFromUrl` (download →
  **mandatory sha-256 verify** → unzip → move into `<pluginsDir>/<id>/` → `pm.discover()`) + `installFromZip`
  (no checksum — the user picked it); **`Unzip`** is a hardened `ZipInputStream` extractor with a
  **zip-slip guard** (`safeEntryName`/`isUnderDir`) + per-entry/total/count caps. Pure helpers
  (`compareVersions`, `isSafeId`, `sha256(byte[])`, the unzip guards) are unit-tested (`RegistryIndexTest`,
  `PluginInstallerTest`). `Settings.pluginRegistryUrl` (default `DEFAULT_PLUGIN_REGISTRY` =
  `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` raw `index.json`, overridable; schema 22→23 additive). UI: a `QuickOpen<RegistryEntry>`
  browse picker (status = Installed / Update available / Install / Requires-newer via `compareVersions` +
  `AppInfo.VERSION`), an install **confirm `Alert`** (name/version/source + trust warning), a `FileChooser`
  install-from-disk, and Settings → Plugins **Registry URL** field + **Browse / Install-from-file / per-plugin
  Remove** buttons (`SettingsWindow.setPluginActions` injected by `MainController`). Commands `plugins.browse`/
  `plugins.installFromDisk` (palette-filtered when plugins off); `MainController.onPluginInstalled` enables the
  id in `PluginStore` + `savePlugins` + `syncPluginsCheck`; `uninstallPlugin` deletes `plugins/<id>/`. **No new
  dependency** (`java.net.http` already required). **Example plugin:** the editor repo keeps a single
  in-tree reference, `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin exercising every
  extension point, with a generic `build.sh` that reads the id from `plugin.json` and emits `<id>.zip` + its
  sha) — this is the SDK example `docs/plugins.md` walks through. **The full plugin catalog (and the live,
  signed `index.json` registry) lives in the separate `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` repo** under
  `plugins/<id>/` — text/encode/hash/json tools, scratchpad, format-runner, regex-tester, markdown-toc,
  color-picker, word-count, calculator, run-task, slug-tools, open-on-github, box-banner, etc. They were
  *not* kept duplicated under `examples/` (that copy had already drifted); add or update a real plugin in the
  registry repo, not here.
  **Security:** consent + integrity + authenticity. (1) *Consent* — `MainController.confirmEnablePlugin` shows a
  **capability disclosure** (jar? declared external commands + argv? keybinding remaps? via
  `pluginCapabilitySummary`) before *enabling* at every arming point (install, install-from-file, the Settings
  per-plugin checkbox). (2) *Integrity/anti-OOM* — `PluginRegistry.readCapped` bounds the index + download
  reads; `RegistryIndex.parse` caps entry field lengths; HTTPS-only + no `https→http` downgrade; a
  non-default registry URL is flagged with its host. (3) *Authenticity* — `PluginSignature` verifies a
  detached **Ed25519** signature of `index.json` (fetched from `<url>.sig`) against a **bundled public key**
  (`resources/com/editora/plugin/editora-registry.pub`; JDK `java.security`, no dependency);
  `PluginRegistry.Result.signed` carries the verdict, and `Settings.pluginRequireSignature` (default on; schema
  23→24) makes `browsePlugins` **block** an unsigned/unverified registry. The registry owner signs with
  `scripts/PluginSigningTool.java` (keygen/sign/verify, Ed25519); the private key is never committed (the
  bundled `.pub` is). Signing proves *who* published — not a sandbox.
  *Deferred (full trust in v1, like VSCode/IntelliJ): sandboxing, hot reload, inter-plugin deps,
  GitHub-API/per-repo discovery, per-plugin/TOFU signing, auto-update, gutter-marker contributions.*
- `editorconfig/` — **EditorConfig (`.editorconfig`) support** (on by default, gated by
  `Settings.editorConfigSupport`; schema 29→30 additive-identity). Honors `root`, `indent_style`,
  `indent_size` (incl. `tab`), `tab_width`, `end_of_line` (lf/crlf/cr), `charset`
  (utf-8/utf-8-bom/latin1/utf-16le/utf-16be), `trim_trailing_whitespace`, `insert_final_newline`, and
  `max_line_length` (incl. `off`). All **pure + unit-tested** (java.base only, no dependency/moditect):
  **`EditorConfigProperties`** (record of nullable boxed fields + `OFF` sentinel + `EMPTY` +
  `merge(lower, higher)` where higher's non-null wins), **`EditorConfigParser`**
  (`parse(text)`→`Parsed{root, List<Section{glob, Map}>}` + `toProperties` typed conversion: keys/values
  lowercased, glob keeps case, `indent_size=tab`→null, `max_line_length=off`→OFF, lenient positive-int),
  **`EditorConfigGlob`** (`matches(glob, relPath)` glob→regex: prepends `**/` when no slash, `**/`→
  `(?:.*/)?`, `*`→`[^/]*`, `?`→`[^/]`, `[!`→`[^`, `{a,b}`→alternation, `{n1..n2}`→numeric alternation
  capped at `MAX_RANGE`), **`EditorConfigCharset`** (`charsetFor`/`writesBom`/`bomFor`/`detectByBom`
  (UTF-8 BOM, then UTF-16BE before LE)/`decode`/`encode`/`displayName`), and **`EditorConfigTransform`**
  (`transform(content, props)`: trim trailing + EOL-normalize + final-newline, idempotent, returns content
  unchanged when nothing is set so EOLs are preserved). The one impure class **`EditorConfig`** —
  `resolveFor(Path)` walks up dirs reading `.editorconfig` (per-file **mtime cache**), matches sections,
  merges nearest-dir-wins, stops at `root=true`; `clearCache()`. **Wiring** (`MainController`):
  `applyEditorConfig(buffer)` (gated `editorConfigEnabled() && path!=null && Vfs.isLocal`) resolves the
  chain and pushes per-buffer overrides — indent (`EditorBuffer.setIndentOverride` → `Indenter.smartTab`/
  `enterEdit` new `(Boolean insertSpaces, Integer size)` overloads, the legacy signatures delegating
  `(null,null)` so the no-`.editorconfig` path is byte-identical) — the **effective** indent is resolved by
  `MainController.applyEffectiveIndent(buffer, props)` with precedence **`.editorconfig` `indent_style` >
  global `Settings.indentStyle` (`detect`/`space`/`tab`, default `detect`; Settings → Editor "Indent style"
  combo + the `editor.setIndentStyle` palette picker via `chooseSetting`; schema 30→31 additive-identity) >
  per-file `Indenter.detectUnit`** (so the global preference applies even when EditorConfig is off / a file
  is remote / has no path — it runs in the early-return branch too; `detectUnit` reads the first indented
  line and **falls back to spaces** when the file has no indentation, matching VSCode/IntelliJ's
  "spaces unless detected as tabs" default), tab width (`setTabSize`), EOL
  (`setEolOverride`, `getLineEnding()` returns it; a manual `chooseLineEndings` change sets it so the
  user wins for the session), ruler column (`setRulerColumn`, OFF hides), charset
  (`setCharsetOverride`/`getEffectiveCharset`) — plus `setEditorConfigProps` for save time; called from
  `applyViewSettings`. `applyEditorConfigSupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`: init + every settings
  apply; off → clear overrides + cache). **Read/write are charset-aware**: `readWithCharset` does
  `Files.readAllBytes` → BOM-detect → else EditorConfig `charset` → else UTF-8, `setDetectedCharset`,
  decode (huge-file `readCapped` stays UTF-8, documented); `saveBytes` runs `EditorConfigTransform` then
  `EditorConfigCharset.encode` (BOM-prefixed when needed) — used by `writeBuffer` (`Files.write`) and
  `autoSaveBuffer` (snapshot bytes on FX, write off-thread); **disk-only** — the live document/caret/undo
  are untouched. StatusBar shows the per-buffer tab size + `EditorConfigCharset.displayName(getEffectiveCharset())`,
  plus a clickable **EditorConfig** segment (`status-editorconfig`) shown only when the active buffer's resolved
  props are non-empty (`refresh()` checks `buffer.getEditorConfigProps()`, hidden in Simple mode); its click runs
  the `editorConfig.openActive` command → `MainController.openActiveEditorConfig` → `EditorConfig.nearestFile(path)`
  (closest `.editorconfig` walking up to `root=true`) → `openPath`. Palette `view.toggleEditorConfig` (via the
  generic `toggleSetting`) + `editorConfig.openActive`; Settings → Editor "Enable
  EditorConfig" checkbox (`viewCheck` + `syncAll`/`syncViewChecks`). The repo ships its own `.editorconfig` at the
  root (Java 4-space/120-col per Palantir, JSON 2-space, shell tabs, etc.). *Deferred: per-language indent
  profiles beyond the std keys, live re-resolve on `.editorconfig` edit (currently mtime-cache-invalidated),
  remote-file support.*
- `logviewer/` — **Server log viewer** (on by default for `.log` files, gated by `Settings.logViewer`; **suppressed in Simple UI mode** via `LogViewerCoordinator.isEnabled()`). Pure, unit-tested core: **`LogLevel`** (TRACE…FATAL with a severity `rank()`; `fromToken` maps Logback/Log4j, `java.util.logging` FINEST…SEVERE, syslog, and zerolog 3-letter forms), **`LogPatterns`** (`levelOf(line)` — an UPPERCASE level token near the line start wins, else a bracketed any-case `[error]` / a `level=…`/JSON field, else an Apache/Nginx access-log status 5xx→ERROR/4xx→WARN/2xx→INFO; deliberately prose-safe so the lowercase word "error" in a message never reclassifies a line; plus `looksLikeLog`/`hasLeadingTimestamp` content sniffs), **`LogFilter`** (`filter(text, minLevel, regex, startCarry)` keeps lines passing a level floor AND regex, where an unleveled continuation/stack-trace line **inherits the previous record's level** so an exception's whole trace survives a `WARN+` filter; `effectiveLevel`/`endCarry` make incremental appends correct), and **`LogTail`** (`readTail(file, maxBytes)` opens a huge log at its **end**, dropping the partial first line; `readAppended(file, fromOffset)` reads only the delta and holds back a trailing incomplete UTF-8 sequence — the pure `completeEnd`/`firstLineStart` byte maths are unit-tested — and flags `reset` when the file shrank = rotation). **`LogTailService`** (the `GitService` daemon idiom: one `ScheduledExecutorService` poll per followed file, ~500 ms, `Platform.runLater` callbacks) drives `tail -f` via `LogTail.readAppended` and returns a `Handle` to stop it. **Highlighting is two complementary layers:** a bundled `grammars/log.tmLanguage.json` (`source.log`, ext `log`) whose `markup.error/warning/info/debug/trace.log` + `constant.other.timestamp.log` scopes map (in `TextMateHighlighter.classify`) to `.text.log-*` classes (AtlantaFX semantic colors in `syntax.css`, so no per-editor-theme override) — inline token color for logs under the 5 MB highlight cap; **plus `editor/LogHighlightOverlay`** (a coalesced, visible-lines-only `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`: a solid left-edge bar per leveled line + a faint WARN/ERROR row wash, level inheritance via a bounded upward scan, cached per line) — **size-independent**, so the huge tail-loaded logs where TextMate is off still show levels. **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the markdown-mode bolt-on: `isLog()` (language `"log"` or forced via `setLogViewForced`), a floating `setLogControl(Node)` overlaid top-right (reusing `attachControlToCodePane`, mutually exclusive with the markdown/html controls), `setLogHighlightEnabled`, `applyLogFilter(minLevel, regex)` (keeps the full text aside in `logFullText`, shows only matching lines, re-applies incrementally on append), `appendLogText`/`resetLogContent` (follow + rotation; auto-scroll to bottom while `logFollowing`; trims past a 12 MB `LOG_FOLLOW_CAP` to bound memory). **`ui/LogControlBar`** (the floating control, the `HtmlPreviewToggle` pattern): a Follow `ToggleButton` (`Icons.arrowDown()`), a minimum-level `ComboBox`, and a regex `TextField`, reporting through callbacks to **`ui/LogViewerCoordinator`** — the first *feature coordinator* extracted from `MainController` (it owns the tail service + the per-buffer follow/offset/control maps and reaches the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface — settings, active/all buffers, status, `fileSize`, `requestSave`, overlay host, prompt; `MainController` supplies an anonymous `Host` adapter and keeps one-line delegations at each call site, and a fake `Host` makes the coordinator unit-testable — see `LogViewerCoordinatorFxTest`). It owns the wiring: `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirrors `applyHtmlPreviewSupport`) (un)attaches the control + overlay on log buffers; `ensureControl` gates on `isEnabled() && isLog()`; log files **open in View mode by default** (`MainController.restoreReadOnly` adds `logViewer.isEnabled() && isLog()` — read-only with the Enable-Editing banner, since logs are for reading and follow-tail still appends programmatically while read-only); `MainController.loadInto` opens a huge `.log` at its tail (read-only, via `logViewer.handlesLogFile`/`recordLoadOffset`) instead of the first chunk; `startFollow`/`stopFollow` manage one `LogTailService.Handle` per buffer (resume from EOF on restart so a stop/start never duplicates); `applyFilter` builds the pattern via the pure `LogFilter.compileFilter` (a **case-insensitive regex**, with a **literal-substring fallback** when the query isn't valid regex — so a partial regex typed live, or a plain string with metacharacters, still filters), and the control's regex field filters **live** (debounced 300 ms) as well as on Enter. Commands `log.toggleFollow`/`log.viewAsLog`/`log.setLevelFilter`/`log.setRegexFilter`/`log.clearFilter` (palette-filtered when off via a new `log` field on `Chrome.PaletteGates`) + the master `view.toggleLogViewer`; `Settings.logViewer` (Settings → Editor → **Logs** checkbox; schema 37→38 additive-identity). Follow/tail is **local-only** (`Vfs.isLocal`); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** *Deferred: tailing remote (SFTP) logs, a multi-file merged tail, a dedicated Logs tool window, timestamp-range filtering, jump-to-next-error navigation.*
- `i18n/` — **UI localization**. `Messages` is a tiny static catalog loaded once by `App.start` (right after `config.load()`, before the command registry / FXML / UI are built) via `Messages.init(Messages.resolve(settings.getUiLanguage(), Messages.available().keySet(), Locale.getDefault().getLanguage()))`. Strings live in `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages.properties` (English **base/fallback**) plus `messages_<lang>.properties` overlays for **it/es/fr/pt/de**, read with `getResourceAsStream` + a UTF-8 `InputStreamReader` (the keymap/snippets loading style, so **no `module-info` opens** — we read our own module's resources; `ResourceBundle`'s JPMS pitfalls are avoided). `tr(key)` resolves active → English → the key itself (a missing key is visible, never throws); `tr(key, args...)` applies `MessageFormat` (e.g. `status.saved = Saved {0}`). `resolve(pref, available, systemLang)` (pure/unit-tested) picks the explicit pref if bundled, else the system language if bundled, else `en`. Bundled languages + endonyms live in `LANGUAGES` (en→English, it→Italiano, es→Español, fr→Français, pt→Português, de→Deutsch). **Command titles** come from this catalog automatically: `Command.of(id, runnable)` (the title-less overload) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id)`, so `MainController.registerCommands()` registers ids and the palette/Settings read titles fresh. **Command descriptions** work the same way: `Command.description()` (a `default` method) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id + ".desc")`, returning `""` when the key is absent (plugin/dynamic commands) so callers degrade gracefully; the command palette shows the highlighted command's description as a detail line (a `.palette-desc` `Label`) between the results list and the navigation hint, updating off the list's selection. Every `command.<id>` title has a matching `command.<id>.desc` in all six catalogs (enforced by `MessagesTest.everyCommandTitleHasAMatchingDescription`), and the website's Commands page reads the *same* `.desc` values via `website/scripts/gen-commands.py` (no separate description source). Other surfaces use explicit keys: `tooltip.*` (toolbar), `toolwindow.*` (tool-window titles), `settings.*` (the whole Settings window, incl. the language picker), `statusbar.*` (status-bar segments + tooltips), `hint.*`/`badge.*` (toolbar Switcher hint + `--dev` badge), `status.*` (the transient echo-area messages, parameterized via `MessageFormat`), `dialog.*` (every `Alert`/`TextInputDialog`/`ChoiceDialog` title/header/content + custom `ButtonType`s), `menu.*` (tab context menu), `editmenu.*` (editor right-click menu), `viewmode.*` (View-Mode banner), `find.*` (Find/Replace bar), `palette.*`/`filefinder.*`/`switcher.*` (popups), `bookmarks.*`/`project.*`/`gitpanel.*`/`branchpopup.*`/`structure.*`/`fileinfo.*` + `char.cat.*` (the tool-window panels), `markdown.*`, `autosave.*`, `branch.*`/`gitlabel.*`, `common.on`/`common.off`, `spell.lang.*`. `App.start` also calls `Locale.setDefault(...)` to the chosen language so JavaFX localizes its **own** built-in `ButtonType.OK/CANCEL/YES/NO` and locale-sensitive controls to match. The picker is a `ComboBox` at the top of Settings → Appearance (`Settings.uiLanguage`, default `""` = Automatic); changing it saves + shows a "restart to apply" `Alert` (set-once chrome is fully relabeled on the next launch). `MessagesTest` enforces **key-parity** — every bundled locale must have exactly the base's key set — so translations can't drift; add a language by dropping a complete `messages_<lang>.properties` + a `LANGUAGES` entry. Essentially **all** user-facing strings are now externalized — command palette, toolbar tooltips, tool-window titles + panel contents, Settings, status-bar segments, status/echo messages, every dialog (title/header/body/buttons), context menus, and popups. The only deliberately-untranslated tokens are technical identifiers (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, the detected language name, an example clone URL).
- **Command line** — `App.main` intercepts `--version`/`-V` and `--help`/`-h` (print via `AppInfo` + `helpText` and exit, before `launch()`, so no GUI). `App.start` parses the rest (pure/unit-tested helpers `configDirArg`/`projectArg`/`zenFlag`/`simpleFlag`/`fileTargets`/`parseTarget`/`newFileArg`/`singleWindowArg`) and calls `MainController.startup(projectDir, List<OpenTarget>, zen, newFile, simple)` instead of `openInitialBuffer()`: it activates a CLI `--project` (only if `projectsEnabled()`), restores the session, then — via a one-shot `pendingAfterRestore` run when the deferred session restore completes — opens any `--new-file[=name]` buffer, the `FILE[:line[:col]]` targets (additive, focused, `gotoInFile`), and toggles Zen / Simple UI mode. **`--simple`** is a *session-only* Simple-UI override (sets a transient `cliSimpleOverride`, OR'd with the saved `Settings.simpleMode` in `simpleModeActive()`); it doesn't change the saved preference, mirroring how `--zen` is session-scoped. **`--single-window[=name]`** opens exactly one window at startup instead of restoring the saved multi-window set — the named project's window, else the no-project window (an unknown name → no-project, with a logged warning); it's **session-only** (`WindowManager.launchSingleWindow` skips `markOpen`/`pm.save()`/the orphan-GC, and the `singleWindowSession` flag makes `reconcileOpenSet()` a no-op), so the persisted open-window layout is untouched and the next normal launch restores everything. `singleWindowArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` (bare → no-project) / project-name, like `newFileArg`. **Welcome page**: when there are no files to restore (and no CLI `--new-file`/`FILE` target opened anything), `openInitialBuffer` no longer creates an empty Untitled buffer — it opens the Welcome page in its own tab via `showWelcomeIfNoTabs()`→`addWelcomeTab()` (see `ui/`). `newFileArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` / name; `--new-file` ⇒ blank untitled, `--new-file=foo.md` ⇒ an unsaved buffer via `EditorBuffer.setDisplayName(name)` (tab title + extension highlighting, `path` stays null so Save prompts Save-As, the dialog's initial name defaulting to `getDisplayName()`). `AppInfo` (NAME/VERSION/HOMEPAGE/COPYRIGHT/LICENSE/buildTime) is the single source for `--version`, the About dialog, and the Welcome footer — **`VERSION` itself derives from `pom.xml`'s `<version>`** (Maven-filtered into `build-info.properties` alongside `build.time` and read via `AppInfo.loadVersion()`, falling back to `"0.0.0"` on an unfiltered non-Maven run), so **a release bump touches only the pom**, never a hardcoded constant — all of which show the home-page link (opened via `HostServices`), copyright, and license. `AppInfo.gitCommit()` adds the **short git commit** (read once at runtime via `git rev-parse --short HEAD`, cached, `""` when unavailable); it's shown in the About dialog and the Welcome footer **only under `--dev`** (`config.isDev() ? AppInfo.gitCommit() : ""` — passed to `SettingsWindow.showAbout(..., commit)` and `new WelcomePane(..., devCommit)`, each rendering the `about.commit` line only when non-blank), so a dev build can tell at a glance which commit it's running. Production builds pass `""` (nothing shown). **macOS "Open With" (Finder file associations):** the packaged `Editora.app` declares `CFBundleDocumentTypes` in its Info.plist so Editora shows up in Finder's *Open With* menu for text/source files. **Wiring is macOS-only + two-part:** (1) **`scripts/aot_build.java`'s `fixMacDocumentTypes`** (run on the macOS app image before the APP_IMAGE copy / DMG wrap) writes `CFBundleDocumentTypes` via `PlistBuddy` — a single entry declaring the **system UTIs `public.text` + `public.source-code`** (role `Editor`, `LSHandlerRank=Alternate` so it doesn't steal the default). **Deliberately NOT jpackage `--file-associations`:** that emits per-extension *custom* UTIs (`com.editora.txt`, …) conforming to `public.data`, which **don't work** — Launch Services never offers the app for a file already typed as a system UTI (a `.txt` is `public.plain-text`, which doesn't conform to `com.editora.txt`), so it wouldn't appear in Open With at all. Declaring the *system* types works because **every** text/source file's UTI **conforms to** `public.text`/`public.source-code`, making Editora an eligible alternate editor for all of them (verified via `lsregister -dump` → `bindings: public.text, public.source-code`). (`fixMacDocumentTypes` first `Delete`s any pre-existing `UT*TypeDeclarations`/`CFBundleDocumentTypes`, tolerating absence; it's a no-op on non-mac and best-effort — a PlistBuddy failure logs and the app still runs, just without the association.) **Two signing gotchas the plist edit exposes, both fixed in `aot_build.java`:** (a) jpackage **ad-hoc-signs** the `.app` during the app-image build, so editing `Info.plist` afterward **invalidates the code-signature seal** (the plist's hash is sealed) — macOS then rejects the app as *tampered* (`spctl`: "invalid Info.plist … modified"; the Finder dialog says it "could not verify … free of malware" with only *Move to Trash*/*Done*, a hard block). So `fixMacDocumentTypes` **re-runs `codesign --force --deep --sign -`** on the bundle after the edit to re-seal it (arm64 needs *some* signature to run; ad-hoc is fine for a locally-built, un-notarized app). (b) The APP_IMAGE-delivery `copyRecursive` **must preserve symlinks** (`Files.isSymbolicLink` → `createSymbolicLink`, not follow-and-copy): the jlink runtime dedups its `legal/*` license files as symlinks, and turning them into regular files breaks the seal in the *delivered* copy (`spctl`: "sealed resource … invalid: file modified: …/legal/…"; the DMG path is unaffected — jpackage does its own symlink-preserving copy). *(A validly ad-hoc-signed local app still shows `spctl -a -t exec: rejected` — that only means "not notarized"; a non-quarantined local app launches fine regardless. Full **notarization** (Apple Developer ID) is the outstanding follow-up for shipping downloadable installers.)* (2) Finder delivers the opened path as an AppKit **`openFiles` Apple Event, not argv**, so the `fileTargets` argv path never sees it — `App.start` (gated to macOS, after the windows build) calls **`MacOpenFiles.install(windows)`**, which sets a Glass `com.sun.glass.ui.Application.EventHandler` (`MacOpenFiles.Handler`) that forwards `handleOpenFilesAction` to `WindowManager.openExternalFiles(List<Path>)` → the focused window's `MainController.openExternalFiles` (each path `openPath`-ed; a cold-launch's buffered event lands in the just-built window). `Handler` **wraps** JavaFX's own handler (delegates every other event — quit/activate/preferences/… — to it) so Cmd-Q etc. still work; everything is `try/catch(Throwable)` so a missing internal API never breaks launch. **The handler is a standalone top-level class `com.editora.MacOpenFiles`, deliberately *not* nested in `App`:** the JavaFX launcher reflects over the `App` main class to find its methods, which eagerly loads `App`'s **nest members** — so a `com.sun.glass.ui` subclass nested in `App` gets class-loaded (and access-checked) *before* `start()` runs, **outside** any `try/catch`, and a missing `--add-exports` there is a hard launch crash (`IllegalAccessError` in `LauncherImpl`). As a separate class it loads only inside `install()`'s guarded body, so it degrades to a logged no-op instead. The internal `com.sun.glass.ui` access needs `--add-exports javafx.graphics/com.sun.glass.ui=com.editora` in **four** places: the **compiler** args (main-compile-scoped), the **`javafx:run`** options, the **dist jpackage `<javaOptions>`**, **and the AOT-training command in `scripts/aot_build.java`** (it launches the image's own `bin/java` with a hand-built option list that must mirror the launcher, else training crashes loading `MacOpenFiles.Handler` and ships no cache). `java.awt.Desktop.setOpenFileHandler` can't be used because `App.main` forces `java.awt.headless=true` (the SVG guard). **Windows/Linux need no handler** — their file associations pass the path as argv, already handled by `fileTargets` (associations there are an installer-time feature and aren't wired yet — a future add). To appear, the built app must be registered with Launch Services (drag `Editora.app` to `/Applications`, or `lsregister -f`).
- `config/` — `ConfigManager` loads/merges/saves config in the config dir, chosen by precedence **`--config-dir <path>` CLI arg (parsed by `App.configDirArg`, pure/unit-tested) > `EDITORA_CONFIG_DIR` env var > `--dev` (`~/.editora-dev/`, the `App.devFlag` flag — a separate dev config so a development instance can't disturb production; future home for extra dev-only behavior like more logging) > `~/.editora/`** (`user.home` is the user profile on every OS); the env/default fallback is the unit-tested pure `ConfigManager.resolveConfigDir(editoraHome, userHome, dev)`. Falls back to defaults on malformed input. **Preferences** (`Settings` POJO: font, theme, keymap, tab size, view options, keybindings) are **TOML** in `settings.toml` via a Jackson `TomlMapper` (jackson-dataformat-toml). **Text zoom** is `Settings.fontZoom` (1.0 = 100%) — a persisted Settings field deliberately *not* shown in the Settings window; `MainController.applyViewSettings` applies the effective size `round(fontSize*fontZoom)` to every buffer, `textZoom(±1/0)` adjusts it (status-bar `−/+`, `C-=`/`C--`/`C-0`, and the scene-level `Ctrl`+mouse-wheel filter in `App`). That wheel filter routes through `MainController.zoomFromWheel`, which zooms the Markdown **preview** (`markdownZoom`) when the active buffer is in **PREVIEW** mode (`getMarkdownViewMode() == PREVIEW`) and otherwise the editor text (Editor/Split always zoom text). **Session state** (`WorkspaceState` POJO: collapsed fold regions, tool-window layout/visibility/dividers) stays **JSON** in `workspace-state.json`, and `RecentFiles` stays JSON in `recent-files.json`; `config.save()` writes both files. **Writes go off the FX thread** via `config/ConfigWriter` (one `config-writer` daemon thread): the caller serializes a consistent snapshot to bytes on the FX thread (single-threaded → no locking) and hands the immutable bytes to the writer, which writes each file via a temp-file + atomic move (no half-written config on a crash), **coalescing per file (latest wins) and ordered through the one thread**. The frequent, coalesced in-session save (`MainController.requestSave` → `config.saveAsync()`) is non-blocking; durable saves (`config.save()` — used by `persistSession()` on quit, one-off actions, and `exportConfig()`) `enqueue` + `flush()` (block until written), and `App.start` registers a JVM-shutdown flush. settings.toml + workspace-state.json are the only files with both an async and a sync writer, and both funnel through the one writer queue, so a stale async write can never land after and clobber a durable one (the other stores — `bookmarks.json`/`notes.json`/… — keep their direct synchronous `writeValue`). **Bookmarks** are deliberately *not* in `WorkspaceState` — they're in their own `bookmarks.json` (`BookmarkStore`), written by `config.saveBookmarks()` (independent of `save()`), but **scoped per project** (bucketed by project key; `config.getBookmarks()` returns the active project's bucket). See the bookmarks paragraph in `editor/` for the per-project model and the one-time migration out of the legacy session files. Both POJOs are `@JsonIgnoreProperties(ignoreUnknown = true)`, so `save()` rewrites with only modeled fields. The switch to TOML was a clean cut — a pre-existing `settings.json` is not migrated. (The bundled keymap `emacs.json` and the TextMate grammars stay JSON — they're app resources, not user config.) The About dialog shows the live settings path via `ConfigManager.getSettingsFile()` — don't hardcode it. **Export config**: `ConfigManager.exportConfig()` zips the *active* config dir into a timestamped `.zip` in the user's home (`~/editora[-dev]-config-<version>-<user>-<yyyy-MM-dd_HHmmss>.zip`, embedding `AppInfo.VERSION` + `user.name`, both filename-sanitized) via the pure, unit-tested `ConfigExporter` (`zipName`/`sanitize` + `export(configDir, destDir, version, userName, now)`); surfaced as the Settings → Advanced "Export Configuration…" button (wired via the `onExportConfig` `Runnable` ctor arg → `MainController.exportConfig`, which shows the result path in a dialog) and the `config.export` command. **Projects** (`ProjectManager`, index in `projects.json`) are named single-folder workspaces; each project's session is a separate `WorkspaceState` JSON under `projects/<id>.json`. **Multi-window config split:** the config is split into a **`SharedConfig`** — the app-wide state (the `Settings` object, the bookmark/note/breakpoint/connection stores, the user dictionary, and the `ProjectManager` index) held **by reference** across every window — and a per-window **`ConfigManager`** that owns only that window's session (`WorkspaceState` + its `workspaceStateFile`) and delegates everything shared to `SharedConfig`. So a `config.save()` from any window writes `settings.toml` + that window's session file without clobbering another window's in-memory copy, and `config.getBookmarks()/getNotes()/getBreakpoints()` return the bucket for *this* window's project (keyed off its session file). `ConfigManager.setWorkspaceStateFile(...)` picks a window's session file (default = `workspace-state.json` for the no-project/global window). **Each project opens in its own window** (see `ui/WindowManager`); the open-window set is tracked in `ProjectManager.Index.openProjectIds` (`""` = the global window) — `markOpen`/`markClosed`/`isOpen` — and restored on the next launch, with `activeProjectId` as the last-focused window. `ProjectManager.Index` schema is **2** (v1→v2 `ConfigMigrations.seedOpenProjectIds` seeds `openProjectIds` from the old single `activeProjectId` so a pre-multi-window install reopens its active project as a window). **Schema versioning + migrations** (`config/migration/`): every structured config file carries a per-file integer `schemaVersion` (baseline **1**; the owning POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` constant — `Settings`/`WorkspaceState`/`BookmarkStore`/`ProjectManager.Index`, and `RecentFiles`), enumerated in `ConfigSchema` (SETTINGS/WORKSPACE/BOOKMARKS/PROJECTS/RECENT) with its current version, the version assumed when the field is absent (=1, the pre-versioning baseline), and an ordered map of `v→v+1` step `Migration`s. All structured reads now go through **`ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(file, mapper, defaults, schema)`**: parse to a Jackson tree → `upgrade` (apply the migration chain via `applySteps`, stamp `schemaVersion`) → merge onto defaults. It's mapper-agnostic (works for TOML + JSON since `TomlMapper` yields ordinary nodes). A file **newer** than this build (`schemaVersion > current`) throws `NewerThanSupportedException` and is **backed up to `<name>.v<n>.bak`, then defaults are loaded** — an older Editora never clobbers a newer config. `recent-files.json` was a bare JSON array (v0); the registered RECENT `0→1` step (`wrapRecentFilesArray`) wraps it into `{schemaVersion,files}` (`RecentFiles.Stored`). **To add a migration later: bump the POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` and add one `v→v+1` entry to that file's `steps` map in `ConfigSchema` — the read path, stamping, and downgrade backup are automatic.** The older one-off `migrateLegacyBookmarks()` (bookmarks flat→bucketed) stays as orthogonal field-level back-compat and runs before the versioned read.
- `ui/` — `MainController` (+ `main.fxml`): toolbar, tabbed `EditorBuffer`s, status bar. **Multiple windows (`WindowManager`)**: each window has its own `MainController`/`Stage`/`CommandRegistry`/`KeyDispatcher` + per-window services (all already per-instance, so no static per-window state) over the shared `SharedConfig`/`KeymapManager`. **`ui/WindowManager`** (created once in `App.start`) owns the set of open windows: `buildWindow(...)` is the per-window construction extracted from `App.start`; `openOrFocus(project)` focuses an already-open project window or builds a new one; `openOrFocusGlobal()` is the no-project window; `newWindow()` always **builds** a fresh no-project window (the palette **`window.new`** command / `C-x 5 2` — so a second window no longer requires loading a project; works regardless of the Projects feature). Each such window gets a unique **`untitled:<uuid>`** key and its **own** session file `windows/<uuid>.json` (so windows never clobber each other's open-files/layout — they are *not* all keyed `""`), is tracked in `openProjectIds` like a project window, and is **restored on the next launch regardless of the Projects feature** — the no-project windows (`""` + `untitled:*`) always restore; only saved *project* ids are dropped when Projects are off. `launch` dispatches a restore key by prefix (`""`→global/`workspace-state.json`, `untitled:`→`untitledStateFile`, else a project id) and `gcOrphanWindowSessions(toOpen)` deletes `windows/*.json` for untitled windows closed in a previous session. **Bucket:** an untitled window shares the global no-project bookmark/note bucket `""` — its `windows/<uuid>.json` session isn't under `projects/`, and `ConfigManager.currentBookmarkKey` returns `""` for anything not directly under `projects/` (only `projects/<id>.json` gets its own bucket). `launch(...)` restores the previously-open window set on startup: with Projects **disabled** that's the global window plus any untitled "New Window"s (the default stays single-window until you open one); with Projects **enabled** it's every previously-open window. A new window is **cascaded** (offset + brought to front, un-maximized if secondary) so it doesn't stack exactly on an existing one (projects carried identical saved bounds from the single-window era). `MainController.setWindowContext(wm, project)` (called right after `init`, before `startup`) binds the window to its project — sets the panel root/title/combo and auto-opens the Projects tool window — so the combo shows *this* window's project (a window switcher, not an in-place swap). **Window title** (`MainController.updateWindowTitle`): the active file's home-collapsed path with a `•` unsaved marker, then the project, then `Editora` (e.g. `~/app/Main.java — MyProject — Editora`); an untitled buffer shows its display name, a non-file/Welcome tab shows just the project/app name. Refreshed on tab switch (the selection listener) and on dirty-flip / Save-As / rename (via `updateTabMeta`, guarded to the active tab). **Current-folder mode:** in the **global ("No Project") window** the Project tool window doesn't sit empty — `MainController.updateProjectFolderView()` (called from the tab-selection listener, `setWindowContext`, and after a Save-As) roots `ProjectPanel` at the **active file's parent dir** and retitles the tool window **"Current Folder"** (`toolwindow.currentFolder`), so it tracks the focused tab like a file explorer. It no-ops when a project is open (tree stays the project root, title "Project") or while a remote folder is mounted (`activeRemoteAuthority != null` — that root is set explicitly); an unsaved/Welcome tab (or remote file) shows the placeholder + default title. Deduped against `ProjectPanel.getRoot()` so switching files in the same folder doesn't rebuild the tree. The retitle works because `ToolWindow`'s title is now a `StringProperty` the `ToolWindowPanel` header `Label` binds to. `switchToProject`→`openOrFocus`; `closeProject` closes this window; `deleteProject` closes the project's window first; the per-window close handler persists the session, **disposes that window's services** (LSP/DAP/git/search/mermaid/pdf/print/run/autosave + buffers, in a defensive `try/catch`), and notifies `WindowManager.onWindowClosed` (no per-window "Quit?" prompt; `app.quit`/`C-x C-c`/last-window-close still `Platform.exit`). A Settings change in one window broadcasts to all via `WindowManager.broadcastSettingsApplied` → each window's `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange`. *Window restore:* the open-window set persisted in `projects.json` (`openProjectIds`) is reconciled to the live set by a **debounced** `WindowManager.openSetReconcile` `PauseTransition` (~350 ms → `reconcileOpenSet()`; not an eager per-close `markClosed`): a genuine single-window close (the app keeps running) outlives the debounce, which then persists the reduced live set, so the closed window is forgotten; a **quit** terminates the JVM before the timer elapses, so the reduced set is never written and the full pre-quit set stays on disk ⇒ **every** window reopens next launch. The debounce delay (rather than a plain `runLater`) is deliberate: it can't elapse inside a quit's close-handler burst, so it never persists a half-drained intermediate even if those close events interleave with the FX event queue. This covers both quit paths — Cmd-Q / OS quit fire every window's close handler in a fast burst, and `app.quit`'s `Platform.exit` fires none at all. `reconcileOpenSet` also guards an empty live set (persist nothing). `ProjectManager.setOpenWindows(keys)` replaces the whole set (deduped, `null`→`""`). (Earlier this used a "remain" rule — eager `markClosed` unless it was the last window — which drained a Cmd-Q down to only the last window.) **Tab content abstraction**: a tab's `userData` is no longer always an `EditorBuffer` — it's a `editor/TabContent` (`node()`/`title()`/`icon()`/`closeable()`; lives in `com.editora.editor` so `EditorBuffer` can implement it without the editor package depending on `ui`, the same independence the completion popup keeps). `EditorBuffer` and `WelcomePane` both implement it, so the Welcome page is a **real tab** (and future diff/image/help views can be too). **Image viewer**: `ui/ImageViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** raster-image tab — opening a `.png`/`.jpg`/`.jpeg`/`.gif`/`.bmp` renders the picture instead of showing its binary bytes as text (the pure/unit-tested `ui/ImageFormats.isSupported(name)` gates which extensions route here; SVG is deliberately excluded — it's editable XML). It decodes the file's bytes (`Files.readAllBytes`, so it works for local **and** remote/SFTP paths; refused above a 64 MB cap) into a JavaFX `Image`, shows a top bar with zoom out/in/fit/actual-size + a read-only badge (Ctrl+wheel zooms; fit-mode never upscales past 100%; small images center, large scroll), and `dispose()`s the decoded `Image` on tab close (releasing its Prism texture — the per-buffer VRAM-bounding rule). `MainController.openPath` routes an image file to `openImageTab(file, select)` before the text path; `imagePaneOf(Tab)` + `tabPath(Tab)` (buffer path else image-pane path) generalize the buffer-only lookups, so image tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (restored via `openImageTab`, a `null` placeholder in the `buffers` list keeps indices aligned — the `buffers.get(i)` reads are null-guarded) and show their path in the window title. i18n `imageviewer.*`; CSS `.image-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **Hex viewer**: `ui/HexViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** hex tab for **binary** files — an executable/archive/`.class`/`.pdf` opens as the classic `offset | hex | ASCII` dump (pure/unit-tested `ui/HexDump.format(bytes, baseOffset)`, 16 bytes/row) instead of dumping its bytes as garbage text. **Binary detection** is by content, not extension: pure/unit-tested `ui/BinarySniff.looksBinary(sample)` (git's rule — a NUL byte ⇒ binary — plus a control-char density fallback, with a **BOM guard** so BOM'd UTF-16/UTF-8 text isn't misrouted, and bytes ≥0x80 aren't counted so UTF-8/Latin-1 prose stays text); `MainController.looksBinaryFile(path)` reads a bounded `BinarySniff.SAMPLE_BYTES` prefix. The dump sits in a read-only monospace RichTextFX `CodeArea` (selectable/copyable), reads up to `MAX_DISPLAY_BYTES` (1 MiB → a large binary shows its first slice with a truncation note, so a multi-GB file can't exhaust memory), and `dispose()`s the text on close. `openPath` routes a binary to `openHexTab(file, select)` **after** the image check + before the text load; `hexPaneOf(Tab)` joins `imagePaneOf` in `tabPath(Tab)`, so hex tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (a `null` `buffers` placeholder, like images) and show their path in the title. Palette command **`view.openAsHex`** force-opens the active file's bytes as hex (works for a text file too). i18n `hexviewer.*`/`command.view.openAsHex`; CSS `.hex-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **Every** `tab.getUserData()` read goes through `bufferOf(Tab)` (returns the `EditorBuffer`, or `null` for a non-buffer tab via `instanceof` — a raw cast would `ClassCastException` on the Welcome tab); `activeBuffer()` delegates to it. `addContentTab(TabContent, select)` is the generic tab factory (sets content/userData/close-request, appends, optionally selects+focuses) and builds a **draggable graphic header** (icon + title `Label`, `enableTabDrag`) — so non-buffer tabs (Welcome) reorder like any other tab; the tab text is left empty, so the Switcher/pickers read the title via `TabContent.title()` (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle`). `addBuffer` calls it then overrides the header via `updateTabMeta` (drag handle, pin, dirty); buffer-only ops (pin, save, edit commands) are inert on the Welcome tab because `bufferOf`/`activeBuffer` yield null and the tab-switch consumers (status bar, Structure, File-Info, breadcrumb, git, external-change) are null-safe. **Welcome page**: `setupWelcome()` just builds the `WelcomePane` + wires its callbacks; `addWelcomeTab()` opens (or re-selects) the single Welcome tab — held in a `Tab welcomeTab` field, cleared in its `onClosed`, with a Close-only context menu; its title (`welcome.tab`) comes from `WelcomePane.title()` — shown in the draggable header and read by the Switcher/pickers (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle` use `TabContent.title()` for non-buffer tabs). Shown at startup with no session (`showWelcomeIfNoTabs`, run after CLI targets) and by the `view.welcome` command (`showWelcome`). Closing the last tab leaves the editor **empty** (VSCode-like — not auto-recreated). **Buffer disposal on close**: the `tabPane.getTabs()` `ListChangeListener` (which already drops closed tabs from `mru`/`pinned`, skipping pin/drag reorders via the `reordering` guard) calls `EditorBuffer.dispose()` on each removed buffer tab — `shutdownNow()` on the buffer's two daemon executors (`markdown-preview` + `editor-highlighter`) + `unsubscribePreview()` — so those threads don't accumulate one pair per opened file. It runs for every real close path (close, close-others/left/right, deleted-file removal, Welcome) but never on a tab switch (selection change doesn't mutate the tabs list); the split secondary view shares the buffer's executors, so one `dispose()` covers it. `WelcomePane` reuses commands (`file.new`/`file.open`/`project.open`/`git.clone`/`palette.show` — `project.open`/`git.clone` gated by `projectsEnabled()`/`gitEnabled()`, `palette.show` listed last) each labelled with its keybinding via a `KeymapManager.bindings()` reverse-lookup (`shortcutFor` — Open File deliberately shows `file.find`'s `C-x C-f`) + the `RecentFiles` list (open via `openRecent`), and a footer with `AppInfo.VERSION` + a home-page link (`AppInfo.HOMEPAGE`, opened via `App`'s `HostServices` passed through `MainController.setHostServices`/`openExternalUrl`) + `AppInfo.LICENSE` (the welcome shows the license only; the author/copyright lives in About); rebuilt on each `refresh()` (also on settings apply while the Welcome tab is open, so Open-Folder/Clone track the Projects/Git toggles); styled `.welcome-*` in `app.css`. The content sits in a `ScrollPane` (`.welcome-scroll`) over a centering `StackPane` (fit-to-width, with a min width) so it stays centered but shows a vertical/horizontal scrollbar when it doesn't fit the window. **In-scene overlays (`OverlayHost`)**: the command palette and *every* keyboard picker/popup are **in-scene overlays**, **not** `javafx.stage.Popup`s — a Popup is a separate native window that on Windows doesn't reliably take OS keyboard focus, so `input.requestFocus()` orphaned focus between the popup's scene and the main window and the keyboard went dead app-wide (mouse still worked). A single shared **`ui/OverlayHost`** (owned by `MainController`, `install(sceneRoot)`-ed into the scene-root `StackPane` from `installZenOverlay`) renders one "card" node at a time over a dim, click-to-dismiss backdrop (`.overlay-backdrop`); it owns focus capture/restore (returns typing to the editor on close), `Esc`/`C-g` dismissal, a `justHidden()` toggle guard, and `showingProperty()`. `show(content, onShown, onHidden)` centers the card near the top; `show(content, anchor, onShown, onHidden)` instead positions it just **above** an anchor node (e.g. a status-bar segment, so a dropdown "drops" from it). Each component supplies its card node (which sets `editora.ownsKeys` so its `C-n`/`C-p`/arrow nav isn't hijacked by the global dispatcher), an `onShown` hook (`input.requestFocus()`), and an `onHidden` hook (clears its own `showing` flag); `MainController.wireOverlayHost()` injects the host into all of them via `setOverlayHost(...)` (on-demand pickers — LSP references, spell/app/editor-theme — get it at their construction site; `MessageLogPopup` via `StatusBar.setOverlayHost`). Converted: `CommandPalette` (M-x; the footer legend lists `esc`/`C-g`, no separator above it), the generic `QuickOpen<T>` pickers (recent files, structure, open files, tool windows, bookmarks, notes/notes-search, snippets, projects, LSP references, themes), `FileFinder` (file + folder finders), `Switcher` (IntelliJ Ctrl-Tab), the Git `BranchPopup` (anchored), and `MessageLogPopup` (anchored). When a card is anchored to a status-bar segment, the full-scene backdrop intercepts a re-click on that segment (closes the overlay, doesn't reach the segment) — a clean click-to-toggle. (`editor/CompletionPopup` stays a `Popup` — it never calls `requestFocus()`, so it's safe.) `FindReplaceBar` (find/replace with case + regex) was already in-scene the same way. **Input dialogs** are also in-scene via **`ui/OverlayInput`** — a stateless helper that builds a form card (title + caller-supplied body + footer Cancel/OK, optional left-aligned Delete `Extra`, optional `okEnabled` validity gate) and shows it through the same `OverlayHost`; the card sets `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` cancel (host), and `Enter` accepts (or `Ctrl/Cmd+Enter` when `ctrlEnterToSubmit` for the multi-line note editor). `onAccept` runs **after** the card hides (focus already back in the editor) — flows are callback-driven, no blocking `showAndWait`. `MainController.promptText(title,label,initial,onAccept)` is the single-line convenience (installs `TextInputKeymap` for Emacs caret nav) and doubles as the `OverlayInput.Prompt` functional interface injected into `BookmarksPanel`/`ProjectPanel` (`setPrompt`) so those tool windows prompt without needing the host/keymap. Converted off native `TextInputDialog`/`Dialog`: the Personal Note editor (`showNoteDialog`, multi-line + Delete), bookmark-note edit, file rename (tab + project tree), Git **clone** (two fields + Browse + validity gate) and **new branch**, **go to line**, and **Save As from the command palette / a keybinding** (`saveAsPrompt` — a path prompt pre-filled with the current path, or the project folder + suggested name for an untitled buffer; a bare name resolves against that folder and `~` expands, via the pure/unit-tested `config/PathKeys.resolveUserInput`; overwriting a different existing file still uses a native confirm `Alert`). The **toolbar Save-As button keeps the native `FileChooser`** (its FXML `onAction="#onSaveAs"`, a mouse action) — only the `file.saveAs` command routes to the in-scene prompt, so keyboard = prompt, mouse = chooser. Deliberately left **native**: simple `Alert` confirmations (overwrite/delete/external-change) and the `ChoiceDialog` selectors (set language / tab size / line endings) + the `i18n` key `dialog.ok`. **Status-bar message log**: every echo-area message set via `MainController.setStatus`→`StatusBar.setMessage` is recorded (non-blank only) in an in-memory, **session-only** `MessageLog` (pure model, capped at `MAX_ENTRIES`=200, oldest evicted, newest-first `entries()`; unit-tested). The echo label is clickable (`view.messageLog` command) → `StatusBar.showMessageLog()` → `MessageLogPopup.toggle` (a second click on the echo **closes** it — the backdrop intercepts it; a `lastHiddenAt` guard absorbs the close-then-click race) → a `MessageLogPopup` (an `OverlayHost`-anchored scrollable `ListView` above the echo; each row an `HH:mm:ss` time indicator + the message; long messages **wrap** (the row grows in height — no horizontal scrollbar, the row width is bound to the list viewport). Rows are **multi-selectable**; a footer **Copy** button copies the selected messages (or all when none are selected, joined by newline — `⌘/Ctrl+C` also works) and a **Clear** action empties the log; Esc / `C-g` / `M-g` close it. (The popup is sized 552×280 — 20% wider than the original — and has no per-row right-click menu; the Copy button replaced it for discoverability.) Not persisted. Styled `.message-log*` in `app.css`. **Debug Log** (distinct from the echo MessageLog): `ui/DebugLog` is a static capture of the app's **`java.util.logging`** output + **uncaught exceptions** — installed in `App.main` (`DebugLog.install()`: a root-logger `Handler` at `Level.ALL` appending to a bounded ring buffer + `Thread.setDefaultUncaughtExceptionHandler`) so a packaged build (DMG/MSI/DEB, no visible stderr) can still surface errors; `App.start` calls `DebugLog.attachFile(config.getConfigDir())` to also mirror records to `editora-session.log` (truncated per session) so they survive a crash for a bug report. `ui/DebugLogWindow` shows the buffer in a read-only monospace `TextArea` (Refresh/Copy/Clear/Export…), opened by the `view.debugLog` command and the **Settings → Advanced → "Show Debug Log…"** button (wired via the `onShowDebugLog` `Runnable` ctor arg → `MainController.showDebugLog`). Pure helpers (`shortName`, the bounded `append`, `format`) are unit-tested. **Unsaved-file indicator consistency**: every surface that lists open buffers shows the same dirty marker as the tab strip (a `• ` prefix + amber-italic `.dirty-name` in `app.css`): the **Switcher** (its cell checks `buffer.isDirty()`), the **Open Files** picker (`buffer.jump` — its label adds the `• ` and `QuickOpen.setItemStyleClass(tab -> isTabDirty(tab) ? "dirty-name" : null)` colors it; the `searchKey` stays the plain name), and the **Project tool window** tree (the pre-existing `.modified-file` cell class, refreshed via `projectPanel.refreshModified()` on every dirty-flag change). **Git file coloring (IntelliJ-style):** the Project tree colors each file by its Git working-tree status — added = green, modified = blue, deleted = gray, renamed = violet, untracked = olive, and a folder containing changed descendants is tinted blue. The pure/unit-tested **`git/GitFileStatus`** enum (`of(FileEntry)` classifies porcelain-v2 index/worktree letters — deleted→renamed→added→modified precedence, untracked first; `byPath(GitStatus, root)` → `Map<Path, GitFileStatus>` keyed by absolute-normalized path) drives it; `GitCoordinator.applyState` pushes the map (or empty on non-repo / Git-off) via `Ops.setProjectGitStatus` → `MainController` → `ProjectPanel.setGitStatus`, which stores it + derives the set of changed ancestor dirs and `tree.refresh()`es. The `PathCell` adds the status's `.git-status-*` class (or `.git-status-dir-changed` on a folder) — but an **unsaved (`.modified-file`) file keeps its amber marker, which takes precedence**. Colors ride the Git feature (updated on the same tab-switch / focus / save / mutation cadence as the gutter change bars); no separate setting/command. CSS `.project-tree .git-status-*` in `app.css` (semantic `-color-accent-fg`/`-color-success-fg` + fixed olive/violet). **Project-tree Git actions** (the cell right-click **Git** submenu, `ProjectPanel.FileActions`): files offer **Stage** / **Unstage** / **Revert…** / **Add to .gitignore** + **Compare with HEAD** / **Compare with Branch…** / **Compare with Revision…** / **Annotate** / **Show File History**; folders offer **Stage** / **Revert…** of the whole subtree. The path-based ops live in `GitCoordinator` (`gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`, all repo-relative via `rel(...)` and refreshing through `afterMutation()`): Revert reuses the confirming `discardChanges` (untracked → `git clean`, else `git checkout`, deciding via the stored `lastStatusByPath`); Add-to-.gitignore appends the pure/unit-tested `git/GitIgnore.entryFor`/`withEntry` line to the repo-root `.gitignore`. The three navigation/inspection actions delegate to path-based entry points: **Compare with Branch** → `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsBranch(path)` (a `QuickOpen<String>` over `GitService.branches` local+remote, diffing working ↔ `<branch>:rel`), **Compare with Revision** → `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsCommit(path)` (the path-based extraction of `diffActiveVsCommit`, a commit picker over the file's log — `diffActiveVsCommit` now delegates to it), and **Annotate** → open the file + `GitCoordinator.annotateActive()` (enables inline blame if off, then `applyBlame`). The menu items enable/disable off `ProjectPanel`'s own `gitStatus`/`gitChangedDirs` (Revert only when the file/folder has changes; Add-to-.gitignore only for untracked), and the whole Git submenu greys out with no VCS (`FileActions.gitAvailable`). **The editor tab's right-click menu mirrors this same Git submenu** (`MainController.installTabMenu`), acting on *that tab's* file (`buffer.getPath()`) via the same path-based ops (`GitCoordinator.gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`/`annotateActive`, `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVs{Head,Branch,Commit}`, `gitFileHistoryForPath`) and the same `project.menu.git.*` labels; `GitCoordinator.statusFor(path)` gates **Revert** (only when the file has changes) / **Add to .gitignore** (untracked only), the submenu is hidden for an untitled buffer and greyed out with no VCS. The pre-existing tab **"Compare With…"** (any two files) + **"Open in Diff Viewer"** (`.patch`/`.diff`) stay *outside* the submenu — they aren't Git ops. **Project tree filesystem refresh**: `ProjectPanel.refreshTree()` re-scans the tree against disk (files/folders added/removed outside Editora) while **preserving the expanded folders + selection** (it collects expanded paths, `reload()`s only the expanded directories, re-expands by path, restores the selection) — no-op while filtering/no project; called on window focus-regain (alongside `checkExternalChanges`/`refreshGit`) **and by a filesystem watcher**. **Live filesystem watcher**: `ProjectPanel` runs a `java.nio.file.WatchService` (daemon `project-fs-watch` thread) over the **root + currently-expanded directories** (re-synced via `syncWatches()` on expand/collapse and after each rebuild — cheap even on huge trees; a collapsed folder isn't watched since it isn't visible, and expanding re-lists it). Disk events (create/delete/modify) are drained and coalesced by a 250 ms `PauseTransition` into a single `refreshTree()`. **Local roots only** (`Vfs.isLocal`; a remote SFTP root has no local watcher). Lifecycle: started in `setRoot` (`ensureWatchOrStop`), torn down in `ProjectPanel.dispose()` (closes the service + thread), called from `MainController.disposeWindow`. *(On macOS the JDK's WatchService is a poller, so external changes can lag a few seconds — the focus-regain refresh covers the immediate case.)* In-app rename/delete update the tree instantly via `refreshAfterChange()` → `refreshTree()` (re-list from disk **by path**, not the captured `TreeItem` — the confirm/rename dialog is a separate window, so closing it regains focus on the main window and fires the focus-regain `refreshTree()` which rebuilds the nodes, detaching the captured item; re-listing by path is immune to that) and call `markLocalChange()` so the watcher **skips its redundant ~1s-later refresh** for the app's own change (a `SELF_CHANGE_WINDOW_MS` guard in the debounce handler). **External change detection**: each buffer records its file's on-disk mtime+size at load/save (`EditorBuffer.setDiskSnapshot`/`diskChangedFrom`); `MainController.checkExternalChanges()` checks the **active tab's** file and, if its disk stamp changed under it, prompts (`promptExternalChange` → `reloadFromDisk`).
