It runs on window focus-regain (`stage.focusedProperty`) and on tab switch — so the prompt only appears for the file the user is looking at; background tabs are checked when switched to. A re-entrancy guard stops the modal prompt from re-triggering itself; "Keep" re-baselines the snapshot; deleted files are skipped; the app's own writes re-baseline so they never prompt. **`SettingsWindow`** is a scalable shell: a top search box + a left **grouped** sidebar + a per-category page (built once into a `Map<Category,Region>`), with a bottom **Reset to Defaults** + Close. The sidebar is a `ListView<Object>` of mixed rows — a non-selectable **`Group`** header (muted, `.settings-group-header`, mouse-transparent) followed by its indented **`Category`** items (`.settings-sidebar-item`), built by `sidebarItems()` in `Category` declaration order; the selection listener swaps the page only for an `instanceof Category` row. **Five groups** (`Group` enum, in order): **General** (Appearance / Interface / Workspace / Tool Windows), **Editor** (Editor = General display+indent+saving+logs+PDF / Code Completion / Snippets / Templates / TODO / Spell Check / Search), **Languages & Tools** (Language Servers / Debugger / Markdown / Mermaid / Web / External Tools), **Version Control** (Git), **System** (Keymap / Remote / Plugins / MCP / Advanced). This replaced the old flat 22-entry list: the catch-all *Editor* page was split (**Code Completion** + **TODO** are now their own leaves), the *Application* grab-bag dissolved into **Interface** (chrome: toolbar/status-bar/tab-bar/breadcrumb/tool-stripe + Simple/Zen **Modes**) + **Workspace** (Projects / show-hidden-files / Notes / Local History), the author field moved to **Templates**, and the two one-toggle *HTTP Client* + *HTML Preview* pages merged into **Web** (two sections). Each feature's master toggle now lives on one canonical page (the Tool Windows page's gated-window notes point there); the empty AI "coming soon" placeholder was dropped (no more `placeholder` flag / `placeholderPage`). `filter()` greys non-matching categories **and** empty group headers (`searchHiddenCats` + `searchHiddenGroups`) and auto-selects the first hit. New i18n: `settings.group.*` + `settings.cat.interface/workspace/completion/todo/web` + `settings.section.modes/htmlPreview/httpClient/templatesList`. The **Snippets** + **Templates** body fields are now RichTextFX `CodeArea`s (not `TextArea`s) with live TextMate highlighting for the snippet/template language (`highlightSnippetBody` via `GrammarRegistry`+`TextMateHighlighter`, re-run on edit) + basic Emacs caret movement (`installEmacsKeys`: `C-a/C-e/C-f/C-b/C-n/C-p/M-f/M-b/C-d/C-k`, since the settings scene has no global `KeyDispatcher`). `formRow` pins each label's min width to its preferred width so a tight `GridPane` never collapses labels to "…". It keeps the **live-apply** model (each control writes its `Settings` field then `apply()` → `config.save()` + `onApply`); there is no OK/Cancel. **Search** filters via the pure/unit-tested `SettingsWindow.matches(query, keywords)` (hides non-matching rows + empty section headers, disables sidebar categories with no hits, auto-selects the first match). The **Appearance** page has a **live preview**: a read-only `CodeArea` (`editor-area`) highlighted once via `TextMateHighlighter.compute(sample, java grammar)`; the Settings `Scene` carries `app.css`+`syntax.css` and an editor-theme override sheet swapped on theme change (mirroring `MainController.applyEditorTheme`), so the preview recolors for free; font changes update its inline style. **Reset** (a single "Reset to Defaults" on the Advanced page) copies a fresh `new Settings()` (preserves `fontZoom`/`keybindings`). **Tool stripe toggle**: the **Interface** page has a "Show tool stripe" checkbox (`Settings.showToolStripe`, default on, schema bumped 3→4 additive-identity) at the top with a `note(...)` warning that hiding the stripe **takes precedence** over each tool window's individual visibility toggle below. It's UI-only — `ToolWindowManager.setStripesEnabled(false)` hides the left/right/bottom stripe `Pane`s (folded into `setStripeShown`'s `stripesEnabled && !zenHidesStripes && !empty` guard) but tool windows still open via their keys (`M-1`…) and the palette. `MainController.applyChromeVisibility()` calls `toolWindows.setStripesEnabled(s.isShowToolStripe())` (re-applied on every settings apply + at init); the palette command `view.toggleToolStripe` (`MainController.toggleToolStripe`) flips the setting, saves, re-applies, and re-syncs the checkbox via `SettingsWindow.syncToolStripeCheck()`. **Simple UI mode** (`Settings.simpleMode`, default off, schema 19→20 additive-identity; Settings → Interface "Simple UI mode", a toolbar `Icons.simpleMode()` square button + `onToggleSimpleMode`, palette `view.toggleSimpleMode`, and the `--simple` CLI session-override) is a single toggle that strips chrome to a minimal surface. `applyChromeVisibility` calls **`applySimpleMode()`** (the effective state is `simpleModeActive()` = `Settings.simpleMode || cliSimpleOverride`): it hides a curated set of toolbar buttons (`newFromTemplateButton`/`recentButton`/`clearRecentButton`/`findInFilesButton`/`splitVertical`/`splitHorizontal` — the **Open** button is deliberately kept so opening a file stays one click away) then **collapses orphaned separators** via `collapseToolbarSeparators()` (a generic pass hiding any `Separator` with no visible control before+after — self-correcting, so toggling off restores them), and pushes `statusBar.setSimpleMode(...)` (hides the git/language/tab-size/line-ending/encoding segments **and the LSP server segment + loading bar** — the LSP ones are event-driven, so `setLsp`/`setLspLoading` store their state and route through `applyLspStatusVisibility()` which suppresses them while `simpleMode`; keeps echo/read-only/zoom/Ln-Col **and the file size**). The **tool-window stripe** and **breadcrumb** are hidden via effective values right in `applyChromeVisibility` (`setStripesEnabled(showToolStripe && !simple)`, `breadcrumb.setEnabled(showBreadcrumb && !simple)`). The project toolbar group is gated inside `applyProjectSupport` (`on && !simpleModeActive()`, since it runs after `applyChromeVisibility`). The minimap is hidden via an **effective value in `applyViewSettings`** (`buffer.setMinimapVisible(showMinimap && !simpleModeActive())`) so the saved pref is preserved; the **whole gutter** is removed via `buffer.setGutterVisible(!simpleModeActive())` (a flag making `refreshGutter()` set a **null `setParagraphGraphicFactory`** — no line numbers, fold chevrons, or bookmark/note/run/breakpoint/git slots), and when Simple mode is active `applyViewSettings` also calls `buffer.unfoldAll()` so collapsed regions aren't stranded behind the hidden chevrons. (`setLineNumbersVisible` is still applied for the non-simple state.) `toggleSimpleMode()` mirrors `toggleToolStripe` (clears `cliSimpleOverride`, flips + saves, `applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`, `syncSimpleModeCheck`, localized `status.toggle.simpleMode` echo) and, when **entering** Simple mode, **closes any open tool window** (`toolWindows.getOpenToolWindows()` → `close`) since the stripe is hidden. (Toolbar layout: the **Settings** button sits just left of **About**, each set off by a small `Separator` — a general arrangement, not Simple-mode-specific.) Simple mode also **disables the heavier features**: `lspEnabled()`, `debugSupportEnabled()`, `httpEnabled()`, `gitEnabled()`, and `multiCaretEnabled()` each fold in `&& !simpleModeActive()`, and their `apply*` methods compute `on` from those helpers — so toggling Simple mode on shuts down language servers + debug adapters, gates off the HTTP ▶, disables the Git integration (status-bar VCS segment, gutter change bars, Commit window), and turns off **multiple cursors / Alt+drag column selection** (`applyMultiCaret` pushes the effective off to every buffer; `withMultiCaret` reports "disabled") — all reusing each feature's existing enable→disable path, and toggling off restores them from the untouched saved settings. The `git.*`/`lsp.*`/`http.*` palette commands (and the Commit/Problems/HTTP tool-window picker entries) are filtered out via those same effective gates while Simple mode is on. Tabs stay; the `--dev` badge stays (a deliberate dev indicator). **About** is no longer in Settings (it's on the toolbar + `help.about`; `SettingsWindow.showAbout` is still the shared dialog); the settings-file link moved to the **Advanced** page. Keep its public API (`show`/`syncThemes`/`syncProjectsCheck`/`syncToolStripeCheck`/`showAbout`/`displaySettingsPath`) — `MainController` wiring is unchanged.

## Conventions

- **Performance is a top priority.** Editora must stay fast and responsive, especially on large files. Treat the UI thread as sacred and these as the hot paths: typing/editing, scrolling, syntax highlighting, the document overlays (whitespace, minimap, 80-column ruler), and the line-number gutter. Rules to uphold:
  - **Never block the JavaFX Application Thread** with non-trivial work — tokenize/parse/search off-thread (see the `highlightExecutor` pattern in `EditorBuffer`) and apply results back on the FX thread with a generation/stale-result guard.
  - **Debounce and coalesce** — re-highlighting is debounced; overlay/ruler/minimap redraws coalesce to one per pulse (a `pending` flag + `Platform.runLater`). Don't add per-keystroke or per-scroll-pulse work that isn't coalesced.
  - **Work incrementally / only on what's visible** — highlighting re-tokenizes only from the changed line; overlays iterate just the visible paragraphs (`firstVisibleParToAllParIndex … last`) and skip folded lines. Avoid O(document) work on edits or scrolls.
  - **Don't defeat the per-node CSS style cache** — keep token rules as the compound `.text.<class>` selector (see `syntax.css`); coalesce adjacent same-style spans (`SpanMerger`) before `setStyleSpans`; never query `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen` synchronously inside a layout/viewport event.
  - **Large/huge files** already disable highlighting + minimap (≥5 MB) and go read-only with a capped load (≥50 MB); preserve those guards. There's also an **intermediate large-source tier** (`EditorBuffer.heavyFile` / `setHeavyFile` / `isHeavyFile`, set in `MainController.loadInto` when a sub-5 MB file's `lineCount()` ≥ `Settings.largeFileThreshold`, default 10000 lines, 0 = off): it **disables the minimap + LSP** (the two heaviest features for a very long single source) but **keeps syntax highlighting + editing**; `largeFile` implies the same minimap/LSP suppression. Per-buffer toggleable (`view.toggleLargeFileMode` → `MainController.toggleLargeFileMode`, which flips `setHeavyFile` then `syncBufferLsp`); threshold via `editor.setLargeFileThreshold` + Settings → Editor → Performance. Bound memory (undo history is capped; loads are capped). **Undo granularity:** `boundedUndoManager` builds the RichTextFX manager with `UndoMerge.PAUSE` as the `preventMergeDelay` (idle break) and a `plainTextChanges` subscriber calls `UndoManager.preventMerge()` at word/whitespace/newline boundaries (pure `editor/UndoMerge.breakAfter`), so one `C-z` undoes a word/line instead of the whole contiguous burst RichTextFX would otherwise merge; split views share the document so both managers are broken together. **Undo History tool window** (`ui/UndoHistoryPanel`, id `undoHistory`, `Side.RIGHT`, `tool.undoHistory`/`M-g u`, buffer-gated; **registered default-hidden** via `register(tw, false)` — the stripe button is off until the user enables it via Settings → Tool Windows or `tool.undoHistory`, since the `undoHistory.jump` popup is the primary entry point): `editor/UndoHistory` keeps a capped (50) in-session list of full-document checkpoints captured on the `UndoMerge.PAUSE` debounce (`EditorBuffer.captureUndoCheckpoint`, skipped for huge/>1 MB files); the panel lists them newest-first (time + caret-line preview) and double-click/Enter calls `EditorBuffer.restoreUndoCheckpoint` (an undoable `replaceText`). A **popup alternative** — command `undoHistory.jump` (`M-g v`; `MainController.undoHistoryPalette`, a `QuickOpen<UndoHistory.Checkpoint>` over the active buffer's `entriesNewestFirst()`, seeding a baseline when empty like the panel) — opens the same checkpoints as a filterable in-scene overlay (label = caret-line preview, detail = `HH:mm:ss`); Enter restores. Session-only, finer-grained than save-based Local History; pure bits (`UndoHistory.add`/`lineAt`/`clamp`) unit-tested.
  - **Bound retained GPU textures.** JavaFX's Prism texture pool has a fixed ceiling (default 512 MB); exhausting it makes the render thread NPE (null `RTTexture`/mask texture) → a black window — seen only in the packaged build. So don't let GPU-backed resources grow with the number of open files: a background (non-selected) tab's buffer drops its minimap snapshot via `EditorBuffer.setRenderingActive(false)` (driven from the tab-selection + tabs-added listeners; `Minimap.setRenderingActive` nulls the cached snapshot and stops rendering, regenerating on show), and the `PreviewImageLoader`/`MermaidImages` image caches are **LRU-bounded** (not unbounded `ConcurrentHashMap`s) since each holds an `Image` (a pinned texture). The `dist` jpackage app (and `mvn javafx:run`) also raise the caps as a safety net (`-Dprism.maxvram=2G -Dprism.maxTextureSize=16384`). When adding any per-buffer Canvas/Image, make sure it's released or bounded.
  - **Packaged-runtime JVM tuning (footprint + install size).** The `dist` jpackage `<javaOptions>` (mirrored into the `javafx:run` options so dev == prod) cap the heap and GC: **`-Xmx2g`** (without it, jpackage inherits the default ergonomic max heap ≈ ¼ of physical RAM — multi-GB on a high-RAM box — which lets GC-driven RSS balloon; 2g is predictable across the release matrix and safe for a 50 MB huge-file load + capped undo) and **`-XX:+UseSerialGC`** (a mostly-idle single-user editor on a small heap gets sub-ms pauses with no parallel GC-thread overhead — lower idle RSS than the default G1; if large-file GC *hitching* ever shows up, generational ZGC is the smoothness-over-footprint alternative). The jpackage `<jLinkOptions>` strip the bundled runtime (`--strip-debug --no-man-pages --no-header-files --compress=zip-6`) → smaller DMG/MSI/DEB + less mapped footprint. (`--strip-native-commands` is deliberately *omitted* from jLinkOptions — `bin/java` must survive the jlink step for the AOT training run below; the `aot_build` helper deletes `bin/` itself afterward, reclaiming the same footprint. The runtime's `bin/` is never used at launch — the jpackage native launcher starts the JVM via `libjli`, and every external tool (java/python/node/git/LSP/DAP) is resolved via the augmented PATH. **WINDOWS EXCEPTION (`aot_build.java` strips `bin/` non-Windows-only):** the Windows JDK layout puts the JVM *inside* `bin/` (`runtime\bin\server\jvm.dll` + the bootstrap `jli.dll`/`java.dll`/`jvm.cfg`/…), and `Editora.exe` loads `jvm.dll` from there — so deleting `bin/` on Windows makes the launcher die with *"Failed to find JVM in …\runtime directory"* (a shipped regression fixed by guarding the strip to non-Windows). On Windows the whole `bin/` is kept — its launcher exes are a negligible footprint.) **AOT cache (JDK 25 Leyden) — implemented, ~28%/≈300–480 ms faster cold start** (measured macOS: first-frame ~1060 ms → ~760 ms; delivered-app wall delta ~480 ms): the build does a **two-phase jpackage** — phase 1 (`prepare`) jlinks an `APP_IMAGE` into `target/aot-image` with `-XX:AOTCache=$APPDIR/editora.aot` baked into the launcher `.cfg`; then `scripts/aot_build.java` (run by `exec-maven-plugin` with the build JDK) **trains a full-GUI cache against the image's own runtime** (so archived classes match the shipped runtime, path-independently — it maps after the install-dir move because the classes live in the jlinked `lib/modules`, keyed to the runtime image not absolute paths), writes `editora.aot` into `$APPDIR`, strips `bin/`, then either copies the image (APP_IMAGE builds) or wraps it into the installer via `jpackage --app-image` (DMG/MSI/DEB). **A *headless* trainer gives ≈0 win** — the gain is JavaFX scene/control/CSS class loading, which only loads when a window renders; the training run is the real GUI driven by `-Deditora.aotTrainExit` (`WindowManager` renders the first frame, settles ~2.5 s for highlight-class coverage, then `System.exit`). On Linux the helper auto-wraps training in `xvfb-run` (release.yml installs `xvfb`+GTK/GL libs on the Linux legs); macOS/Windows runners use their session. **Fully failure-tolerant:** if training fails (no usable display on a runner, etc.) the build continues and ships without the cache — a missing/invalid `-XX:AOTCache` file logs to stderr (invisible in the packaged app) and starts normally under the default `AOTMode=auto`. **Cost: the cache is ~60 MB**, so the installed image grows accordingly (the DMG/MSI/DEB compress it — the DMG download stayed ~81 MB). **Prism pipeline order is per-OS** (the `${prism.pipeline}` property set in the `os-mac`/`os-windows`/`os-linux` profiles, passed as `-Dprism.order=${prism.pipeline}` to both the dist `<javaOptions>` and `javafx:run` `<options>`): **macOS = `mtl,es2,sw`** — the **Metal** pipeline, added in **JavaFX 26**, which fixes the blank/garbled render-to-texture glitches the deprecated es2/OpenGL backend produced on Apple silicon (e.g. M-series: empty breadcrumb crumbs + tool-stripe icons); es2/sw stay as fallbacks since Metal is opt-in. **Windows = `d3d,es2,sw`** (must keep Direct3D — a blanket `mtl,es2,sw` would strip d3d and lose Windows GPU accel). **Linux = `es2,sw`**. JavaFX 26 runs on JDK 24+, so the JDK stays **25**. Still a **commented-out opt-in** in the pom (DEVICE-TEST before enabling, touches correctness): JDK 25 **compact object headers** (`-XX:+UseCompactObjectHeaders`, experimental, ~10–20% live-heap cut — note it changes the AOT cache's recorded layout, so retrain after enabling). *(Aside: `App.main` exits `--version`/`--help` via `System.exit(0)`, not a bare return — launching this `Application` subclass in module mode pre-starts the FX toolkit, whose non-daemon keep-alive thread would otherwise hang the process after `main` returns.)*
  - **Assess and report the performance cost of every change.** For any implementation or bug fix, evaluate its cost on the hot paths (allocation per keystroke/scroll, added FX-thread work, extra layout/CSS passes, memory) and tell the user about it — even if it's "negligible." If a change risks a regression, measure (e.g. the temporary `System.nanoTime` instrumentation used for the startup investigation) rather than guess.
- **Code style — Palantir Java Format, enforced by Spotless.** All Java is auto-formatted with [Palantir Java Format](https://github.com/palantir/palantir-java-format) (a lambda-friendly, 120-col fork of google-java-format) via the `spotless-maven-plugin` (config in `pom.xml`; versions in the `${spotless.version}`/`${palantir.version}` properties). **Run `mvn spotless:apply` before committing** — `mvn spotless:check` is bound to the `verify` phase, so `mvn verify`/`mvn package`/CI fail on unformatted code (the `mvn javafx:run`/`mvn compile` dev loop is deliberately left untouched). Pipeline: `removeUnusedImports` → `palantirJavaFormat` → `importOrder` → `toggleOffOn`. **Import groups** (blank-line separated; longest-prefix wins, so `javafx` is *not* swallowed by `java`): JDK (`java`/`javax`) → `javafx` → everything else (third-party + `com.editora`) → static imports last. Escape hatch for hand-aligned code: wrap it in `// spotless:off` … `// spotless:on`. Palantir 2.72.0+ supports JDK 25. The two tree-wide mechanical reformats are recorded in `.git-blame-ignore-revs` (enable locally once with `git config blame.ignoreRevsFile .git-blame-ignore-revs`; GitHub honors it automatically) so `git blame` skips them.
- **Code size — soft limits, not hard gates.** Keep classes and methods small enough to hold in your head; these are review heuristics, not a build check. **Per class (target):** ≤ ~500 lines is ideal, ≤ ~1000 is fine; **~1000–1500** is acceptable only for a *genuinely cohesive subsystem* (e.g. `editor/EditorBuffer`, which coordinates one buffer's many overlays/managers — treat it gently); **> ~2000 lines is a refactor smell** — split it. **Per method (target):** ≤ ~50 lines ideal, **> ~100 is a smell** (extract helpers / a pure decision function). What actually matters is **responsibility count** and **cyclomatic complexity**, not raw line count — a 600-line class doing one thing is healthier than a 300-line class doing five. When a class creeps over the line, the first move is to extract the *pure* logic (a decision/format/parse helper in its own class, unit-tested) and, for a whole feature, a **`CoordinatorHost`-style coordinator** (see the `ui/*Coordinator` classes). **`ui/MainController` is the known outlier** (~12k lines) and is being incrementally decomposed one feature at a time into `ui/*Coordinator` classes (External Tools, Macros, TODO, Search, Run done; Notes, Bookmarks, LSP, Debug pending) — so **a new feature should be its own coordinator (or pure package), never bolted onto `MainController`**. No tooling enforces these numbers (JaCoCo gates *coverage*, not size); they're for human judgement during review and when deciding where new code lives.
- **Adding a feature = add a `Command`, and surface it in the command palette.** Every time we add a command or an applicable user-facing feature, it must be discoverable in the palette. Register it in `MainController.registerCommands()` and, if it needs a key, add a binding to `emacs.json`. The palette is populated from `CommandRegistry.all()`, so a properly registered command appears automatically — never add a user-facing action that bypasses the registry. Toolbar buttons and the palette both dispatch through commands; don't wire UI handlers to logic directly when a command fits.
- **Every setting also needs a palette command** — Editora is command-driven, so a Settings-window control (toggle, picker, font, path, number, …) is **not** enough on its own; it must have a command-palette equivalent too. Register a command in `MainController.registerCommands()` that flips/prompts the **same** `Settings` field, persists (`requestSave()`), re-applies the feature (`applyGitSupport`/`applyLspSupport`/`applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`/…), and keeps an open Settings window in step via `SettingsWindow.syncAll()`. Toggles → `view.toggle*` (master feature-enable toggles use a `view.`/`appearance.`/`debug.` prefix so the palette's feature-gating filter never hides them); values → a `promptText` prompt or a `QuickOpen` picker; many per-item settings (e.g. the per-server LSP / per-adapter Debug commands) → one grouped picker command. Reuse the generic helpers `toggleSetting`/`promptStringSetting`/`promptIntSetting`/`chooseSetting`, and add `command.<id>` + `command.<id>.desc` to all six i18n catalogs (the two shared status keys `status.settingToggled`/`status.settingChanged` reuse the command's own title). The 2026-06 sweep (PR #56) closed every gap — keep parity when adding a setting.
- **Every user-facing string is localized — never hardcode UI text.** Any new label, status/echo message, tooltip, dialog title/header/body, button, menu item, prompt, or placeholder must go through the i18n catalog: `import static com.editora.i18n.Messages.tr;` then `tr("some.key")` (or `tr("key", args…)` for `MessageFormat` parameters like `Saved {0}`) — never pass a raw English literal to a JavaFX control. **Add the key to all six `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages[_<lang>].properties` files** (English base + `it/es/fr/pt/de`) with a real translation in each; `MessagesTest`'s key-parity check fails the build if any locale is missing a key. New `Command`s get their title for free via `Command.of(id, runnable)` + a `command.<id>` key. Only deliberate exceptions stay literal: technical tokens (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, detected language names, example URLs) and the pre-GUI `--help`/`--version` text. See the `i18n/` architecture bullet for the full system.
- **App icon / branding:** the source logo is `branding/editora-icon.svg`. Window-icon PNGs (16–512) live in `resources/com/editora/icons/` (loaded into `stage.getIcons()` in `App`; also the About-dialog logo). Native-installer icons `branding/editora.{icns,ico,png}` are generated from the SVG (rsvg-convert + iconutil + a small ICO writer) and passed to jpackage via `${jpackage.icon}`, set per-OS in the OS-activated profiles. Regenerate after editing the SVG.
- **Context-menu icons:** **every right-click `MenuItem` carries a leading icon** (`MenuItem.setGraphic(...)`). UI-package menus (tab strip + Welcome close in `MainController.installTabMenu`, `ProjectPanel`, `GitPanel`, `BookmarksPanel`, `NotesPanel`, `MessageLogPopup`, `FileBreadcrumb`) use `com.editora.ui.Icons` directly; the **editor** package's menus (`EditorBuffer.installContextMenu` + `showPreviewContextMenu`) can't depend on `ui`, so they use **`com.editora.editor.MenuIcons`** — a package-local mirror of `Icons` (same Material 24dp single-path glyphs, `toolbar-icon` style class, 0.8 scale) holding only the glyphs those two menus need (cut/copy/paste/undo/redo/selectAll, markdown bold/italic/strike/code/link, LSP goto-def/refs/hover, spellcheck/add/block, note/run/download/print); the Run item reuses `FoldManager.runGlyph()`. Icons are colored via the global `.toolbar-icon` rule (`-color-fg-muted`, theme-aware), so they track light/dark for free — **no new CSS**. When adding a context menu or item, give every item a `setGraphic` glyph (reuse an existing one where no exact match exists, e.g. the close-tab X across all close-variants). The recent-files toolbar **MenuButton** dropdown is not a right-click menu and is intentionally excluded (its entries already carry an inline remove-icon); the snippet **choice** dropdown lists content values, not commands, and is likewise excluded.
- **File-type icons:** **`com.editora.ui.FileIcons`** maps a file name to a small monochrome glyph reflecting its type, shown wherever a file is listed: editor tabs (`MainController.updateTabMeta`), the `ProjectPanel` tree (file rows; folders keep `Icons.project()`), the `FileFinder` file/folder pickers, the `Switcher` cell, and the **Open Files** / **Recent Files** `QuickOpen` pickers (via the new optional `QuickOpen.setItemIcon(Function<T,Node>)`). The pure, unit-tested **`FileIcons.iconKeyFor(name)`** resolves a name → glyph key — non-language extensions first (image png/jpg/svg/…→`image`, `pdf`, archive zip/jar/…→`archive`, csv/tsv→`table`, `*.lock`, txt/log→`text`), else `LanguageRegistry.forFileName(name)`'s language id → key (java/python/js/ts/go/php/ruby/c/cpp/csharp/kotlin/html/css/markdown/yaml/json/xml→code/shell/powershell+batchfile→terminal/dockerfile/terraform/mermaid/sql→storage/ini+toml+…→settings/rust+lua+groovy+http→code); unknown ⇒ `generic` → the existing `Icons.fileSheet()` fallback (so unrecognized files look exactly as before). **`forFileName(name)`** turns the key into a fresh `Icons.of(path)` node — glyphs are single-path SVGs in the `toolbar-icon` style (theme-aware, no per-theme overrides, **no new CSS**). Brand logos are vendored from **Simple Icons** (CC0); category glyphs from **Material Design Icons** (Apache-2.0) — attributed in `NOTICE`. `Icons.of(...)` was made package-private so `FileIcons` (same package) reuses it. To add/adjust a mapping: extend the `iconKeyFor` switch + add the glyph path to `FileIcons.PATHS` + a `FileIconsTest` case. *(No new dependency; glyphs are inlined path strings, like the existing browser logos.)*
- **Bundled fonts:** five monospace families ship under `resources/com/editora/fonts/<family>/` (Regular/Bold/Italic/BoldItalic TTFs; Fira Code has no italic), **plus Inter** (sans-serif, `fonts/inter/`) as the Markdown **preview + PDF prose** font. `Fonts.load()` registers them all via `Font.loadFont` at the very start of `App.start` (before any CSS), so they resolve by family name regardless of the OS. `Fonts.BUNDLED` (JetBrains Mono first = default) is the **monospace** editor-font picker list and deliberately **excludes Inter** (Inter isn't an editor font); it's listed ahead of the system monospaced families in the Settings font picker. Inter is the preview prose font on **all platforms** (`.markdown-preview .md-text` in `app.css` — pinned explicitly because raw `Text` nodes don't reliably inherit the scene font, and because the macOS chrome's logical "System" family can't be bold-rasterized cleanly by JavaFX) and the PDF prose font (`MarkdownPdfWriter`). They're plain resources (no `module-info`/moditect change) and are picked up by the `dist` build automatically. Attributed in `NOTICE` (all OFL-1.1).
- **Theming:** AtlantaFX is the user-agent stylesheet and themes standard controls (`Themes`, set via `Application.setUserAgentStylesheet`). It does **not** style the RichTextFX `CodeArea` — editor surface, line-number gutter, and syntax token colors live in `styles/app.css` + `styles/syntax.css` (the **Primer Light** defaults). **Editor color themes** (`EditorThemes`) layer an override stylesheet from `styles/editor-themes/<name>.css` onto the scene *after* those defaults (Primer Light = no override); `MainController.applyEditorTheme` swaps that sheet on the scene and sets each buffer's current-line highlight color (RichTextFX's line-highlight fill is set in code, not CSS). The editor theme follows the AtlantaFX theme (`EditorThemes.defaultFor`) until the user picks one (`Settings.editorThemeUserSet`). Token rules must stay the compound `.text.<class>` form — see the header comment in `syntax.css`. The **Project tool window file tree** is themed via two looked-up CSS colors `-project-folder-color`/`-project-file-color` (defined on `.project-tree` in `app.css`, defaulting to AtlantaFX accent/muted); each editor theme overrides them, so a new editor theme should add a `.project-tree { -project-folder-color: …; -project-file-color: …; }` rule. **Bundled community themes:** beyond the 7 built-in AtlantaFX themes (Primer/Nord/Cupertino/Dracula), `Themes` also lists 19 MIT-licensed community themes from the DLSC `atlantafx-themes` collection (Blue/Navy/Army L/D, the four seasonal L/D sets, Autumn/Browny/News/Yacht — the GitHub colorblind/tritanopia variants are excluded on purpose). Their control-theme CSS is **vendored** under `styles/atlantafx-themes/<name>.css` (self-contained AtlantaFX user-agent stylesheets; `url()`s resolve to JDK modena assets) and served by `Themes.BundledTheme` — a small `atlantafx.base.theme.Theme` impl **kept in `com.editora.ui`** so `theme.getClass().getResource(...)` finds the vendored CSS in *this* module (a `Theme.of(...)` instance would resolve against atlantafx-base and return null). `Themes.BUNDLED` (name → {css base, dark, bg-default hex}) drives `themeFor`/`backgroundFor`. **The matching editor themes all share one file** — `styles/editor-themes/adaptive.css` — whose `.editor-area`/`.text.<class>`/`.project-tree` rules are written entirely in the theme's own `-color-*` semantic variables (keyword→`danger-fg`, string→`success-fg`, number→`accent-fg`, type→`warning-fg`, function→`accent-emphasis`, comment→`fg-muted`, …), so one palette adapts to every theme with no per-theme syntax file. `EditorThemes` still needs per-theme **code-driven** colors that CSS vars can't reach (startup background, current-line highlight, minimap block/viewport), taken from each theme's `-color-bg-default`/`-color-fg-default`/`-color-bg-subtle`/`-color-fg-muted`/`-color-accent-emphasis`. **To add another AtlantaFX theme:** vendor its `.css`, add a `Themes.BUNDLED` entry + the name to both `Themes.NAMES`/`EditorThemes.NAMES`, and add `EditorThemes` map entries (CSS→`adaptive`, plus the 5 code-driven colors). `ThemesTest` guards that every theme resolves a loadable stylesheet + has a matching editor theme + parseable colors. Community-theme CSS is MIT (attributed in `NOTICE`). **User-defined themes** (`ui/UserThemes`, loaded once in `App.start` via `UserThemes.load(configDir)` before the theme is applied; palette command `theme.reloadUserThemes` re-scans): two folders under the config dir — **`themes/*.css`** = full AtlantaFX control themes (each becomes an app theme *and* an adaptive editor theme, exactly like the bundled community ones — served via a file-URL `BundledTheme` + `adaptive.css`, with code-driven colors parsed from the CSS's `-color-*`), and **`editor-themes/*.css`** = hand-authored editor overrides (editor-theme picker only, served by the file URL). The picker/combo lists now come from `Themes.names()` / `EditorThemes.names()` (built-ins + user), not the static `NAMES` (kept as the built-in list); `normalize`/`defaultFor`/`stylesheetFor`/the color accessors consult `UserThemes.controlThemes()`/`editorThemes()`. The theme **name is the file base name Title-Cased** (`my-theme.css` → "My Theme"); a name colliding with a built-in is skipped. `UserThemes.titleCase`/`parseColor`/`baseName` are pure/unit-tested; a user theme's `file:` URL passes straight through `Themes.stylesheetFor`'s `hasUrlScheme` check.
- **Tests** are mostly **pure logic** (keymap resolution, command registry, config merge, highlighting spans), plus a small **headless-JavaFX harness** for toolkit-bound `ui/` behavior (see below). Prefer extracting pure decision helpers and unit-testing those (it's faster + needs no toolkit) — but real controller behavior (Zen toggling chrome, Simple-mode stripping, tab/window lifecycle) is now covered end-to-end via the FX harness. **Coverage:** `mvn test` runs the JaCoCo agent and writes a report to `target/site/jacoco/index.html` (+ `jacoco.xml`); `mvn verify` additionally runs a JaCoCo **`check`** that enforces a per-package LINE-coverage **floor** on the well-covered pure packages (migration·diff ≥0.90, config ≥0.86, template·editorconfig ≥0.82, completion·http·pdf ≥0.70 — see the `jacoco-check` execution in `pom.xml`), so their coverage can't silently regress. Floors sit comfortably below current levels (a regression net, not a target) — **when you raise a package's coverage, ratchet its floor up**. `ui`/`editor` are still **deliberately ungated** (the FX harness covers only a few % of `ui`'s ~16.7k lines so far — add a floor only once coverage is meaningful). The dev loop (`mvn javafx:run`/`compile`) is unaffected — the check runs only at `verify`/`package`. The cheapest way to raise `ui` coverage is still to extract pure decision helpers (effective-visibility/gating predicates, caret-navigation math, path keying, …) and unit-test those — see `ui/Chrome`, `editor/TextNav`, `config/PathKeys`.
  - **Sample corpus (`samples/`)** — a curated, feature-organized set of small text samples for **manual** smoke-testing/demos (one subdir per feature: `syntax/` per language, `folding/`, `indent/`, `markdown/`, `mermaid/`, `todo/`, `spell/`, `search/`, `editorconfig/` (hermetic, `root=true`), `http/`, `log/`, `diff/`, `encodings/`). It's a **human aid**, not part of the behavioral suite; `samples/README.md` is the manifest and `SamplesCorpusTest` only guards that the manifest ↔ committed files stay in sync + the core languages each have a syntax sample (add/remove a sample ⇒ update the README or the test fails). Large/perf inputs are **generated** by `java scripts/GenSamples.java` (a JDK 25 compact source file, run from the repo root) into the git-ignored `samples/perf/` (never committed — keeps history lean). A scoped root `.gitattributes` marks `samples/encodings/**` + `samples/diff/conflict.txt` `-text` so git never normalizes the encoding/EOL/conflict-marker bytes, and `samples/**` `linguist-vendored`. Samples are inert-by-name (no real `.gitignore`/secrets; the EditorConfig fixture is sandboxed with `root=true`). Spotless only formats `src/{main,test}/java`, so sample `.java` files are left untouched.
  - **Headless-FX harness** (`src/test/java/com/editora/ui/`): **TestFX** (`testfx-core`/`testfx-junit5`) drives only the toolkit **lifecycle** (`FxToolkit.registerPrimaryStage()`) over **JavaFX 26's built-in Headless Glass platform** (`-Dglass.platform=Headless`, part of `javafx.graphics` since 26 — no Monocle jar, no native libs) — so FX tests run headless on CI with **no display/xvfb**. The harness never drives the TestFX **robot** (no `clickOn`/key simulation — everything goes through `runOnFx`/`callOnFx` + reflection), so the prototype headless platform's input/rendering limitations don't apply, and TestFX needs no changes despite not yet officially adopting the new platform. All FX tests are `@Tag("fx")`; run the pure suite alone with `./mvnw test -DexcludedGroups=fx`. `FxTestSupport` boots the toolkit once (Headless platform + `Fonts.load`/`Messages.init`/AtlantaFX UA sheet/classloader pin) and exposes `runOnFx`/`callOnFx` + reflection helpers (`field`/`invoke`/`call`) to read private `@FXML` nodes and invoke private methods (tests run on the **classpath** as the unnamed module, so `setAccessible` is unrestricted). `FxWindowFixture` builds a real window via `WindowManager.buildWindowForTest()` (a package-private seam mirroring `buildWindow`) against a temp config dir — **if that boot path changes, the fixture/seam must track it**. The **surefire config** is what makes this work: `<useModulePath>false</useModulePath>` (classpath mode), the headless system properties (`glass.platform=Headless`, `prism.order=sw`), and **`<argLine>@{argLine}</argLine>`** — the `@{argLine}` token is mandatory so JaCoCo's injected coverage agent (set via the `argLine` property) survives; a plain `<argLine>` would clobber it.

## Packaging note (important)

RichTextFX is a **personal fork** (`io.github.adriandeleon:richtextfx`, vendored in the in-project
`m2-repo/`, source at github.com/adriandeleon/RichTextFX) that adds VS Code–style **multiple cursors +
Alt+drag column/box selection** via a self-contained `org.fxmisc.richtext.multi.MultiCaretController.install(area)`
add-on (a layered wellbehaved `InputMap`, gated on `MultiCaretManager.hasExtras()` so it's transparent with
one caret). **`EditorBuffer`** installs it on `area`/`area2` via `setMultiCaretEnabled(...)` (gated by
`Settings.multiCaret`, default on; pushed by `MainController.applyMultiCaret`), exposes
`hasMultipleCarets()` + delegating `addCaretNextOccurrence`/`addCaretAbove`/`addCaretBelow`/`collapseCarets`
(palette commands `edit.addCaret*`/`edit.collapseCarets`, `view.toggleMultiCaret` — **no keymap bindings**:
gestures are mouse + Esc, native to the fork). Because Editora's area-level KEY filters (auto-indent/close,
snippets, completion, view paging) are capture-phase *filters* that run before the fork's node InputMap,
each one early-returns (no consume) via `multiCaretActiveOn(a)` when that area has extra carets, so editing
fans out to all carets. *Known limitation:* Emacs movement chords (`C-f`/`C-n`/…) are resolved by the
scene-level `KeyDispatcher` on the primary caret and don't fan out — use arrows for multi-caret movement.
To update the fork: rebuild it, copy the new `richtextfx-<version>.{jar,pom}` into `m2-repo/`, bump
`<richtextfx.version>`. RichTextFX and its transitive deps (`reactfx`, `flowless`, `undofx`, `wellbehavedfx`)
are **automatic modules**, which `jlink` cannot link. The `moditect-maven-plugin` in
the `dist` profile injects explicit `module-info` descriptors into them. If you bump
RichTextFX or add a dep it uses, you may need to adjust those descriptors' `requires`
(e.g. several of them need `javafx.controls` for `IndexRange`). Use RichTextFX
**0.11.7+** — earlier versions are incompatible with JavaFX 25.

tm4e (the syntax engine) ships as the NetBeans repackaging
`org.netbeans.external:org.eclipse.tm4e.core-0.14.0:RELEASE260` (tm4e is not on
Maven Central). Its Oniguruma backend (`org.jruby.joni:joni`, `org.jruby.jcodings:jcodings`)
and `com.google.code.gson:gson` are already proper modules, but tm4e core is an
automatic module, so `moditect` injects a `module-info` for it too. The NetBeans
jar is also **code-signed**, and `jlink` rejects signed modular jars — the `dist`
profile's antrun step strips `META-INF/*.SF,*.RSA,*.DSA,*.EC` before linking.

**Headless FX testing — built-in platform (no Monocle).** As of **JavaFX 26** the headless Glass backend for the
FX test harness is the **built-in Headless platform** that ships inside `javafx.graphics` (`-Dglass.platform=Headless`,
set in the surefire `<systemPropertyVariables>`). **No jar, no native libs, no separate download, nothing vendored** —
it's part of the JavaFX runtime, so it can never go stale on a JavaFX bump. This **replaced** the previously
self-built **Monocle** backend (`io.github.adriandeleon:openjfx-monocle`, which had to be rebuilt from the OpenJFX
sources on every JavaFX bump and vendored in `m2-repo/`) — that whole rebuild ritual and its vendored artifacts are
gone. The new platform is officially a **prototype** in 26, but the harness only uses TestFX's `FxToolkit` to **boot
the toolkit** and never drives the robot (input/clicks) or renders/snapshots in tests, so the prototype's
rendering/input limitations don't apply (and TestFX needs no changes despite not yet adopting it — see
[TestFX #819](https://github.com/TestFX/TestFX/issues/819)). No `module-info`/jlink impact — it's test scope only and
never on the runtime path. *(If a future need ever requires real headless rendering or robot input under the
prototype, Monocle could be re-vendored, but as of 26 it isn't needed.)*
